- **MQ arithmetic decoder (the core, bit-exact)**: `pypdfbox/jbig2/decoder/arithmetic/` — `ArithmeticDecoder` (MQ-coder: INITDEC/DECODE/BYTEIN/RENORMD + the 47-row Qe/NMPS/NLPS/SWITCH table), `CX` (context), `ArithmeticIntegerDecoder` (IAx/IAID). 32-bit C/A register wraparound reproduced via explicit masking. New `oracle/probes/ArithDecodeProbe.java` drives the bundled Java `ArithmeticDecoder`; the port is **bit-exact** across 10 differential cases (varied inputs, contexts, FF-markers, EOF).
- **bit-reader I/O**: `pypdfbox/jbig2/io/` — `ImageInputStream` (big-endian bit reader mirroring `javax.imageio.stream.ImageInputStreamImpl`: `read_bit`/`read_bits`/position/offset/seek/align), `SubInputStream` (windowed sub-stream), `InputStreamFactory`/`DefaultInputStreamFactory`.
- **bitmap + ops**: `pypdfbox/jbig2/bitmap.py` (`Bitmap` — MSB-first 8-px/byte packing, `get_pixel`/`set_pixel`, row stride, pad-bit-ignoring equality), `util/combination_operator.py` (`CombinationOperator` OR/AND/XOR/XNOR/REPLACE), `jbig2_globals.py` (`JBIG2Globals`).
- **errors**: `pypdfbox/jbig2/err/` (`JBIG2Exception`/`IntegerMaxValueException`/`InvalidHeaderValueException`).

190 new tests (128 in `tests/jbig2/`). Subsequent waves: Huffman + MMR coders, segment headers + document structure, generic/refinement/halftone/pattern regions, symbol-dictionary + text-region, then image assembly + reader, then re-wire `pypdfbox/filter/jbig2_decode.py` to the Python decoder and re-enable the full image-level oracle.

## Wave 1420 — remove GPL `jbig2-parser` dependency (/JBIG2Decode unsupported)

The `jbig2-parser` runtime dependency was dropped. It declared **MIT** in its PyPI metadata (so the metadata-only pip-licenses pre-push gate passed it), but its compiled extension statically links the Rust crate **`jbig2dec` 0.3.1**, whose license is **GPL-3.0** — a Rust binding to Artifex's AGPL-3.0 `jbig2dec` C library. GPL/AGPL are on the hard-forbidden list (CLAUDE.md §4; a §20 project-failure condition), and the metadata-based license gate cannot see bundled native copyleft code.

- `pyproject.toml`: `jbig2-parser` dependency line removed; the venv package uninstalled.
- `pypdfbox/filter/jbig2_decode.py`: `JBIG2Decode.decode` now raises a clear "unsupported" `OSError` instead of wrapping the GPL decoder. The filter stays registered in `FilterFactory` so `/JBIG2Decode` is still recognised by name (a PDF using it reports an explicit unsupported-filter error rather than an unknown-filter parse failure). `encode` continues to raise.
- All jbig2 tests updated to assert the unsupported-decode contract.

JBIG2 decode support is to be restored by porting the Apache-2.0, pure-Java `apache/pdfbox-jbig2` (~63 files) to Python — tracked as an open item in `DEFERRED.md`.

## Wave 1419 — expand the live oracle to 6 more surfaces (6 real bugs fixed)

6 agents extended the live PDFBox 3.0.7 oracle to Type3 fonts, FDF/XFDF, separable blend modes, JBIG2 + JPX images, and output intents. Bugs fixed in Type3 / FDF / blend modes; output intents clean; JPX not oracle-testable (the app jar lacks a JPEG2000 ImageIO reader — added a structural test); **JBIG2 work was reverted** pending a license decision (the `jbig2-parser` dependency bundles GPL-3.0 native code — see `DEFERRED.md`). Surfaces fixed:

- **Type3 fonts (1 bug)**: `PDType3Font` inherited `PDSimpleFont.get_encoding_typed()`, which seeds a *base encoding* under the `/Differences` overlay; upstream `PDType3Font.readEncoding()` uses the no-base `DictionaryEncoding`, so codes absent from `/Differences` must resolve to `.notdef` (pypdfbox wrongly mapped them via StandardEncoding — ~250 codes off). Added a `get_encoding_typed()` override in `pd_type3_font.py`. Type3 font matrix / widths / encoding / extracted text now match PDFBox.
- **blend modes (1 bug)**: vector fills/strokes ignored a non-Normal `/BM` ExtGState blend mode entirely (painted opaque as if Normal) — only image XObjects/groups blended. `pypdfbox/rendering/pdf_renderer.py` `_paint`/`_paint_through_clip` now route a non-Normal blend mode through the layer compositor + `_blend()`. All 11 separable modes (Multiply…Exclusion) match PDFBox (MAD≤0.39); `blend_mode.py` formulas were already correct.
- **output intents (parity confirmed, no bug)**: `OutputIntentProbe` — output condition/identifier/registry/info + the `/DestOutputProfile` decoded ICC byte length + SHA-1 match PDFBox on `PDFA3A.pdf` (GTS_PDFA1, 3144-byte sRGB ICC) + a built synthetic intent.
- **JPX (not oracle-testable)**: the bundled `pdfbox-app` jar has no JPEG2000 ImageIO reader (`MissingImageReaderException`), so there's no Java baseline. Added a non-oracle structural test (`tests/pdmodel/graphics/image/oracle/test_jpx_image_structural.py`) confirming pypdfbox decodes JPX (gray/RGB/CMYK) via its `imagecodecs`/OpenJPEG path.

### FDF/XFDF (2 real bugs fixed)

Added the FDF/XFDF live PDFBox 3.0.7 oracle (`FdfProbe`, modes `dump` / `roundtrip`) covering the FDF catalog's fields (fully-qualified names + values + per-field kids), the `/F` source reference, and FDF annotations (subtype + rect), across both `Loader.loadFDF` and `Loader.loadXFDF`. No FDF/XFDF fixtures ship with the repo, so the rig builds an FDF via pypdfbox (scalar field, nested-kids field, multi-select field, two annotations, a `/F`), saves it as both FDF and XFDF, and runs both libraries over the artefacts. 2 real bugs fixed:

- **FDF save wrote a `%PDF-` header instead of `%FDF-` (bugfix)**: `pypdfbox/pdmodel/fdf/fdf_document.py::FDFDocument.save` drove the shared `COSWriter`, which hardcoded the `%PDF-` marker. PDFBox's `FDFParser` rejects a `%PDF-` header (`Error: Header doesn't contain versioninfo`), so a pypdfbox-saved FDF could not be reloaded by PDFBox. Added an `fdf=True` flag to `pypdfbox/pdfwriter/cos_writer.py::COSWriter` (mirrors upstream COSWriter, whose `doWriteHeader` switches the marker when `write(FDFDocument)` set an `fdfDocument`); `FDFDocument.save` now passes it. Cross-module root cause: the header-marker switch lives in `pdfwriter`.
- **`FDFDocument.load` rejected every real FDF file (bugfix)**: `FDFDocument.load` routed through `Loader.load_pdf`, whose `PDFParser.parse_header` only accepted `%PDF-` — so a genuine `%FDF-`-headed FDF (including one pypdfbox itself just saved) failed to load. Taught `pypdfbox/pdfparser/pdf_parser.py::parse_header` to accept `%FDF-` as well (the rest of the object/xref/trailer structure is identical; matches upstream's generic `COSParser.parseHeader(marker, default)`). The existing `FDFParser` could not be used directly here because pypdfbox's xref-chain walk lives in `PDFParser`, not `COSParser`. Cross-module root cause: the header check lives in `pdfparser`.

Documented (not bugs): the XFDF serialiser (`FDFDictionary.writeXML`) does not emit `<annots>`, so XFDF round-trips fields + `/F` but drops annotations — both libraries identical. A multi-select field written to XFDF as repeated `<value>` elements collapses to the *last* value on reload — both libraries identical (PDFBox's `FDFField(Element)` keeps only the last `<value>`).

## Wave 1418 — expand the live oracle to 6 more surfaces (~12 real bugs fixed)

6 agents extended the live PDFBox 3.0.7 oracle to the writer decrypt-then-re-encrypt path, CCITTFax images, TrueType/Type0 subset embedding, public-key encryption, image soft masks, and trailer `/ID`. ~12 real bugs fixed, several high-impact (soft-mask + subset-embed detail in the subsections below; public-key detail near the file's public-key section):

- **writer decrypt-then-re-encrypt double-hop (bugfix, closes the wave-1409 xfail)**: a stream loaded encrypted + lazily decrypted (`_decrypted=False`) was re-enciphered a second time on save (its raw body was still ciphertext) → FlateDecode garbage on reload. Added `COSStream.ensure_decrypted()` (one-shot decrypt-on-access), called from `COSWriter.visit_from_stream` before re-enciphering. The 4 strict `xfail`s (Java-encrypt → pypdfbox-re-encrypt → Java-decrypt, all 4 algorithms) now pass.
- **CCITTFax image decode polarity (bugfix)**: `CcittImgProbe` showed pypdfbox decoded *every* CCITT Group 3/4 image as the exact **bit-inverse** of PDFBox (black/white swapped), all K modes + both `/BlackIs1`. Flipped the decoder photometric + encoder raster-inversion in `ccitt_fax_decode.py` to match `CCITTFaxFilter`; pypdfbox's G4 encoder output is now byte-identical to `CCITTFactory.createFromImage`.
- **public-key (certificate) encryption interop (3 bugfixes)**: `/Recipients` emitted/read inside `/CF /DefaultCryptFilter` (not `/Encrypt` top level), `/CF` subtree marked direct/inline, crypt-filter `/Length` written in bits. pypdfbox-pubkey-encrypts → Java-decrypts now FULL for AES-128/256 (was entirely broken); Java→pypdfbox stays UNSUPPORTED (PDFBox's RC2-CBC CMS envelope — `cryptography` does AES-CBC only) via a clear `UnsupportedAlgorithm`.
- **trailer `/ID` on incremental save (bugfix)**: incremental save copied the source `/ID` verbatim, leaving `/ID[1]` unchanged — an ISO 32000-1 §14.4 violation. Now preserves `/ID[0]` and regenerates `/ID[1]` (digest recipe differs from upstream's MD5, so the test asserts the structural contract, not byte-equality).

### image soft masks / explicit + color-key /Mask (2 real bugs fixed)

Extended the live PDFBox 3.0.7 render oracle (`RenderProbe`) to image-XObject masking over a coloured backdrop, 72 DPI, 16x16 luminance grid gated at MAD<6 / MAXDIFF<60 (`tests/rendering/oracle/test_soft_mask_oracle.py`). Three mutually-exclusive mask forms covered: `/SMask` soft mask, explicit 1-bit `/Mask` stencil, color-key `/Mask` array. The renderer's `_op_do` honoured `/SMask` (already correct, MAD 0.11) but **silently ignored both the explicit `/Mask` stream and the color-key `/Mask` array** — the base image painted fully opaque (stencil MAD 6.36; color-key MAD 31.85). Both fixed in `pypdfbox/rendering/pdf_renderer.py`:

- **explicit `/Mask` stencil ignored (1 bug)**: `_op_do` never consulted `get_mask()`. Added `_apply_explicit_mask` — decodes the 1-bit stencil, applies it as alpha (PDF §8.9.6.3: with default `/Decode [0 1]` sample 1 = masked-out/transparent, sample 0 = painted; `/Decode [1 0]` reverses), resized nearest-neighbour to the base image. Now MAD 0.89.
- **color-key `/Mask` array ignored (1 bug)**: `_op_do` never consulted `get_color_key_mask()`. Added `_apply_color_key_mask` — pixels whose every component falls inside the per-component `[min max]` ranges (PDF §8.9.6.4) are made transparent; exact for 8-bit DeviceRGB/DeviceGray. Now MAD 0.00. `/SMask` takes precedence, then explicit `/Mask`, then color-key (mutually exclusive per spec).

### TrueType / Type0 font embedding + subsetting (3 real bugs fixed)

New live-oracle probe `SubsetEmbedProbe` loads a pypdfbox-produced PDF, reaches the embedded font program through Apache PDFBox's own loaders (`PDTrueTypeFont.getTrueTypeFont()` / `PDCIDFontType2.getTrueTypeFont()`), and emits the embedded program's glyph count, unitsPerEm, cmap/glyf/hmtx presence, per-GID advances, and per-used-code `getWidthFromFont`. pypdfbox embeds LiberationSans full + subset (composite CIDFontType2 and simple TrueType), and the embedded program / widths / text round-trip are asserted line-for-line against PDFBox 3.0.7 plus `PDFTextStripper` text recovery (`tests/pdmodel/font/oracle/test_subset_embed_oracle.py`, 19 cases). Three real bugs fixed in `pypdfbox/pdmodel/font/pd_type0_font.py`:

- **embedded Identity-H `encode` emitted the codepoint instead of the glyph id (1 bug)**: `PDType0Font.encode` / `_encode_codepoint` returned the raw Unicode codepoint as the 2-byte CID for an embedded Identity-H font, so with `/CIDToGIDMap /Identity` every glyph rendered wrong (PDFBox extracted "Hello" as "e£ªª­"). Now mirrors upstream `PDCIDFontType2.encode` (PDCIDFontType2.java:357-414): for an embedded font under an Identity- CMap the CID is `cmap.getGlyphId(unicode)` (the embedded program's glyph id). Non-embedded / no-cmap fonts keep the predefined-CMap reverse-lookup fallback.
- **`subset()` left `/W` and `/CIDToGIDMap` stale after glyph renumbering (1 bug)**: fontTools renumbers the subset's glyphs, but `subset()` only swapped `/FontFile2` bytes — `/W` still carried the full font's ~2600 glyph widths and `/CIDToGIDMap` was still `/Identity`, so the original-GID CIDs in the content stream resolved to nonexistent / wrong subset glyphs. Now pins the encoded original glyph ids into the subset, then rebuilds `/CIDToGIDMap` (a stream mapping original-GID → renumbered-subset-GID) and `/W` (keyed by the surviving CIDs only), mirroring `PDCIDFontType2Embedder.buildSubset`. Subset PDF shrank 33 KB → 11 KB.
- **embedded Type0 font had no `/ToUnicode` CMap (1 bug)**: `_build_type0_from_ttf` never wrote `/ToUnicode`, so text extraction from a freshly embedded font produced garbage even though the glyphs rendered correctly. Now builds a `/ToUnicode` CMap keyed by glyph id (= the content-stream code under our Identity-H encoding) via the embedded program's reverse cmap.

The simple `PDTrueTypeFont` embed/subset path was already correct (1-byte WinAnsi codes + name-keyed cmap lookup survive renumbering) and is covered as a parity guard. Width parity uses a 1e-3 numeric tolerance on the 4th decimal: Java `String.format("%.4f")` rounds half-up while Python rounds half-even (e.g. 519.53125 → 519.5313 vs 519.5312); the underlying width is identical.

## Wave 1417 — expand the live oracle to 6 more surfaces (~9 real bugs fixed)

6 agents extended the live PDFBox 3.0.7 oracle to embedded Type1 fonts, simple-font `/Encoding`+`/Differences`, ExtGState, name/number trees, XMP typed schema values, and the Adobe glyph list. **Oracle infra**: the standalone `pdfbox-app` jar does NOT bundle `xmpbox`, so `oracle/download_jars.sh` now also fetches the Apache-2.0 `xmpbox-3.0.7.jar` (sha256-pinned) and `tests/oracle/harness.py` globs every jar in `oracle/jars/` onto the probe classpath. Bugs fixed across Type1/encoding/ExtGState/glyph-list; name/number trees and XMP typed values confirmed clean.

- **Type1 font embedding (3 bugs; closes the wave-1416 deferred item)**: `PDType1FontEmbedder` constructed fontTools `T1Font(BytesIO)` but fontTools needs a file path → pypdfbox could not embed a classic Type1 `/FontFile` at all. Fixed to parse via `Type1Font.from_bytes`. Surfaced 2 more: the `/FontFile` was tagged `FlateDecode` but stored uncompressed (unreadable on reload) — now written through `create_output_stream(FLATE_DECODE)`; and `/Widths` were all 0 because the width read happened before a glyph draw. Round-trip verified: pypdfbox embeds → Apache PDFBox reads back the same name/encoding/widths. (`build_font_descriptor` was rewritten onto the `Type1Font` accessor surface; 3 white-box branch-coverage tests using the old `.font`-dict stub were updated to the accessor contract.)
- **simple-font `/Encoding` `/Differences` base fallback (1 bug)**: `PDSimpleFont.get_encoding_typed()` built `DictionaryEncoding` without the symbolic flag, so a `/Differences` font with no `/BaseEncoding` lost the StandardEncoding (non-symbolic) / built-in (symbolic) base — every non-overridden code resolved to `.notdef`. Now mirrors upstream `readEncoding`'s symbolic-aware dictionary branch.
- **ExtGState accessor defaults (4 bugs)**: absent-key defaults in `PDExtendedGraphicsState` were wrong vs upstream — `getLineCapStyle`/`getLineJoinStyle` absent→`None` (should be `-1`), `getOverprintMode` absent→`0` (should be `None`), `getFlatness`/`getSmoothness` absent→`1.0`/`0.0` (should be `None`), `getBlendMode` absent→`None` (should be `NORMAL`). All four corrected; renderer call sites were already None-guarded so rendering is unaffected.
- **Adobe glyph list (2 bugs, incl. a deadlock)**: `glyph_list.py` synthesized algorithmic `uXXXX` names of length 5–7 (so `u1F600`→U+1F600) where upstream gates on exact length (`u` must be 5, `uni` must be 7); tightened the regex + `_derive`. **Also fixed a latent deadlock**: `to_unicode` called `_derive` while holding the non-reentrant cache lock, and `_derive` recurses into `to_unicode` to strip `name.suffix` → re-acquiring the same lock hung the thread permanently. Restructured to derive lock-free.
- **name/number trees (parity confirmed, no bug)**: `PDNameTreeNode`/`PDNumberTreeNode` flatten + `/Limits` descent + `get(key)` match across single/multi-level trees; pypdfbox is strictly more robust than upstream on malformed (`/Limits`-missing) nodes (documented).
- **XMP typed schema values (parity confirmed, no bug)**: Dublin Core / XMPBasic / AdobePDF / PDF-A-id typed getters match Apache xmpbox across PDFA3A + Acrobat fixtures (1 documented strict-mode leniency: pypdfbox tolerates undefined-namespace properties where upstream's strict parser throws).

## Wave 1416 — expand the live oracle to 6 more surfaces (3 real bugs fixed)

6 agents extended the live PDFBox 3.0.7 oracle to COS scalar self-serialization, inline-image pixel decode, object-stream/compressed save, embedded Type1 fonts, the remaining non-widget annotation appearance handlers, and pattern rendering. Bugs fixed in the first two + annotations; object-stream save, Type1 fonts, and pattern rendering confirmed clean. Clean-surface notes: **object-stream/compressed save** (`ObjStmSaveProbe` — pypdfbox's `COSWriter(xref_stream=True, object_stream=True)` is qpdf-valid, packs the same order of magnitude of objects as PDFBox, never packs a `COSStream` or the `/Encrypt` dict, reloads identically); **Type1 fonts** (`Type1FontProbe` — encoding map / per-glyph widths / hasGlyph / font matrix match across built embedded-Type1 fixtures; matrix compared numerically since PDFBox widens `float`→`double`); **pattern rendering** (`RenderProbe` — coloured/uncoloured tiling + axial/radial shading patterns render within the wave-1408 MAD<6 tolerance). A cross-module Type1-embedder bug was surfaced and deferred (see `DEFERRED.md`).

### COS float self-write unification (1 real bug fixed)

`CosWriteSelfProbe` drives each COS scalar type's own `writePDF`. **`COSFloat.format_string`/`write_pdf` carried a SEPARATE float formatter** (the wave-1415 fix only touched `COSWriter.format_float`) using `repr`+`Decimal.normalize`, which leaked float32 representation noise on the self-write path (`0.1`→`0.10000000149011612`, `123456789.0`→`123456792.0`) and crashed with `OverflowError` formatting `Float.MAX_VALUE`. Unified all float serialization onto a single shared `cos_float.format_float32` (with an OverflowError guard): `COSFloat.format_string`, `COSFloat.write_pdf`, and `COSWriter.format_float` now all delegate to it — one formatter, zero drift (removed the writer's duplicate copy). All scalar self-writes (float/int/name `#`-escaping/string/bool/null) match PDFBox byte-for-byte; corrected 2 tests asserting the buggy float64 `Float.MAX_VALUE` form. Documented: the smallest subnormal (`Float.MIN_VALUE`) emits the truly-shortest round-tripping decimal vs Java's non-minimal legacy `FloatingDecimal` form (re-parses to the identical float32).

### inline-image (BI/ID/EI) pixel decode (1 real bug fixed)

New live-oracle probe `InlineImgProbe` decodes every inline image on a page through PDFBox 3.0.7 (`PDFStreamEngine` + a `BeginInlineImage`-keyed `OperatorProcessor` building `PDInlineImage`, then `getImage()`) and emits per image `width height bpc colorSpaceName` + a 16×16 luminance fingerprint of the decoded raster. pypdfbox is compared on the same content streams across the abbreviated filters (`AHx` / `A85` / `Fl` / `RL` / `DCT`) and abbreviated colour spaces (`G` / `RGB` / `CMYK` / `I`), plus a 1-bit bilevel image and a multi-image page. Tests in `tests/rendering/oracle/test_inline_image_oracle.py` (10 cases, all `@requires_oracle`).

**Real bug fixed — `PDInlineImage.to_pil_image` was a stripped-down decoder that returned `None` (blank/undecodable) for Indexed, DeviceCMYK, sub-byte (1/2/4 bpc) and 16-bit rasters** that PDFBox's `PDInlineImage.getImage()` decodes fine. The XObject path (`PDImageXObject.to_pil_image`) already had the full decoder; the inline path duplicated only an 8-bit DeviceGray/RGB subset. Refactored the proven raster-decode core into a shared module-level `decode_pdimage_to_pil(pd_image, filter_names)` in `pypdfbox/pdmodel/graphics/image/pd_image_x_object.py` (operating purely on the `PDImage` accessor surface) and routed both `PDImageXObject.to_pil_image` and `PDInlineImage.to_pil_image` through it. Now Indexed (1/2/4/8 bpc), DeviceCMYK, sub-byte/16-bit DeviceGray and the abbreviated filters all decode. Device gray/RGB/indexed/1-bit rasters match PDFBox byte-for-byte (MAD=0, MAXDIFF=0); DeviceCMYK matches within the already-documented CMYK→RGB CMM-vs-explicit-math band (CHANGES "color spaces → RGB"). Also confirmed PDFBox's `getImage()` on a stencil returns a (non-null) decoded bilevel raster — pypdfbox now matches (was returning `None`); 5 white-box/upstream tests that asserted the old None behaviour were corrected to the now-faithful decode.

### remaining non-widget annotation appearance handlers (1 real bug fixed)

`AnnotAppear2Probe` covers the markup types wave 1414 left untouched: Text (Note icon), Caret, FileAttachment (PushPin), StrikeOut, Underline, Squiggly, FreeText (+ Popup/Stamp which have no upstream handler → NOAP on both sides). **Same wave-1414 bug in 7 more subclasses: `construct_appearances()` was a no-op on the default (no-custom-handler) path** — the built-in handler existed in `handlers/` but the subclass only invoked a *custom* handler and otherwise fell through to the base no-op, so a freshly-built annotation produced no `/AP`. Upstream always instantiates the default handler when `customAppearanceHandler == null`. Fixed `pd_annotation_text.py`, `pd_annotation_caret.py`, `pd_annotation_file_attachment.py`, `pd_annotation_strikeout.py`, `pd_annotation_underline.py`, `pd_annotation_squiggly.py`, `pd_annotation_free_text.py`. Every `/BBox` now matches PDFBox; Text/Caret/StrikeOut/Underline operator sequences match after normalising the documented `CS/SC`→`RG` colour-op divergence (same as wave-1414 Ink). Documented draw-form divergences (BBox exact): Squiggly inline zig-zag vs tiling-pattern form XObject, FileAttachment stylized icon, FreeText line-wrap layout. Corrected 5 stale tests that encoded the old no-op (switched to `PDAnnotationUnknown`, the genuine handler-less base type). Tests in `tests/pdmodel/interactive/annotation/oracle/test_annotation_appearance_gen2_oracle.py`.

## Wave 1415 — expand the live oracle to 6 more surfaces (5 real bugs fixed)

6 agents extended the live PDFBox 3.0.7 oracle to COS scalar write-serialization, COSString text/date decode, glyph outlines, page boxes, predefined CMaps, and annotation flags/MK/border. Bugs fixed in the first three surfaces; page boxes / predefined CMaps / annotation flags confirmed clean (page-box clipping + UserUnit, the bundled-CMap subset's CID/codespace/WMode, and `/F` flags / `/BS` / `/MK` all match — with two documented API-shape `_or_default()` accessor splits).

### COSWriter float serialization (1 real bug fixed)

`WriteScalarProbe` writes individual COS scalars (float / int / string literal-vs-hex / name `#`-escaping / bool / null) via PDFBox's own serialization and compares the exact bytes (70 cases). **`COSWriter.format_float` leaked float32 representation noise on every float written to a PDF** — `format(value, ".10g")` on the float32-coerced double gave `0.1`→`0.1000000015`, `-0.000123`→`-0.0001230000053`, `3.14159…`→`3.141592741`, `123456789.0`→`123456792`, and dropped trailing `.0` from whole numbers. Upstream `COSFloat.formatString` does `Float.toString(value)` verbatim unless it has an `E` (then `BigDecimal(s).stripTrailingZeros().toPlainString()`). Fixed in `pypdfbox/pdfwriter/cos_writer.py` via `_shortest_float32_decimal` (shortest `%g` digit string round-tripping through `struct` float32) + `_java_float_format` (signed-zero; plain-with-`.0` in `[1e-3, 1e7)`, else `Decimal.normalize`). All 70 cases now byte-identical; rewrote 3 white-box tests that asserted the buggy `.10g` internals. (Cross-module follow-up: `cos_float.py::COSFloat.format_string` has a *separate* formatter on its own `write_pdf` path — should route through the same logic; flagged, out of this wave's writer scope.)

### COSString text decode + PDF date parse (3 real bugs fixed)

New live-oracle probe `CosStrTextDateProbe` (two modes: `str` emits `COSString.parseHex(hex).getString()` as space-separated Unicode code-point hex; `date` emits `DateConverter.toCalendar(str)` normalised to ISO-8601 or `NULL`). pypdfbox is asserted byte-for-byte against Apache PDFBox 3.0.7 across a text-decode battery (UTF-16BE/LE BOM, full PDFDocEncoding high range 0x80–0xA0, block-1 deviations 0x18–0x1F, undefined 0x7F/0x9F → U+FFFD, NUL-defaulted 0xAD, ASCII) and a date battery (full/partial dates, `Z` / quoted / unquoted / partial offsets, out-of-range fields, out-of-range offsets). Tests in `tests/cos/oracle/test_cos_string_text_oracle.py` (74 cases, all `@requires_oracle`). Three real bugs fixed:

- **`COSString.get_string()` raised `UnicodeDecodeError` on truncated/malformed UTF-16.** `pypdfbox/cos/cos_string.py`: the UTF-16BE/LE BOM branches decoded with the default `strict` error handler, so an odd trailing byte after the BOM (e.g. `FE FF 00 41 00`) crashed instead of yielding `…�`. Upstream `COSString.getString()` uses `new String(byte[], offset, length, StandardCharsets.UTF_16BE)`, whose default malformed-input action is REPLACE. Fixed: both UTF-16 branches (and the UTF-8 branch) now decode with `errors="replace"`, matching PDFBox's lenient substitution.
- **PDF date second 60 (leap-second-style) was clamped to 59 instead of rejected.** `pypdfbox/cos/cos_dictionary.py::_parse_pdf_date`: previously clamped `second == 60` → 59 and returned a `datetime`. Upstream `DateConverter.toCalendar` parses with `GregorianCalendar.setLenient(false)`, so second 60 (and any other out-of-range field) fails the parse and returns `null`. Fixed: removed the clamp; the out-of-range second now propagates through the `datetime(...)` `ValueError` → `None`, matching PDFBox.
- **Out-of-range PDF timezone offset crashed with `ValueError`.** `pypdfbox/cos/cos_dictionary.py::_parse_pdf_date`: a designation like `+24'00'`, `+99'00'`, or `+05'99'` built a `timedelta` ≥ 24h and `datetime.timezone(...)` raised an uncaught `ValueError`. Upstream builds the zone from a raw offset and lets `Calendar.ZONE_OFFSET` reduce it modulo 24h (truncating toward zero, Java `%` semantics: `+99'00'` → +03:00, `-99'00'` → −03:00, `+48'30'` → +00:30, `+05'99'` → +06:39, `+24'00'` → +00:00). Fixed: offset minutes are reduced via `t - 1440 * int(t / 1440)` before constructing the `timezone`, matching PDFBox exactly.

Active divergences (documented, asserted as pypdfbox-side):

- **`COSString.get_string()` strips a UTF-8 BOM (`EF BB BF`) and decodes as UTF-8.** `pypdfbox/cos/cos_string.py`: a deliberate forward-port of PDF 2.0 §7.9.2.2 / PDFBox 4.0. The pinned upstream baseline (PDFBox 3.0.7) has no UTF-8-BOM branch in `getString()` and decodes those bytes as PDFDocEncoding (`EF BB BF 41` → `ef bb bf 41`); pypdfbox yields the BOM-stripped text (`41`). Confirmed against the live oracle in `test_utf8_bom_is_documented_divergence`.
  upstream: PDFBox 3.0.7 `org.apache.pdfbox.cos.COSString#getString`
  reason: PDF 2.0 / PDFBox 4.0 forward-compat; matches the project's 4.0-alignment policy in CLAUDE.md.
- **`_parse_pdf_date` handles only the compact `D:YYYYMMDDHHmmSSOHH'mm'` numeric form.** `pypdfbox/cos/cos_dictionary.py`: upstream `DateConverter.toCalendar` additionally tolerates separator-bearing numeric forms (`D:2024-03-15`, `2024/03/15`, `D:2024-03-15T12:00:00-05:00`, space/`T`-separated, 1-or-2-digit fields) and a long list of `SimpleDateFormat` alpha-start fallback patterns. The cos-level helper deliberately mirrors only the common compact subset (consistent with its docstring); the separator-tolerant + alpha-format fallbacks are served by `pypdfbox/xmpbox/date_converter.py::to_calendar` + `pypdfbox/util/date_util.py` for the XMP/metadata surface. Inputs outside the compact subset return `None` from `_parse_pdf_date`.
  upstream: PDFBox 3.0.7 `org.apache.pdfbox.util.DateConverter#toCalendar`
  reason: the cos-level fast path covers the dominant on-disk `D:` form; separator/alpha tolerance lives in the dedicated DateConverter port.
- **Year 0 / BCE PDF dates return `None` (Python `datetime` minimum year is 1).** Standing Python-platform limitation (kept). Observable result agrees with PDFBox here only incidentally — PDFBox's non-lenient Gregorian calendar also rejects a four-zero year — but the cause differs.
  upstream: PDFBox 3.0.7 `org.apache.pdfbox.util.DateConverter#toCalendar`
  reason: `datetime.MINYEAR == 1`; pre-Gregorian / proleptic years are out of range.

Annotation common-property live-oracle parity (`AnnotFlagsProbe`, two modes — `read` lists every annotation's `/F` flag predicates + `/BS` width/style/dash + `/MK` rotation + `/BC`/`/BG` component counts + caption; `write` builds an all-`/F`-bits + dashed-`/BS` + full-`/MK` widget so every branch is exercised). pypdfbox's `is_*` flag predicates, `PDBorderStyleDictionary` (width/style/dash/phase) and `PDAppearanceCharacteristicsDictionary` (rotation + colour component counts + caption) match Apache PDFBox 3.0.7 byte-for-byte across `AnnotationTypes.pdf`, the AcroForm widget fixtures (`AcroFormsBasicFields`, `AcroFormsRotation`, `PDFBOX-5784`, `PDFBOX-3656-SF1199AEG (Complete)`), and the built all-bits fixture. Tests in `tests/pdmodel/interactive/annotation/oracle/test_annotation_flags_oracle.py` (all `@requires_oracle`). No real bugs found. One API-shape note documented below.

Active divergence (documented, API-shape — NOT a bug):

- **`PDBorderStyleDictionary.get_dash_style()` returns `None` when `/D` is absent; `get_dash_style_or_default()` is the upstream-faithful accessor.** `pypdfbox/pdmodel/interactive/annotation/pd_border_style_dictionary.py`: upstream `getDashStyle()` *always* returns a non-null `PDLineDashPattern`, seeding the spec default `[3]` into the dictionary (a side-effecting write) when `/D` is missing. pypdfbox splits this into a side-effect-free `get_dash_style()` (returns `None` when absent) plus `get_dash_style_or_default()` (the upstream-equivalent that seeds `[3]`). The appearance handlers (`pd_appearance_content_stream.py`, `handlers/annotation_border.py`) use `get_dash_style_or_default()`, so rendered/generated borders match upstream. The `AnnotFlagsProbe` differential reads via `get_dash_style_or_default()` and confirms exact parity. Same precedent as the `getPageLayout`/`getPageMode` vs `get_*_or_default()` note above.
  upstream: PDFBox 3.0.7 `org.apache.pdfbox.pdmodel.interactive.annotation.PDBorderStyleDictionary#getDashStyle`
  reason: a side-effecting getter (mutating the dict on a read) is non-idiomatic in Python; the upstream behaviour is preserved verbatim under the `_or_default` name, which all internal callers use.

Glyph-OUTLINE (path) live-oracle parity (`GlyphPathProbe` — per-GID fingerprint of `getPath()`'s `java.awt.geom.GeneralPath`: tight control-curve bounding box + segment count + M/L/Q/C/Z type sequence, read straight from the embedded FontBox program: TrueType via `ttf.getGlyph().getGlyph(gid).getPath()`, CFF via `cff.getType2CharString(gid).getPath()`). pypdfbox's glyph path matches Apache PDFBox 3.0.7 per GID across embedded TrueType (Liberation, Calibri, Verdana, Symbol) and CFF (Century, Courier) fonts. Tests in `tests/fontbox/ttf/oracle/test_glyph_path_oracle.py` (all `@requires_oracle`; 5 fixtures). One real bug fixed:

- **TrueType simple-glyph outlines were missing the left-side-bearing x-shift.** `pypdfbox/fontbox/ttf/glyph_data.py` + `pypdfbox/fontbox/ttf/glyph_table.py`: upstream `GlyphTable.getGlyphData` threads `hmtx.getLeftSideBearing(gid)` into `GlyphData.initData`, and `GlyfSimpleDescript` starts the x-coordinate accumulator at the LSB instead of the glyf-stored `xMin` — equivalent to translating every simple-glyph point by `(leftSideBearing − xMin)` in x. pypdfbox decodes glyf via fontTools (spec-correct xMin-aligned coordinates), so `getPath()` placed glyphs whose LSB ≠ xMin (subset/hinted fonts) at the wrong x (e.g. Verdana `.notdef` at x 256 vs PDFBox's 103). Fixed: `GlyphTable.get_glyph` now passes the per-gid LSB to `GlyphData`; `GlyphData._x_shift()` computes `(lsb − xMin)` for **simple** glyphs only (composites place components by their own recursively-shifted coordinates + offsets, matching upstream's `GlyfCompositeDescript` which takes no LSB), and the shift is applied in `GlyphDescription.get_x_coordinate` and the fontTools-backed `get_path()`. `tests/fontbox` (5332) stays green.

Active divergences (documented representational differences — NOT bugs; the fingerprint normalises them):

- **CFF `Type2CharString.get_path()` omits the trailing no-op `moveTo` PDFBox emits after each `closePath`.** Upstream builds the CFF outline through `Type1CharString` whose `closeCharString1Path` appends `GeneralPath.moveTo(currentPoint)` after every `closePath()` (priming the next sub-path). pypdfbox delegates to fontTools' charstring `draw`, which omits that no-op moveTo (a moveTo with nothing drawn after it). The glyph shape is identical; only the trailing path command differs. The test re-inserts the moveTo (and coalesces consecutive moveTos the way `GeneralPath` does) to prove segment-structure parity.
  upstream: PDFBox 3.0.7 `org.apache.fontbox.cff.Type1CharString#closeCharString1Path`
  reason: a dangling trailing moveTo carries no rendered geometry; pypdfbox's `get_path()` returns the clean fontTools command list its own renderer consumes.
- **TrueType outline representation: fontTools' packed `qCurveTo` vs PDFBox's per-quad `quadTo`.** fontTools' `RecordingPen` packs a run of N off-curve TrueType points (with implied on-curve midpoints) into one `qCurveTo`; PDFBox's `GlyphRenderer` emits one `quadTo` per off-curve point and closes an on-curve-start contour with an explicit `lineTo` to the start. Both describe the identical curve. The differential drives pypdfbox's own *ported* `GlyphRenderer` (`pypdfbox/fontbox/ttf/glyph_renderer.py`) — a faithful line-by-line port whose op stream is already one-segment-per-quad and bit-matches the Java `PathIterator` — so the type sequence + count compare exactly with no synthetic normalisation.
  upstream: PDFBox 3.0.7 `org.apache.fontbox.ttf.GlyphRenderer`
  reason: fontTools owns glyf decoding (library-first); the ported renderer reproduces upstream's exact segment emission for parity-sensitive callers.
- **Bbox is the tight curve box, matching AWT.** Java `Path2D.getBounds2D()` returns tight Bezier-arc bounds (it evaluates curve extrema), not the loose control-point union; the test mirrors this by solving each quad/cubic coordinate's derivative for the in-range critical parameter. A 1-unit per-edge epsilon absorbs only the `Math.round` (half-up) vs Python `round` (half-even) split at an exact `.5`.

## Wave 1414 — expand the live oracle to 6 more surfaces (4 real bugs fixed)

6 agents extended the live PDFBox 3.0.7 oracle to non-widget annotation appearance generation, PDF functions + shading colour, glyph advance width from the font program, document catalog properties, per-glyph TextPosition geometry, and stream-length/COS-scalar parsing edge cases. Four real bugs fixed:

- **glyph advance — CFF out-of-range GID (bugfix)**: `GlyphAdvanceProbe` (per-GID advance in design units + unitsPerEm from the embedded FontBox program, not `/Widths`) matched across embedded TrueType + CFF fonts except out-of-range GIDs. `pypdfbox/fontbox/cff/cff_font.py::get_type2_char_string` returned an empty wrapper (width 0) for `gid >= numCharStrings`; upstream `CFFFont.getType2CharString` falls back to `.notdef` (GID 0, `bytes = charStrings[0]`). Fixed to fall back to GID 0 (negative GID keeps the non-raising empty-wrapper ergonomic divergence). Corrected the misleading test that asserted the empty wrapper.
- **stream length — wrong/missing `/Length` recovery (bugfix)**: `StreamLenRecoverProbe` + `ParseEdgeTokenProbe` over hand-crafted tricky-but-valid PDFs. A present-but-wrong `/Length` (too small/large/zero/indirect-wrong) made pypdfbox raise `expected 'endstream'` and fail the object, where PDFBox recovers by scanning to `endstream` and rewriting `/Length`. `pypdfbox/pdfparser/pdf_parser.py::_read_stream_body` now validates the declared length and falls back to `read_until_end_stream` (the upstream `COSParser.parseCOSStream` ports existed but were never wired into the live load path). COS-scalar parsing (numbers `--2`/`.5`/`4.`/`+3`/`007`, octal/nested-paren/line-continuation strings, `#`-hex names, duplicate dict keys) was already at full parity — no change needed.
- **per-glyph TextPosition geometry (parity confirmed, lite carve-outs)**: `TextPosGeomProbe` (subclasses `PDFTextStripper`, emits unicode + xDirAdj/yDirAdj/widthDirAdj/heightDir/fontSizeInPt). Run/line origins and effective font size match PDFBox within <0.5pt (confirms the wave-1409 CTM work). Documented lite-port carve-outs: one `TextPosition` per show-text run (not per glyph → intra-line x drift from average-advance widths), y-up frame (relates to Java `getYDirAdj()` by `page_height − y`), `getHeightDir()` returns font size not bbox height. No code change.
- **document catalog properties (parity confirmed, no bug)**: `CatalogProbe` (`/Version`, `/PageLayout`, `/PageMode`, `/Lang`, `/OpenAction` kind, `/MarkInfo` flags, `/ViewerPreferences` sub-flags, `/OutputIntents`, AcroForm/StructTreeRoot/PageLabels presence) matches across tagged PDF/A, AcroForm, outline, and a built all-properties fixture. (API-shape note: Java's `getPageLayout`/`getPageMode` bake in the spec default; pypdfbox's `get_*_or_default()` are the upstream-equivalent accessors.)

### non-widget annotation appearance generation (1 bug fixed)

New live-oracle probe `AnnotAppearGenProbe` (write mode builds a page of markup annotations — Line, Square, Circle, Polygon, PolyLine, Ink, Highlight — sets rect / stroke colour / interior colour / border width / line endings, calls `constructAppearances(doc)` on each, and saves; read mode re-opens and emits per annotation the `/AP /N` operator-token sequence via `PDFStreamParser` plus the appearance `/BBox` rendered as canonical floats). pypdfbox builds the identical battery, calls `construct_appearances()`, tokenises the generated `/AP /N`, and the operator KEYWORD sequence + bbox are asserted exact against Apache PDFBox 3.0.7. Tests in `tests/pdmodel/interactive/annotation/oracle/test_annotation_appearance_gen_oracle.py` (3 tests, all `@requires_oracle`).

- **`construct_appearances()` was a no-op on the default (no custom handler) path for Line / Square / Circle / Polygon / PolyLine / Ink / Highlight — no `/AP` stream was generated at all.** Upstream `constructAppearances(PDDocument)` always instantiates the matching built-in appearance handler when `customAppearanceHandler == null` (verified against `PDAnnotationLine.java:422`, `PDAnnotationInk.java:126`, `PDAnnotationSquare.java:68`, `PDAnnotationCircle.java:67`, `PDAnnotationPolygon.java:176`, `PDAnnotationPolyline.java:191`, `PDAnnotationHighlight.java:71`). The pypdfbox subclasses fell through to the base no-op, so a freshly-built annotation never produced an appearance. Fixed each subclass to instantiate + run the built-in handler on the default path. The handlers themselves were already correct — once wired, every operator sequence and bbox matches PDFBox exactly. Files: `pypdfbox/pdmodel/interactive/annotation/pd_annotation_line.py:347`, `pd_annotation_ink.py:169`, `pd_annotation_polygon.py:276`, `pd_annotation_polyline.py:256`, `pd_annotation_highlight.py:50`, `pd_annotation_square_circle.py:255` (Square) + `:308` (Circle). Four stale tests that asserted the old no-op behaviour were corrected (`tests/pdmodel/interactive/annotation/test_pd_annotation_square_circle.py`, `test_pd_annotation_line_wave1273.py`, `test_pd_annotation_ink_wave1273.py`, `test_pd_annotation_highlight_wave268.py`) — empty-geometry annotations still write no `/AP` (the handler early-returns when rect/line/inklist/quadpoints is absent, matching upstream).

Documented (NOT bugs — pre-existing lite-surface divergences, normalised in the oracle test):
- **Ink stroking-colour operator `RG` vs upstream `CS SC`.** Upstream `PDInkAppearanceHandler` calls `cs.setStrokingColor(PDColor)` which, for a DeviceRGB colour, emits `/DeviceRGB CS` + `r g b SC`; pypdfbox's lite annotation colour surface has no typed `PDColor` with an explicit colour space (deferred to the rendering cluster — see the `getColor` note elsewhere in this file), so `set_stroking_color([r,g,b])` emits the device shorthand `r g b RG`. Identical colour, identical path-drawing operators (`m l l S`); only the colour-set operator spelling differs. The Line handler (which uses `setStrokingColorOnDemand` upstream → `RG`) matches exactly.
- **Highlight transparency group.** Upstream wraps the quad fill in a two-form-XObject transparency group with a Multiply blend (outer stream is `gs gs Do`). `PDFormXObject` group emission isn't ported, so the lite highlight handler applies the same alpha + Multiply `ExtGState` inline and fills the quad directly (`gs gs <colour> <path> f`). The `/BBox` matches PDFBox exactly.

Cross-module observation (NOT in annotation scope, NOT fixed): two distinct `Operator` classes exist — `pypdfbox.pdfparser.pdf_stream_parser.Operator` (what `PDFStreamParser` returns) and `pypdfbox.contentstream.operator.Operator`. `isinstance` against the wrong one silently fails. The annotation oracle test imports the parser's `Operator`; the duplication itself is a `pdfparser`/`contentstream` concern to reconcile in those modules.

### PDF functions + axial/radial shading colour (1 bug fixed)

New live-oracle probe `ShadingFuncProbe` (hard-codes a battery of PDF functions — Type 2 exponential, Type 3 stitching, Type 0 sampled at 4/8/16-bit and 1-D/2-D grids, Type 4 PostScript calculator — and axial/radial shadings, then emits each function's `eval(inputs) -> outputs` and each shading's colour function at t=0,0.25,0.5,0.75,1.0 as canonical `%.6f` lines). pypdfbox rebuilds the identical COS objects and asserts line-by-line equality against Apache PDFBox 3.0.7. Tests in `tests/pdmodel/graphics/shading/oracle/test_shading_func_oracle.py` (1 test, `@requires_oracle`). Epsilon: function math is near-exact; Java float32 vs Python float64 agree to 6 dp across the whole battery (documented `2e-6` numeric fallback never triggers).

- **`PDFunctionType2.eval` was clipping its input to `/Domain` before the exponential interpolation; upstream does not.** Apache PDFBox `PDFunctionType2.eval` raises `input[0]` to `/N` directly with no domain clip (verified against 3.0.7 `PDFunctionType2.java:90-104` and the live oracle — domain `[0.2,0.8]`, C0=0/C1=1/N=1, input 0 returns `0.0` not `0.2`; input ∞ returns `∞`; domain `[-2,2]` input 3 returns `3.0`). pypdfbox's `eval` called `self.clip_input(input)` first, producing wrong outputs for any input outside `/Domain` (the gradient sampling case where shadings feed `t` values that have already been mapped through `/Encode` and can legitimately leave `[0,1]`). Fixed to read `input[0]` directly. File: `pypdfbox/pdmodel/common/function/pd_function_type2.py:170`. Four hand-written tests that asserted the old (incorrect) clipping were corrected to the upstream contract (`tests/pdmodel/common/function/test_pd_function_type_2.py`, `test_pd_function_type2_exponent_matrix.py`, `test_pd_function_dispatch_and_clamp.py`, `test_pd_function_type3_partition_semantics.py`). Type 0/3/4 eval already matched upstream (Type 3 *does* clip input to `/Domain`, Type 0 encodes-then-clamps, Type 4 clips input — all confirmed by the oracle).

## Wave 1413 — expand the live oracle to 6 more surfaces (2 real bugs fixed)

6 agents extended the live PDFBox 3.0.7 oracle to filter ENCODE (round-trips), AcroForm field-set + appearance regen, page-tree operations, destination coordinate types, access permissions, and Type0/CID code→CID→GID. Two real bugs fixed (AcroForm appearance regen, CID→GID bound); the other four surfaces matched PDFBox (with two documented intentional divergences). Clean surfaces: **filter encode** (`FilterEncodeProbe` — Flate/LZW/ASCII85/ASCIIHex/RunLength round-trip across the Java↔py boundary both directions; Flate/ASCIIHex/RunLength byte-identical encode; documented: pypdfbox Flate/LZW encode honour a top-level `/Predictor` superset, ASCII85 emits unwrapped digits + `~>`), **page tree** (`PageTreeProbe` — `getNumberOfPages`, `/Kids` traversal order, inherited MediaBox/Resources, and remove/insert round-trips all match across nested/unbalanced trees), **access permissions** (`PermProbe` — all can-* predicates match across a 12-value `/P` sweep + a pypdfbox-encrypt→Java-readback `/P` round-trip; documented: `AccessPermission(-1)` stores `~3` not literal `-1`, predicate-identical).

### Type0 / CID code→CID→GID (1 bug fixed)

Extended the live Apache PDFBox 3.0.7 oracle to the composite-font glyph-resolution pipeline (`pypdfbox/pdmodel/font` Type0 / CID classes). New probe `oracle/probes/CidGidProbe.java` emits, per Type0 font on each page, `code → CID → GID` (via `PDType0Font.codeToCID` + descendant `PDCIDFontType2.codeToGID`) for every code the descendant's `/W` array addresses (Identity-H ⇒ code == CID), plus CID 0 and two synthetic out-of-range CIDs. Differential suite `tests/pdmodel/font/oracle/test_cid_gid_oracle.py` asserts the full triple matches Java across all 6 fixtures that carry a Type0/CIDFontType2 font (Identity ⁠`/CIDToGIDMap` absent, name `/Identity`, and dense `/W`).

- **`PDCIDFontType2.cid_to_gid` — out-of-range CID not clamped to GID 0 (bugfix)**: for an embedded font with an Identity `/CIDToGIDMap` (absent or name `/Identity`), pypdfbox returned the raw CID as the GID *unbounded*, whereas upstream `PDCIDFontType2.codeToGID` (embedded branch, verified against the pinned 3.0.7 bytecode) returns `cid < ttf.getNumberOfGlyphs() ? cid : 0` — a CID at or beyond the embedded program's glyph count resolves to GID 0. Fixed in `pypdfbox/pdmodel/font/pd_cid_font_type2.py` (`cid_to_gid`): the Identity path now bounds the CID against `get_number_of_glyphs()` (with the upstream OTF-with-CFF exception, where CID == GID is returned unbounded). In-range CIDs and stream-mapped CIDs were already correct; only the out-of-range tail diverged. No fixture relied on the old behaviour (5250-line oracle on `unencrypted.pdf` matches byte-for-byte after the fix).
- **fontTools-delegated GID lookup (parity confirmed)**: where `/CIDToGIDMap` is a stream the big-endian `uint16` interpretation already matched; where it is Identity the CID → GID pass-through (now bounded) matches. No CIDFontType0 (CFF) or embedded-stream `/CIDToGIDMap` fixture exists in the corpus, so those cases are covered by the probe's logic but not exercised live; the synthetic out-of-range CIDs exercise the bound on both engines.

### destination coordinate types (parity confirmed, documented divergence)

Extended the live Apache PDFBox 3.0.7 oracle to explicit page-destination **types + coordinates** (`pypdfbox/pdmodel/interactive/documentnavigation/destination`). New probe `oracle/probes/DestTypeProbe.java` builds-free: it walks a PDF's catalog `/Names /Dests` name tree and emits, per entry, the resolved `/D[1]` destination type + the type-appropriate coordinate getters (XYZ left/top/zoom; FitH/FitBH top; FitV/FitBV left; FitR left/bottom/right/top; Fit/FitB no coords). Differential suite `tests/pdmodel/interactive/documentnavigation/destination/oracle/test_destination_type_oracle.py` builds a battery covering every type plus per-coordinate-null and all-null XYZ / null-edge FitR shapes into one saved PDF and asserts pypdfbox's resolved type + coordinates equal Java's byte-for-byte. **All types and null-coordinate handling matched exactly — no coordinate or dispatch bug found.**

- **`/XYZ` `/FitH` `/FitBH` `/FitV` `/FitBV` `/FitR` `/Fit` `/FitB` coordinates — confirmed at parity (no bug)**: pypdfbox's `get_left`/`get_top`/`get_zoom`/`get_bottom`/`get_right` return the same values as PDFBox's `getLeft`/`getTop`/`getZoom`/… for every shape. The established `None` ↔ upstream-`-1` "unset slot" sentinel convention (already documented for the XYZ getters) holds uniformly across all subtypes; the test normalises both to `-1` and they agree.
- **bounding-box destination subtype dispatch — pre-existing intentional divergence (no behavioural impact)**: `PDDestination.create` dispatches `FitB`→`PDPageFitBoundingBoxDestination`, `FitBH`→`PDPageFitBoundingBoxWidthDestination`, `FitBV`→`PDPageFitBoundingBoxHeightDestination` (dedicated pypdfbox subclasses), whereas upstream PDFBox 3.0.7 reuses `PDPageFitDestination`/`PDPageFitWidthDestination`/`PDPageFitHeightDestination` for those three names (verified against the pinned bytecode `PDDestination.create` switch table). The divergence is the concrete *Python class identity* only — the behaviourally-observable `/D[1]` type name and the coordinate getters (top at slot 2 for FitBH, left at slot 2 for FitBV, no coords for FitB) are identical, which the live oracle confirms. No fix warranted: the type-name + coordinate contract is byte-for-byte equal to PDFBox.

### AcroForm field-set + appearance-regen (1 real bug fixed)

Extended the live Apache PDFBox 3.0.7 oracle to AcroForm field **setting + appearance generation** (`pypdfbox/pdmodel/interactive/form`). New probe `oracle/probes/FieldSetProbe.java` has two modes: SET (load an AcroForm PDF, `setValue(value)` each `name=value` argv pair, save) and READ (reload + emit per field `value`, `/AP /N` presence, decoded content-stream token count, and the operator-name sequence via `org.apache.pdfbox.pdfparser.PDFStreamParser`). Differential suite `tests/pdmodel/interactive/form/oracle/test_field_set_appearance_oracle.py` sets the same field value via Java and via pypdfbox `field.set_value(...)` on `AcroFormsBasicFields.pdf` / `MultilineFields.pdf`, saves + reloads both, and asserts identical stored value, identical `/AP /N` presence, and a structurally-equivalent appearance (the canonical `BMC … BT … (text) Tj … ET … EMC` flat-text operator skeleton).

- **`PDTextField` / `PDComboBox` / `PDListBox` `.set_value()` did not regenerate the appearance by default (bugfix)**: pypdfbox's value-field `set_value` defaulted `regenerate_appearance=False`, so after a bare `set_value("…")` the widget carried **no** `/AP /N` normal-appearance stream — viewers without `NeedAppearances` showed an empty field. Upstream `PDTextField.setValue(String)` (and the `PDComboBox` / `PDListBox` overloads) end in `applyChange()`, which calls `constructAppearances()` (regenerating `/AP /N`) **unless** the AcroForm carries `/NeedAppearances true` (verified against the pinned 3.0.7 bytecode). Fixed in `pypdfbox/pdmodel/interactive/form/pd_text_field.py`, `pd_combo_box.py`, `pd_list_box.py`: `regenerate_appearance` now defaults to `None` = follow the upstream gate (regenerate unless `NeedAppearances`); a new `PDTerminalField._should_regenerate_appearance` (`pd_terminal_field.py`) resolves the tri-state (`True`/`False` force on/off, `None` consults `acro_form.is_need_appearances()`). The explicit `regenerate_appearance=False` force-off path is preserved for callers that flatten / re-render externally.
- **`PDCheckBox` / `PDRadioButton` `.set_value()` left at force-off default (intentional, documented)**: the base `PDButton.set_value` already performs the value-visible appearance step for buttons — it syncs each widget's `/AS` to the matching *existing* `/AP /N` on-state (or `/Off`), which is exactly what upstream `PDCheckBox.setValue` / `PDRadioButton.setValue` do (real button widgets ship their on/off appearance streams; setting the value only flips `/AS`). Re-running the appearance *generator* after a button set_value would rebuild the `/AP /N` subdictionary from scratch and discard producer-chosen state keys (e.g. the numeric `/Opt`-indexed keys in PDFBOX-3656, which `get_selected_index` reads), so button redraw stays opt-in (`regenerate_appearance=True`).
- **appearance content-stream formatting (legitimate documented difference)**: both implementations emit the canonical flat-text frame, but pypdfbox writes the black non-stroking colour as `0 g` where Java emits `cs <name> sc` (explicit DeviceGray colour-space + `sc`), and Java's auto line-wrap can split a multi-line value into a different number of `Td (line) Tj` pairs than pypdfbox's wrap heuristic. The differential suite asserts the structural `BMC/BT/Tj/ET/EMC` operator skeleton + that the set text appears in the `( … ) Tj` operand, tolerating the colour-operator and wrap-count differences. No byte/token-exact appearance parity is claimed.

## Wave 1412 — expand the live oracle to 6 more surfaces (4 real bugs fixed)

Extended the live Apache PDFBox 3.0.7 oracle (6 agents) to stream filters, color-space→RGB, ToUnicode/CMap mapping, content-stream generation, actions, and font descriptors. Four real bugs fixed; color spaces + content-stream generation confirmed at parity (or documented-intentional divergence).

- **filters — ASCII85 / ASCIIHex decode (2 bugfixes)**: `FilterDecodeProbe` decodes raw bytes via PDFBox's `FilterFactory`; pypdfbox matched byte-for-byte on Flate (incl. PNG/TIFF predictors), LZW, and RunLength, but two decoders were over-strict vs upstream. (1) `pypdfbox/filter/ascii85_decode.py` rejected input PDFBox accepts — re-implemented `_decode_bytes` to mirror `ASCII85InputStream`: whitespace is LF/CR/SPACE only, digits `!`..`~` with 32-bit overflow masking, `z` is the 4-zero shortcut only at a group boundary, a lone trailing digit is dropped (not rejected). (2) `pypdfbox/filter/ascii_hex_decode.py` re-implemented to mirror `ASCIIHexFilter`: whitespace skipped only before the first nibble of a pair, invalid hex chars feed `REVERSE_HEX`'s `-1` into the byte arithmetic instead of raising. 6 value-based tests that had baked in the stricter (wrong) behaviour were corrected.
- **ToUnicode — MacRoman `nbspace` (bugfix)**: `ToUniMapProbe` (per-font code→Unicode over 6 fixtures) caught `BidiSample.pdf` font `TT3` code 202 returning `None` where PDFBox returns `U+00A0`. `pypdfbox/pdmodel/font/encoding/mac_roman_encoding.py` was missing the upstream PDFBOX-1611 override `add(0o312, "nbspace")`; added (one line, upstream-faithful). CMap layer was already correct.
- **PDFDocEncoding — soft hyphen `0xAD` (bugfix)**: the actions oracle (`ActionProbe`) surfaced it via a GoTo named-destination. `pypdfbox/pdmodel/common/pdfdoc_encoding.py` initialised the 256-entry decode table to `U+FFFD`; byte `0xAD` (unmapped by PDFDocEncoding) must decode to `U+0000` (upstream's `int[]` default + `(char)` cast), not `U+FFFD`. Changed the fill default; the two explicitly-undefined slots (`0x7F`, `0x9F`) stay `U+FFFD` (upstream-faithful).
- **font descriptor — Standard-14 synthesis (bugfix)**: `FontDescProbe` compares every `PDFontDescriptor` metric. Embedded TrueType/Type1C/Type0 descriptors matched, but the Standard-14 *synthesized* descriptor was missing `/FontBBox`/`/Ascent`/`/Descent`/`/CapHeight`/`/XHeight`. `pypdfbox/pdmodel/font/pd_type1_font_embedder.py::build_font_descriptor_from_metrics` called non-existent AFM accessors (`get_font_bbox` vs `get_font_b_box` returning a `BoundingBox`; vertical metrics live on `get_font_metrics_object()`) — the wrong names raised into a swallowing `try/except`, zeroing the metrics. Fixed the accessor names + bbox normalisation; `pd_font_descriptor.py` itself was already correct.
- **color spaces → RGB (parity / documented divergence, no bug)**: `ColorSpaceProbe` across DeviceGray/RGB/CMYK, CalGray/CalRGB, Lab, Indexed, Separation (Type-2 + Type-4 PS), DeviceN. DeviceGray/RGB/CalGray/Indexed/Separation-via-Gray match byte-for-byte; DeviceCMYK/CalRGB/Lab/Separation+DeviceN-via-CMYK diverge **by design** (deltas 21–34/255, not rounding) — PDFBox routes through the JVM CMM (CGATS001 ICC / AWT D50 PCS) while pypdfbox uses platform-deterministic explicit math (subtractive CMYK + IEC 61966-2-1 D65 matrix, chosen waves 1330C/1386). pypdfbox outputs pinned as regression guards.
- **content-stream generation (parity confirmed, no bug)**: `ContentGenProbe` — pypdfbox's `PDPageContentStream` emits the identical operator/operand stream to PDFBox for a fixed text+graphics+state drawing sequence (only the auto-allocated font resource key `/F0` vs `/F1` is normalised).

## Wave 1411 — expand the live oracle to 6 more surfaces (1 real signature bug fixed)

Extended the live Apache PDFBox 3.0.7 oracle (6 agents) to digital signatures (cross-library), document outline/destinations, optional content (OCG/layers), the tagged-PDF logical structure tree, embedded files + name trees, and document metadata/page-labels/XMP. One real interop bug fixed (signatures); the other five surfaces matched Apache PDFBox exactly (standing differential regression suites added).

- **digital signatures — BER indefinite-length CMS (real interop bugfix)**: Apache PDFBox's default signer (BouncyCastle `CMSSignedDataGenerator`) emits the detached `SignedData` in **BER indefinite-length** form (`30 80 … 00 00`), which the DER-only signature parser mishandled — so a valid Java-signed PDF failed `PDSignature.verify` with "Unable to parse PKCS7 data" and full signature math was silently skipped (`is_valid=False`). Made the parser BER-aware: `sig_utils.strip_signature_padding` now bounds indefinite-length blobs via a new `_ber_tlv_end` (the EOC `00 00` octets are otherwise indistinguishable from `/Contents` placeholder padding); `pd_signature.py` gains `_scan_ber_body_len` + `_tlv_sibling_start` and teaches `_read_der_tlv` / `_walk_signer_info` the indefinite-length form; and `verify` suppresses PyCA's BER-fallback `UserWarning` so strict (`-W error`) suites don't spuriously fail. Cross-library now interoperates both directions (Java-signs→pypdfbox-verifies and pypdfbox-signs→Java-verifies): signer subject/serial, `/ByteRange`, and digest-intact all agree; tamper is detected on both sides. Probes `SignProbe`/`SigInspectProbe`, tests `tests/pdmodel/interactive/digitalsignature/oracle/`.
- **document outline / destinations (parity confirmed, no bug)**: `OutlineProbe` (pre-order title + resolved destination page index) matches across 17 fixtures — string-named `/Dest` via the `/Names/Dests` name tree, `/A` GoTo actions, nested items, and unresolvable targets (`-1`).
- **optional content / OCG (parity confirmed, no bug)**: `OcgProbe` (default config `/Name` + `/BaseState`, per-OCG visibility) matches across base-state ON/OFF/Unchanged, explicit ON/OFF overrides, and the no-`/OCProperties` sentinel. (Representation nuance: PDFBox `BaseState.name()` upper-cases `UNCHANGED` vs pypdfbox's spec spelling `Unchanged`; same resolved visibility — the dump upper-cases the Python side.)
- **tagged-PDF structure tree (parity confirmed, no bug)**: `StructTreeProbe` (pre-order role + `/Alt`/`/ActualText` flags) matches on `PDFA3A.pdf` and a built 3-level tagged doc, including role-map resolution (`Heading→H1`, `Para→P`).
- **embedded files + name trees (parity confirmed, no bug)**: `EmbedFilesProbe` (name, `/F`/`/UF`, decoded length, SHA-1) matches exactly on `attachment.pdf` and a built 2-attachment doc, including a binary payload with NUL bytes.
- **document metadata + page labels + XMP (parity confirmed, no bug)**: `MetaProbe` (info-dict fields with normalised dates, per-page computed labels, raw XMP packet length + SHA-1) matches across 8 fixtures spanning decimal/Roman/lettered/prefixed page-label styles and FlateDecode-compressed XMP.

## Wave 1410 — fix flaky PKCS#7 signature verification (real latent bug)

Root-caused the intermittent signature-verify failure surfaced wave 1409. It was a **real product bug**, not just test flakiness: `PDSignature.verify` (and the signature tests) stripped the `/Contents` placeholder padding with `rstrip(b"\x00")`, but a PKCS#7 DER blob may legitimately **end in `0x00` bytes** — so `rstrip` truncated the blob and `cryptography` then raised "Unable to parse PKCS7 data". Intermittent because it depends on the (random) signing key's blob ending; reproduced deterministically at `PYTHONHASHSEED=7`.

- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/interactive/digitalsignature/sig_utils.py`: new `strip_signature_padding(contents)` slices the blob by the outer DER `SEQUENCE` length (reading the ASN.1 length via the existing `_read_der_length`) — what conforming readers do — and only falls back to `rstrip` when the data isn't a DER `SEQUENCE`. Exported from the package.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/interactive/digitalsignature/pd_signature.py::verify` now uses it instead of `rstrip(b"\x00")`; the five signature tests that hand-rolled the same `rstrip` now use the helper too. Deterministic regression coverage in `tests/pdmodel/interactive/digitalsignature/test_strip_signature_padding_wave1410.py` (blob ending in `0x00`, long-form length, non-SEQUENCE / truncated fallbacks). Verified: the previously-failing `PYTHONHASHSEED=7` full-`tests/pdmodel` run is now green; 60× standalone loop clean.

### Wave 1417 detail — simple-font /Encoding resolution incl. /Differences (1 bug fixed)

Extended the live Apache PDFBox 3.0.7 oracle to simple-font `/Encoding` resolution (`pypdfbox/pdmodel/font/encoding`). New probe `oracle/probes/EncodingDiffProbe.java` emits, for every `PDSimpleFont` on each page **and** in the AcroForm default-resources (where `/Differences`-bearing form fonts live), the resolved encoding class, whether it is a `DictionaryEncoding`, the base-encoding identifier, and the full `code → glyph-name` map for codes 0..255 (`Encoding.getName(int)`). Differential suite `tests/pdmodel/font/oracle/test_encoding_differences_oracle.py` asserts pypdfbox's `font.get_encoding_typed().get_name(code)` map equals Java's across 5 real fixtures whose form fonts use `/Differences` (Helvetica family over StandardEncoding; LucidaGrande TrueType over MacRomanEncoding) plus 4 built fixtures placing a custom `/Differences` array over each of StandardEncoding / WinAnsiEncoding / MacRomanEncoding / MacExpertEncoding.

- **simple-font dictionary-/Encoding base resolution (bugfix)**: `pypdfbox/pdmodel/font/pd_simple_font.py::get_encoding_typed` built a `DictionaryEncoding(font_encoding=raw)` with no symbolic flag, selecting `DictionaryEncoding`'s Type-3 form (base == `None`). For a `/Differences` font with no (valid) `/BaseEncoding` this left every non-overridden code as `.notdef` and lost the StandardEncoding (non-symbolic) / built-in (symbolic) base fallback that upstream `PDSimpleFont.readEncoding` applies. `get_encoding_typed` now mirrors `readEncoding`'s dictionary branch (passes `is_non_symbolic` + the symbolic font's `built_in`), so Helvetica-family form fields over StandardEncoding and the LucidaGrande TrueType field over MacRomanEncoding now produce the exact upstream `code → glyph-name` map. Side effect: a non-symbolic Standard-14 font with a *trivial* `/Differences` (restating the base) is now correctly reported as Standard-14 (oracle-confirmed `isStandard14() == true`); `tests/pdmodel/font/test_pd_font_remaining_wave717.py::test_simple_font_standard14_with_dictionary_encoding_no_base` was updated from the prior bug-pinned `False` expectation, and the non-trivial-difference disqualification (PDFBOX-2372) is asserted alongside. The `encoding/` static tables themselves were already correct. **Documented divergence (cross-module, not fixed):** for a non-embedded Standard-14 ZapfDingbats with no `/Encoding`, upstream `PDType1Font.readEncodingFromFont` builds a `Type1Encoding` from the bundled AFM (mapping codes 128..141 / a89..a96), whereas pypdfbox's `get_encoding_typed` keeps its established "return `None` when `/Encoding` is absent" contract (29 tests pin it; the built-in encoding is surfaced lazily by per-subclass helpers). PDFBox's own static `ZapfDingbatsEncoding` class also returns `.notdef` for 128..141, so the encoding tables are byte-identical — the divergence is purely the AFM-vs-static source `PDType1Font` selects. The differential drops that one built-in ZapfDingbats block from both sides and stays strict everywhere else.

### Adobe Glyph List + Zapf Dingbats `to_unicode` algorithmic synthesis (2 bugs fixed)

New probe `oracle/probes/GlyphListProbe.java` emits `GlyphList.toUnicode(name)` (PDFBox 3.0.x: `org.apache.pdfbox.pdmodel.font.encoding.GlyphList`, via `getAdobeGlyphList()` / `getZapfDingbats()`) for a battery of glyph names (common AGL names, algorithmic `uniXXXX` / `uXXXX`, ligatures, `.notdef`, `name.suffix`, multi-code-point AGL entries, surrogate-area names, unknown names → null). Differential suite `tests/fontbox/encoding/oracle/test_glyph_list_oracle.py` asserts pypdfbox's `to_unicode` equals Java's for every name across both lists (43-name battery × 2 lists + 49 Zapf `aNN` names; 0 mismatches).

- **`to_unicode` suffix-recursion deadlock (latent bugfix)**: `pypdfbox/fontbox/encoding/glyph_list.py::to_unicode` called `_derive` *while holding* the non-reentrant `_cache_lock`, but `_derive` recurses back into `to_unicode` to strip a `foo.suffix` name down to `foo`. When the stripped base was itself unknown (e.g. `g123.alt` → `g123`, not in the AGL), the inner `to_unicode` re-acquired the same `threading.Lock` and **deadlocked the thread permanently**. `to_unicode` now reads the cache under the lock, releases it, computes `_derive` lock-free, then re-acquires only to write the result back — mirroring upstream's lock-free `ConcurrentHashMap` recursion. No behaviour change for resolvable names; previously-hanging suffixed-unknown names (`g123.alt`, `ff.alt`, any `<unknown>.suffix`) now correctly return `None`. This was unreachable by prior tests because none exercised a suffix name with an unmapped base; the live-oracle battery surfaced it.

- **algorithmic `uniXXXX` / `uXXXX` length gating (bugfix)**: `pypdfbox/fontbox/encoding/glyph_list.py::_derive` synthesized any `u`-prefixed name of 5–7 chars (`uXXXX`/`uXXXXX`/`uXXXXXX`), so `u1F600` resolved to U+1F600 and `u01F600` to U+1F600. Upstream `GlyphList.toUnicode` gates strictly on exact name length — a `uni` name must be length 7 (one 4-hex code point) and a `u` name length **5** (one 4-hex code point); it does **not** synthesize longer `u` forms nor multi-code-point `uni…` runs. `_derive` now matches the exact-length form (`len == 7 && uni…` → start 3, `len == 5 && u…` → start 1), and the `_UNI_NAME_RE` used by `is_unicode_lookup` / `get_or_unicode_lookup` was tightened from `u[0-9A-Fa-f]{4,6}` to `u[0-9A-Fa-f]{4}` to match. `u1F600`, `u00041`, `u000041`, `u01F600`, `u110000` and multi-code-point `uni004100420043` now all resolve to `None`, matching the live oracle (which returns null for each). The bug-pinned hand-written tests were corrected: `tests/fontbox/encoding/test_glyph_list_wave287.py` (whole file) and `tests/fontbox/encoding/test_glyph_list_parity.py::test_is_unicode_lookup_short_u_form`.
  upstream: PDFBox 3.0.7 `pdmodel/font/encoding/GlyphList.java` (`toUnicode`, length-7 `uni` / length-5 `u` gating)
  reason: upstream parity — pypdfbox previously over-accepted 5–6-hex `u`-forms the reference never synthesizes; verified against the live oracle. The strict `uniXXXX` (single 4-hex), `name.suffix` → `name` stripping, surrogate-area rejection (`0xD7FF < cp < 0xE000` → null), multi-code-point ligature values (`ff` → U+FB00, `ffi` → U+FB03), and unknown → null behaviours were already byte-identical to upstream.

## Wave 1409 — close deferred items + expand the live oracle (4 surfaces, 4 bugs fixed)

Continued the behavioural-parity campaign (6 agents): closed 2 wave-1408 deferred items, expanded the live PDFBox 3.0.7 oracle to 4 new surfaces (merge/split, encryption interop, annotations/forms, page geometry + image extraction), and fixed 4 real bugs. The font `encode()` error-contract deferred item is held pending user sign-off.

- **parser inline-direct flag parity (bugfix, closes deferred)**: pypdfbox inflated trailer `/Size` ~6× on full save because inline dictionaries/arrays were not flagged direct, so the writer (faithfully) promoted each to a free-standing indirect object. Mirrored upstream's three flag mechanics: `COSArray.__init__` now defaults `set_direct(True)` (upstream `COSArray` ctors lines 53/67/75 — keeps arrays-nested-in-arrays like a CIDFont `/W` table inline; `COSDictionary` keeps `direct=False` and is flagged via the parser); `cos_parser.py` `parse_direct_object`→`parse_cos_dictionary(is_direct=True)` for inline `<<…>>` and flags each inline dict/array value direct (upstream `COSParser.parseDirObject` 1072 / `parseCOSDictionaryNameValuePair` 963 / `PDFStreamParser` 131); the indirect-object body itself is reset not-direct in the loaders (upstream `parseFileObject` 634, `PDFObjectStreamParser` 102/160). `set_direct`/`set_key` restricted to `COSDictionary`/`COSArray` so interned scalar singletons aren't mutated across documents. Result: `/Size` now 0.80–0.96× of Java (was ~6×; unencrypted.pdf 53 vs 56), qpdf-valid, reloads identically, COS-graph oracle still matches. Writer oracle `/Size` bound tightened from a 12× ceiling to a 0.5×–2× band.
- **text CTM/graphics-state (bugfix, closes deferred-CTM)**: the lite `PDFTextStripper` now tracks the CTM via a `q`/`Q`/`cm` graphics-state stack and composes textMatrix×CTM (the text-rendering matrix) to recover device-space glyph origins + effective font size (the `Tf` operand scaled by the matrix), mirroring upstream `PDFStreamEngine.showText`/`TextPosition`; text-space advances (show-text, `Td`/`TD`/`T*`/`'`/`"`/`TJ`-numeric) are carried through the text-matrix scale. Producers that fold the point size into `Tm` with a `1 Tf` and position each line via per-line `cm` now lay out correctly instead of collapsing to one baseline. `BidiSample.pdf` reaches byte-parity (xfail→real pass; `test_bidi.py::test_not_sorted` unskipped); `eu-001` + poems-beads narrowed to documented multi-column/article-thread `xfail`s. Also tightened duplicate-overlap suppression (glyph-width fraction, not `0.25×font_size`) and suppressed a double-space at explicit-space boundaries.
- **encryption cross-library interop (2 bugfixes)**: extended the oracle with `EncryptProbe`/`DecryptProbe` for cross-library encrypt/decrypt round-trips (RC4-40/128, AES-128/256; both directions, user+owner passwords, wrong-password rejection; recovered text byte-compared to plaintext). (1) **Object-stream double-decryption** (`pypdfbox/pdmodel/pd_document.py::decrypt`): per PDF 32000-1 §7.6.2, strings/streams inside an `/ObjStm` are never individually encrypted, but pypdfbox attached a per-object cipher to every stream and parsed members before their container had a handler → `FlateDecode: invalid block type` on every Java-encrypted file, all four algorithms. Fixed using the xref-table object-stream-membership marker (negative offset): attach handlers to containers/direct streams first, materialise members afterward without a cipher, skip members in the string-decrypt pass (mirrors upstream `COSParser#parseObjectDynamically`). (2) **RC4-40 owner password rejected** (`standard_security_handler.py`): Algorithm 3(b)'s 50-round MD5 loop must re-hash only the first `key_len_bytes`; pypdfbox hashed all 16 (no-op at 128-bit, wrong at 40-bit). Truncated per spec on both read + `/O` write paths. Result: full single-hop interop parity. (A decrypt-then-re-encrypt double-hop divergence rooted in `pdfwriter` is documented under Active divergences and pinned strict-`xfail`.)
- **forms (bugfix)**: `PDChoice.get_value_as_string` corrected from a comma-join to upstream's `Arrays.toString` form (`"[]"`, `"[a, c]"`), caught by the `FieldProbe` oracle; 7 value-based test assertions that had baked in the wrong expectation updated.
- **multipdf merge/split (parity confirmed, no bug)**: `MergeProbe`/`SplitProbe` — total/per-page counts, page geometry, split boundaries, and qpdf validity all match Apache PDFBox across 5 merge sets + 7 split cases.
- **page geometry + image extraction (parity confirmed, no bug)**: `PageGeomProbe` (resolved `/MediaBox`/`/CropBox`/`/Rotate` + resource counts) matches exactly across 8 fixtures (all 4 rotation quadrants, inherited page-tree MediaBox, fractional MediaBox); `ImageExtractProbe` (`PDImageXObject` width/height/bpc/colorspace + a 16×16 luminance fingerprint) matches exactly on metadata and within MAD<2 on the decoded raster across Indexed/DeviceRGB/ICCBased images (per-channel colour-conversion rounding only).
- **page boundary boxes + clipping (parity confirmed, no bug — wave 1415)**: `PageBoxProbe` reads the full `PDPage` box surface (`getMediaBox`/`getCropBox`/`getBleedBox`/`getTrimBox`/`getArtBox` + `getUserUnit`) through the public accessors so each line exercises upstream's default+clip+inheritable logic. `pypdfbox/pdmodel/pd_page.py` matches Apache PDFBox byte-for-byte across 5 programmatically-built fixtures: only-MediaBox (all boxes fall back), CropBox oversized on every side (clips to MediaBox; Bleed/Trim/Art inherit the clipped crop), explicit Bleed/Trim/Art with one oversized (oversized clips to MediaBox, others unchanged), `/UserUnit` 2.5, and an inherited-MediaBox page tree (MediaBox on the intermediate `/Pages` node). Confirms `clip_to_media_box` = max(media.ll, box.ll)/min(media.ur, box.ur) and the non-inheritable Bleed/Trim/Art → CropBox fallback exactly match upstream.

## Wave 1408 — live Java PDFBox differential oracle + behavioural parity (6 real bugs fixed)

Stood up a **live Apache PDFBox 3.0.7 differential oracle** and used it across 6
behavioural surfaces (6 parallel agents). Unlike value-based parity tests (which
assert against expected values we translated from upstream by hand, so they
can't catch a divergence we also got wrong in translation), the oracle runs the
*same input* through real Java PDFBox and pypdfbox and compares — and it
immediately found genuine bugs that had been masked behind 100% coverage.

Infrastructure (committed): `oracle/download_jars.sh` fetches the Apache-2.0
`pdfbox-app-3.0.7.jar` (gitignored, sha256-pinned; a test-only oracle tool like
qpdf, never a runtime dep); `tests/oracle/harness.py` compiles small Java
"probe" programs (`oracle/probes/*.java`) against the jar and runs them, with a
`@requires_oracle` marker that skips when java/the jar is absent so the suite
stays green on machines without Java.

- **COS-graph fidelity (bugfix)**: `CosDumpProbe` emits a canonical structural fingerprint (per-indirect-object type tags, sorted dict keys, refs unfollowed, float32 bit patterns, stream raw lengths) and pypdfbox reproduces it across 12 fixtures (traditional xref, object/xref streams, linearized, PDF/A, missing-catalog recovery).

- **pdfparser (bugfix)**: `pypdfbox/pdfparser/pdf_parser.py::populate_document` now copies the consolidated byte-offset map into `COSDocument` via `add_xref_table(...)` (positive value = file offset; negative = `-objstm_object_number` for compressed objects), mirroring upstream `COSParser`'s `document.addXRefTable(...)`. Previously the parser populated the object pool but left `COSDocument.get_xref_table()` empty after a load — diverging from Java PDFBox, where the same accessor returns every parsed object. Found by the COS-graph live oracle (every fixture's pypdfbox dump was empty because the dump walks the xref table). No behaviour change for callers that only used the lazy object pool.
- **pdfwriter (bugfix)**: `pypdfbox/pdfwriter/cos_writer.py::_do_write_trailer` now strips the cross-reference-*stream*-only keys (`/Type /XRef`, `/W`, `/Index`, `/Filter`, `/Length`, `/DecodeParms`) from the trailer dictionary before emitting a classic `trailer` keyword block. When a source document used an xref stream, its trailer COSDictionary *is* that stream's dictionary and carried those keys; pypdfbox's default full save writes a classic `xref` table, so the keys were leaking into the classic trailer — a structurally malformed file (PDF 32000-1 §7.5.5 confines the permitted trailer entries; §7.5.8 confines those keys to the xref *stream* dictionary). qpdf recovered via the table but flagged it; strict readers could choke. Found by the writer live-oracle (`SaveRoundTripProbe`) comparing pypdfbox's re-save against Apache PDFBox 3.0.7's on a spread of fixtures (simple / AcroForm / attachment / multipage / rotated / page-tree / outline). After the fix every fixture re-saves to a `qpdf --check`-clean classic-table file. Regression: `tests/pdfwriter/test_classic_trailer_strips_xref_stream_keys_wave1408.py` (oracle-free) + `tests/pdfwriter/oracle/test_save_round_trip_oracle.py` (differential).
- **pdfwriter (validated, documented divergence)**: full-save xref strategy. PDFBox 3.0.7 re-saves PDF 1.5+ documents using a cross-reference *stream*; pypdfbox's default full save emits a classic `xref` *table*. Both are spec-valid; the writer-surface oracle asserts each side emits exactly one coherent xref style and that both pass `qpdf --check`. Incremental save (`save_incremental`) is append-only on both sides — the output begins with the source bytes verbatim (existing objects are not rewritten) and carries an appended xref linked via `/Prev`; verified against PDFBox's `saveIncremental` (`SaveIncrementalProbe`).
- **text extraction (2 bugfixes)**: (1) `pypdfbox/text/pdf_text_stripper.py` defaulted `paragraph_end` to `"\n"` where upstream defaults `""`; combined with the separately-emitted line separator, every detected paragraph break produced a spurious blank line (`with_outline.pdf`: 19 lines vs Java's 15). Default corrected to `""`; output now byte-identical to the Java oracle. (2) `pypdfbox/text/pdf_text_stripper_by_area.py` dropped the trailing line separator that upstream's region writer always emits for a non-empty region; now appended. Three further divergences (BiDi `BidiSample`, `eu-001`, poems-beads) trace to the lite stripper's flat text-state machine ignoring the page CTM / `cm` operator — a **content-stream-engine** limitation outside the text module — and are pinned as strict `xfail` with the cross-module root cause noted (see `DEFERRED.md`).
- **rendering (2 bugfixes)**: `RenderProbe` emits an AA-robust fingerprint (exact pixel dimensions + a 16×16 luminance grid) so structural/perceptual parity is checked with tolerance (pixel-exact is unachievable — Pillow/skia vs Java2D AWT). It caught two real bugs in `pypdfbox/rendering/pdf_renderer.py`: (1) page `/Rotate` (90°/270°) was ignored during rasterisation — rotated pages rendered at the un-swapped mediabox size with content unrotated; now the rendered width/height swap and a rotation transform is composed into the device CTM (matching upstream `PDFRenderer.renderImage`). (2) Rendered pixel dimensions rounded half-up instead of truncating (upstream `(int)` cast == floor) — an 841.89 pt page at 72 DPI is now 841 px, not 842. Correct renders measure MAD ≤ 2.3 / MAXDIFF ≤ 14 against the oracle; the gate (MAD<6 / MAXDIFF<60) sits well above the AA ceiling and below any gross-failure floor (a blank render measures MAD>10).
- **content-stream tokenization (parity confirmed, no bug)**: `TokenizeProbe` emits a canonical operator/operand token stream; pypdfbox's `PDFStreamParser` matches PDFBox 3.0.7 exactly across 10 page fixtures + 2 raw inline-image streams, including the `BI`/`ID`/`EI` inline-image fold (image bytes carried by `BI`, no standalone `ID`/`EI` tokens — SHA-1 byte-parity, including the embedded-`EI` lookahead heuristic). The only difference was benign float rendering (pypdfbox widens float32→float64), normalised in the test dump (shortest round-tripping float32 string) to mirror Java `Float.toString`.
