- **font metrics (parity confirmed, no bug; one documented divergence)**: `FontMetricsProbe` compares per-code advance widths (codes 32–126), `/Subtype`, and `isEmbedded`. Every per-code width matches Apache PDFBox exactly across Standard-14 (AFM-driven Helvetica/Times/Arial), embedded Type1C/CFF, TrueType subsets, and Type0/CIDFontType2. The only divergence: pypdfbox's lenient `encode(str)` substitutes `?`/CID 0 for glyphs absent from a subset font (pinned by existing tests), so `get_string_width` returns a number where PDFBox's `getStringWidth` raises `IllegalArgumentException`. Reversing this is a cross-module encode-contract change touching writer/appearance/render callers — deferred (see `DEFERRED.md`).

## Wave 1407 — parity-surface round-out, round 2 (close deferred items + deep inner-class audit)

Second parity-completion wave (6 agents). Closed both wave-1406 deferred items, ported 2 genuine fontbox misses found by a deeper audit that enumerated **every** Java type declaration (not just one primary class per file — 977 types across pdmodel / fontbox+text / core / rendering+xmpbox+tools), and fixed one latent bug. The audit confirms the rest of the surface is at full type-level parity; remaining unmatched Java types are documented Java-only plumbing (visitor/builder internals, AWT/Java2D helpers, annotation interfaces realized as class attributes) or fontTools/Pillow-delegated decode internals.

- **encryption**: renamed `PDInvalidPasswordException` → `InvalidPasswordException` to match the exact upstream class name, closing the PD-prefix deviation. Moved to its own module `invalid_password_exception.py` (one-class-per-file, mirroring upstream); base class unchanged (`OSError`), no alias retained, all ~30 references across pypdfbox + tests updated.
- **xmpbox/xml**: `XmpSerializer.serialize`/`save` now raise `XmpSerializationException` (chaining the original cause) when DOM rendering or the output-stream write fails, instead of letting a bare `OSError`/`ValueError`/`TypeError` propagate — the Python analogue of upstream `save(...) throws TransformerException`. Closes the wave-1406 deferred item (the ported exception now has a producer).
- **fontbox/encoding**: ported `BuiltInEncoding` (`fontbox/encoding/BuiltInEncoding.java`) — a real public `Encoding` subclass distinct from the already-ported `pdmodel.font.encoding.BuiltInEncoding`, previously folded into a dict representation.
- **fontbox/ttf**: ported `OTLTable` (OpenType-Layout placeholder, `extends TTFTable`, `TAG="JSTF"`); `OTFParser.read_table` now returns typed `OTLTable`/`CFFTable` placeholders mirroring the upstream `readTable` switch (BASE/GDEF/GPOS/GSUB/JSTF → `OTLTable`) instead of a generic tag-stamped `TTFTable`. Observable behaviour unchanged — the real GSUB projection still comes from `TrueTypeFont.get_gsub` via fontTools.
- **type4 function (bugfix)**: the `Operators` registry's class-name map pointed `"true"`/`"false"` at non-existent `True`/`False` classes (Python keyword collision; the ported classes are `TrueFunc`/`FalseFunc`), silently falling back to the internal legacy adapter. Fixed the map; `get_operator("true"/"false")` now returns the dedicated operator classes. Functionally equivalent before/after (the adapter delegated correctly), but restores the registry's intent.

## Wave 1406 — parity-surface round-out (15 genuinely-unported PDFBox classes ported)

First wave of the parity-completion campaign (target redefined: "done" = full PDFBox port + identical behaviour, not internal coverage %). An API-surface audit against the pinned upstream commit `a71c5679` (1057 `src/main` classes) found a small genuine tail of unported classes behind the ~100% coverage number. 15 closed this wave across 5 disjoint module clusters; several audit hits were false positives (already ported under restructured names — Type-4 PostScript operators, shading contexts, `InvalidPasswordException`→`PDInvalidPasswordException`, the `CertificateProccessingException` alias).

- **FDF annotation subtypes** (`pypdfbox/pdmodel/fdf/`): ported `FDFAnnotationHighlight`, `FDFAnnotationSquiggly`, `FDFAnnotationStrikeOut`, `FDFAnnotationUnderline` (all `FDFAnnotationTextMarkup`), `FDFAnnotationSound`, `FDFAnnotationLink`. `FDFAnnotation.create()` factory now dispatches these instead of falling back to the base markup type. `FDFAnnotationLink`: XFDF URI-action init exposed via `init_action_uri(uri)` (the OnActivation/Action/URI DOM walk lives in the XFDF parser layer, matching the repo's existing `init_*` attribute-handler pattern); GoTo destinations remain unhandled, same as upstream.
- **Restored two collapsed abstract bases** (CLAUDE.md hard rule "do not collapse hierarchies"): `PDSpecialColorSpace` (between `PDColorSpace` and `PDSeparation`/`PDDeviceN`/`PDIndexed`/`PDPattern`) and `DecryptionMaterial` (parent of `StandardDecryptionMaterial`/`PublicKeyDecryptionMaterial`). Both are empty markers upstream, so re-parenting is behaviour-neutral; existing suites unchanged.
- **`StandardStructureTypes`** (`pdmodel/documentinterchange/taggedpdf/`): the 49 standard structure-type constants existed only as a private frozenset inside `pd_structure_element.py`; now a proper non-instantiable holder class (`__init__` raises `TypeError`), `types` list built from the declared constants at class-definition time rather than via Java reflection. Upstream odd-spelling `Figure` constant preserved.
- **`DeviceSettingsType` / `FlashType`** (`xmpbox/type/`): ported as structured XMP types; upstream `@StructuredType`/`@PropertyType` annotations realized as `NAMESPACE`/`PREFERRED_PREFIX` class attributes + `_FIELD_TYPES` dict (the project-wide `AbstractStructuredType` convention; the Java `StructuredType` annotation has no standalone Python equivalent — deliberately not a separate class).
- **`DamagedFontException`** (`fontbox/type1/`): ported as `OSError` subclass (upstream extends `IOException`), matching the sibling `OSError` raises in the Type1 parser.
- **xmpbox**: `XMPPageTextSchema` (double-P; a typo'd single-P `XMPageTextSchema` variant predated it under a name absent upstream), `XmpConstants` (non-instantiable class re-exporting the existing module-level constants in `xmp_metadata.py` as single source of truth), `XmpSerializationException` (now a proper `Exception` subclass — compatibility surface; `XmpSerializer.save` still raises `RuntimeError` internally, wiring deferred — see `DEFERRED.md`).

## Wave 1405 — malformed-input robustness pass, round 2 (font parsers + content stream + XML; 3 fixes)

Extended the wave-1404 fuzz harness to the remaining untrusted-input surfaces: TTF / CFF / Type1 / CMap font parsers, the content-stream tokenizer (`PDFStreamParser`), and XFDF/XML (including billion-laughs entity expansion + XXE). TTF / Type1 / CMap / content-stream parsing all came back clean (graceful on every input). Three fixes, each with a regression test; full suite green (+10 tests), 100% line + branch coverage held. None are upstream divergences — each restores intended parity.

- `pypdfbox/util/xml_util.py`: the DOCTYPE guard scanned only the first 2048 bytes, so a large leading comment could push `<!DOCTYPE` past the window and bypass it — reaching the stdlib `minidom`/expat fallback (`defusedxml` is not a dependency), which expands internal entities (billion-laughs DoS). New shared `contains_doctype(data)` helper scans the whole buffer (case-insensitive); `XMLUtil.parse` rejects any DOCTYPE with `OSError`. Matches upstream's hardened `DocumentBuilderFactory` (DTDs disabled).
- `pypdfbox/xmpbox/dom_xmp_parser.py`: `parse` handed packet bytes straight to `ET.fromstring` (expat) with **no** DTD guard — the most-exposed XML surface, since XMP metadata is parsed on nearly any PDF. Now rejects any DOCTYPE (ISO 16684-1 §7.3.2 forbids it in an XMP packet) with `XmpParsingException` before parsing.
- `pypdfbox/fontbox/cff/cff_parser.py`: `parse` delegates the CFF binary decode to fontTools (library-first), which validates with bare `assert` (e.g. `assert offSize <= 4`) and can raise struct/index/key errors on malformed data. A raw `AssertionError` surprised callers catching `OSError`, and `python -O` strips `assert` entirely. The delegated decode + per-font construction is now wrapped so fontTools failures become `OSError` (mirroring upstream `CFFParser`'s `IOException`); the parser's own intentional `OSError` raises pass through. CFF is embedded in PDFs (Type1C / CIDFontType0C via `/FontFile3`).

## Wave 1404 — malformed-input robustness pass (3 hostile-input fixes; coverage held at 100%)

Driven by a stdlib-only fuzz harness (mutation-fuzzing of valid fixtures through `Loader.load_pdf_from_bytes` + random-byte fuzzing of every `*Decode` filter + hand-crafted adversarial structures), all under SIGALRM timeouts to surface hangs. 30,000+ filter iterations and 12,000 mutated-PDF parses showed **no hangs, no recursion/memory blowups** in the filters or parser beyond the items below. Three contract leaks fixed (each with a regression test; full suite 46,607 passed, 100% line + branch coverage held):

- `pypdfbox/cos/cos_stream.py::create_input_stream`: an unknown / corrupted `/Filter` name now raises `OSError("Invalid filter: ...")` instead of leaking the filter registry's `KeyError`. **Restores upstream parity** — `FilterFactory.getFilter` throws `IOException` for an invalid filter; this is a fix toward upstream, not a divergence. (`FilterFactory.get` keeps its documented `KeyError` contract; the conversion happens at the decode boundary.)
- `pypdfbox/pdfparser/base_parser.py::parse_dir_object`: deep-nesting `RecursionError` → `PDFParseError` (see Active divergences).
- `pypdfbox/pdfparser/base_parser.py::parse_cos_number`: overlong-integer `ValueError` → `PDFParseError` (see Active divergences).

## Wave 1400 — audit + remove wave-1397 `# pragma: no branch` markers on `rendering/pdf_renderer.py` (16 → 2)

Wave 1397 (Agent A) closed `rendering/pdf_renderer.py` to 100% branch coverage but reached for `# pragma: no branch` on 16 conditionals. Wave 1399 sibling agents on adjacent files closed comparable work with only 2 pragmas total, exposing 1397's batch as over-pragmatised relative to project policy ("no-pragma by default"). Wave 1400 audits all 16, retains the 2 genuinely unreachable ones (with verified reason comments), and replaces the remaining 14 with behavioural tests in `tests/rendering/test_pdf_renderer_pragma_removal_wave1400.py`.

Pragmas retained (2):

- Line 757 — `if scale > 1.0` inside `_calc_patch_level`: mathematically guaranteed by the outer `0.0 < smoothness < 0.1` guard (`scale = 0.1 / smoothness > 1.0` before clamping, and the clamp ceiling 16.0 is also > 1.0).
- Line 2987 — `elif stroke or fill` inside `_paint`: a `return` at line 2945 already filters out the `not (stroke or fill)` case (PDF `n` operator), so by the time control reaches the `elif` at least one of stroke/fill is True.

Pragmas removed + behavioural test added (14):

- Line 1275 (`_render_page_into` finalizer flush): `self._draw` is None when the content stream / annotation render dropped it. Test `test_render_page_into_finalizer_handles_none_draw` monkeypatches `process_page` to drop the draw.
- Line 2853 (`_op_close_path` first-element-is-M guard): malformed subpath whose first element is not a moveto. Test `test_op_close_path_non_moveto_first_element_keeps_current_point` hand-crafts the malformed state and checks `_current_point` stays put.
- Line 3049 (`_paint_through_clip` inner layer flush): `_draw_via_aggdraw` (e.g. PIL even-odd detour) cleared `self._draw`. Test stubs `_draw_via_aggdraw` to set None.
- Line 3642 (`_render_tiling_cell` flush after `_process_form_bytes`): pattern content stream cleared the draw. Test stubs `_process_form_bytes`.
- Line 4026 (`_paint_radial_shading` pre-paste flush): `self._draw = None` pre-call exercises the False arm; the helper re-binds aggdraw on the new image after paste.
- Line 4191 (`_paint_function_shading` pre-paste flush): symmetric to radial.
- Line 4359 (`_paint_patch_mesh_shading` pre-paste flush): test stubs `_rasterise_single_patch` so the helper reaches the flush guard without needing a real decoded patch stream.
- Line 5751 (`_render_soft_mask_alpha` mid-try flush): `_render_form_xobject` cleared the draw mid-render. Test builds a real `PDSoftMask` so the `isinstance` check passes.
- Line 5953 (`_render_transparency_group` finally flush): same `_render_form_xobject` clear, finally-block path.
- Line 6012 (`_restore_knockout_snapshot` pre-paste flush): `self._draw = None` exercises the False arm directly.
- Line 6754 (`_maybe_end_text_knockout` sub-canvas flush): TK sub-canvas's draw cleared mid-composite.
- Line 7340 (`_draw_glyph` Type 1 path None guard): `_build_aggdraw_path_from_commands` returns None when commands list contains only a moveto. Test stubs `_fill_aggdraw_path` to verify it was NOT called.
- Line 7375 (`_draw_glyph` fallback `upgraded > 0.0` guard): substitute font's `get_width` returns 0 → fallback returns `default_units` (0.0) → guard's False arm leaves the original advance untouched.
- Line 7383 (`_draw_glyph` placeholder-box `self._draw not None` guard): `self._draw = None` exercises the False arm; test asserts `_draw_placeholder_box` not called.

Pragmas added (2, mathematically unreachable):

- `pypdfbox/pdfparser/pdf_xref_stream.py:168` (`elif first + length < num`): the implicit else (`first+length > num`) is unreachable because `sorted(unique-set)` guarantees strict monotonic growth, so `first+length <= num` at every iteration.
- `pypdfbox/pdfparser/pdf_xref_stream.py:173` (`if first is not None and length is not None`): `obj_numbers` is always seeded with `{0}`, so the first iteration always assigns `first = 0; length = 1` and the post-loop guard is always True.

Notes:

- All 32 partials closed with behavioural tests — no pragmas needed.
- A few branches were unreachable through the public split() pipeline
  (e.g. ``source_annots_array`` is None requires source-page and
  imported-page diverge in ways the deep-copy import doesn't allow);
  these are exercised by direct calls to the private helpers
  (`_process_annotations`, `_finalize_annotation_links`,
  `_remove_possible_orphan_annotation`, `_k_create_clone`,
  `_scrub_acroform`) with controlled COS fixtures. The helpers are
  underscored but public-by-convention (upstream PDFBox marks them
  ``protected``), so this is parity-safe.

`pypdfbox.xmpbox` 100% line + 100% branch, `pypdfbox.multipdf` 100%
line + 100% branch (1,108 / 1,108 branches; 7,525 + 2,763 + 1,969 =

mark mathematically unreachable arms exposed by upstream's defensive
guards:

1. `pd_free_text_appearance_handler.py:118` — `if has_stroke:` False
   arm. `extract_non_stroking_color` always returns a non-None list,
   and line 103 (`text_components = list(stroke_components)`) would
   raise `TypeError` before the guard could ever evaluate False.
2. `pd_text_appearance_handler.py:143` — `if painter is not None:` False
   arm. `_SUPPORTED_NAMES` and the dispatch dict carry the same 16 keys,
   so once line 113's membership check passes, `dispatch.get(name)`
   always returns a callable.

## Wave 1398 — branch coverage round-out (622 → 560 partial branches across 30+ files)

Continuation of wave 1397's mid-tier branch closure. After wave 1397

two-pronged approach:

1. **Behavioural tests** (`tests/coverage_boost/test_wave1398_branch_round_out.py`,
   27 new tests, all passing) targeting the most reachable False-arms:
   - `annotation_border.py` 38->42 + 44->55 (legacy /Border array <3
     elements / non-array dash slot).

     entries in PDActionNamed).

     resources=None — driven through the bare PDAbstractContentStream).
   - `pd_cid_font.py` 230->232 (no /W2 in read_vertical_displacements).
   - `pd_font.py` 215->214 (non-numeric /Widths entries skipped).
   - `pd_selector_rendition.py` 31->29 + 33->29 (non-dict and
     unwrappable /R entries).
   - `fdf_document.py` 289->293 (close() on a borrowed COSDocument).
   - `sig_utils.py` 146->149 (set_mdp_permission reuses existing /Perms)
     and 110->104 (DocTimeStamp signature does not block DocMDP).
   - `pdf_object_stream_parser.py` 63->66 (parse_object returns None
     for missing object number).
   - `file_system_font_provider.py` 379->372 (unknown suffix skipped).
   - `exif_schema.py` 335->338 (LangAlt without x-default key).
   - `pd_type0_font.py` 1125->1127 (descendant lacks encode_glyph_id,
     fall through to manual big-endian 2-byte encode).
   - `pd_ink_list.py` 30->28 (non-COSArray entries in /InkList).
   - `pd_appearance_characteristics_dictionary.py` 45->47 (duck-typed
     icon holder whose get_cos_object returns a non-stream).
   - `pd_document_security_store.py` 96->94 (non-stream entries skipped).

     /Differences).

     `fdf_dictionary.py` 62->60 (skip non-dict entries in

   - `revisions.py` 129->131 (remove_at when revision slot absent).

2. **Targeted `# pragma: no branch` pragmas** for clearly defensive

## Wave 1398 (cont.) — root-cause two reported test flakes (no teardowns, no pragmas)

Two flakes were reported on the back of waves 1396–1397:

1. **`tests/debugger/signaturepane/test_signature_pane.py::test_parse_pkcs7_certificates_strips_trailing_nul_padding`**
   (and its siblings that share `_make_pkcs7_blob()`) — reported as
   "fails in full suite, passes in isolation; introduced by wave 1396 or
   1397".

   *Root cause*: the test helper `_make_pkcs7_blob()` generated a fresh
   2048-bit RSA key on every call and produced a PKCS#7 SignedData blob
   via `cryptography.hazmat.primitives.serialization.pkcs7`. In ~0.5–1 %
   of invocations the freshly-built blob is rejected by the very same
   library's `pkcs7.load_der_pkcs7_certificates` reader with
   `ValueError: Unable to parse PKCS7 data`. Reproducible standalone
   (7/1000 in tight loops, 1/500 in a different process). The
   "full-suite-only" appearance was a sampling-rate artefact: the bigger
   the suite, the more shots the random fixture gets at producing a bad
   blob. No cross-test pollution; the cryptography Rust binding has an
   intrinsic round-trip bug on a small fraction of freshly-built blobs.

   *Source-side fix* (`tests/debugger/signaturepane/test_signature_pane.py`):
   - `_make_pkcs7_blob()` is now a thin reader over a module-cached
     `_CACHED_PKCS7_BLOB`, built lazily on first call via
     `_build_pkcs7_blob_once()`.
   - `_build_pkcs7_blob_once()` retries the keygen + DER-encode cycle
     until `load_der_pkcs7_certificates(blob)` accepts the round-trip
     (up to 20 attempts; probability of every attempt failing is
     < 10⁻⁴⁰).
   - Side effect: the test module is also ~6× faster (one RSA keygen
     instead of one per test).

2. **`tests/fontbox/ttf/test_ttf_subsetter_round_out_wave1369.py::test_to_bytes_is_deterministic_for_same_input`**
   — reported as a ~50-wave-old flake that wave 1396 Agent C "couldn't
   reproduce" and patched defensively with a function-scoped
   `fresh_liberation_sans` fixture.

   *Root cause*: there was no cross-test pollution to begin with.
   `TTFSubsetter.to_bytes()` calls `TrueTypeFont._read_all_bytes()`,
   which returns the immutable raw byte buffer captured at parse time,
   then builds a **fresh** `ttLib.TTFont` from it. The shared
   `liberation_sans` fixture's lazily-populated `_tt` reader is never
   consulted by `to_bytes()`, so cross-test traffic against the source
   font cannot influence the subset output. The 200-iteration in-process
   stress run shows 0 mismatches. Wave 1396's `fresh_liberation_sans`
   fixture was effectual paranoia patching a flake that did not actually
   exist (or was a transient unrelated to source-font state).

   *Source-side fix* (`tests/fontbox/ttf/test_ttf_subsetter_round_out_wave1369.py`):
   removed the unnecessary `fresh_liberation_sans` fixture; the
   deterministic-bytes test now uses the module-scoped `liberation_sans`
   directly, with an inline comment recording the by-construction
   determinism argument so future readers don't re-add the fixture.

Verification: full suite (`.venv/bin/pytest -q --no-cov`) reports 45,824
passing / 138 skipped / 0 failures after the fixes; the two specifically
flagged tests pass cleanly across multiple repetitions; no other tests
were touched. Diagnostic tooling (`pytest-randomly`) was installed
locally for the bisection sweep and uninstalled before commit;
`pyproject.toml` was not modified.

  garbage-byte / EOF; `_peek_two_bytes` EOF cases; plus existing
  surface like `get_brute_force_parser`, `create_random_access_read_view`,
  `parse_object_stream_object`, `parse_cos_stream`, `get_encryption`,
  `get_access_permission`, `validate_stream_length`, `has_pdf_header`.
  One genuinely-unreachable defensive arm (`if self.position < offset:`
  after `seek(offset - 1)` on `RandomAccessReadBuffer`, which always
  honours seek) is marked `# pragma: no branch` with parity rationale.
- **Branch-coverage delta on the two files**: 41 + 26 = 67 partial
  arrows → 0. Tests added: 158 (77 merger + 81 parser). No new
  dependencies, no production-API changes, no camelCase aliases. Two
  `# pragma: no branch` annotations added with explanatory comments
  pointing to the upstream code they mirror.

## Wave 1396 (cont.) — branch coverage push: 992 → 865 partial branches (-127, 12.8% reduction)

Targeted branch coverage closures across 20 modules. The line-coverage
sweep had already locked in 100% line coverage; this round targets the
"both arms" requirement of `--cov-branch` reporting. Each test exercises
the previously-missed False arm of an `if` / `elif` / `and` / `or`
predicate with deliberately crafted inputs (insufficient operands,
missing dictionary keys, mistyped tokens, absent optional fields) so the
arrow appears in the coverage summary as a "covered both arms" rather
than "False arm missing".

  parametrize expansion) across 24 new `*_branch_wave1396.py` test
  files. No production code changed; no `# pragma: no cover` added; no

  coverage 97.3% → 97.7%. Line coverage stays at 99.996% (5 unreachable

## Wave 1396 — upstream sync from `6b9b255` → `a71c567` (PDFBOX-5660 cleanup batch)

- **Previous upstream SHA**: `6b9b255eb471b384bac3d2d55c4e47f24fac6dac` (wave 1390 sync point).
- **New upstream SHA**: `a71c5679d69bc3fd3ab15e248b69441ee91dca6c` (apache/pdfbox `trunk`, fast-forwarded).
- **New commits inspected**: 3 (all PDFBOX-5660 batch from Tilman Hausherr, Valery Bokov suggestions).
- **Ported**: 1.
  - `1e5bee9` — `rendering/TilingPaint.java`: wrap `drawer.drawTilingPattern(...)` in try/finally so the `Graphics2D` is disposed on exception. Ported to `pypdfbox/rendering/tiling_paint.py::TilingPaint.get_image` — the inner block now uses try/finally with symbolic `del draw, new_pm` cleanup. The Python `ImageDraw.Draw` analogue holds no OS resources (release is symbolic), but the structural parity is preserved so future drawer changes that *do* acquire resources inherit the correct cleanup ordering. 5 new tests in `tests/rendering/test_tiling_paint_wave1396.py` (handled-exception parametrised over `AttributeError`/`TypeError`/`ValueError`, unhandled `RuntimeError` propagation, happy path).
- **Skipped**: 2.
  - `7decf6f` — `pdmodel/PDPage.java`: removed `throws IOException` from `getContents()`, `getContentsForStreamParsing()`, `getContentsForRandomAccess()`. **Java-only**: Python doesn't declare checked exceptions, so the signature change has no Python equivalent. `pypdfbox/pdmodel/pd_page.py` already returns without an `OSError` declaration on these methods.
  - `a71c567` — `pdmodel/PDPage.java`: pre-size `ArrayList<>(streams.size() * 2)` instead of `new ArrayList<>()`. **Java-only**: Python `list()` does not take a capacity hint in the same way (`list.__init__` doesn't pre-allocate by size). The `streams` list-comprehension idiom in `pypdfbox/pdmodel/pd_page.py` is the canonical Python form.
- **No new Python dependencies. No camelCase aliases. No `# noqa` suppressions. No `# pragma: no cover` markers added.**
- **Files touched**: `pypdfbox/rendering/tiling_paint.py`, `tests/rendering/test_tiling_paint_wave1396.py` (new), `PROVENANCE.md` (upstream SHA marker), `CHANGES.md` (this entry).

## Wave 1396 (cont.) — harden `test_to_bytes_is_deterministic_for_same_input` against module-fixture pollution

- **Context.** `tests/fontbox/ttf/test_ttf_subsetter_round_out_wave1369.py::test_to_bytes_is_deterministic_for_same_input` was tagged as a known cross-test flake (passes in isolation, intermittent under full-suite). Investigation across multiple full-suite runs (`-p randomly`, fixed seeds, PYTHONHASHSEED variations, intentional pre-pollution of the shared `liberation_sans` font with `add_compound_references` / `get_gid_map` / `get_new_glyph_id` / `to_bytes` sequences) failed to reproduce a binary-output mismatch — `TTFSubsetter.to_bytes()` is by construction free of cross-instance state (it re-reads the source font's immutable raw bytes via `_read_all_bytes` and builds a fresh `fontTools.ttLib.TTFont` per call, with `recalc_timestamp = False` and `sorted()` over the per-instance unicode / glyph-id sets). The remaining plausible leak vector is the module-scoped `liberation_sans` fixture: every prior test in the module touches the shared `TrueTypeFont._tt` fontTools instance through composite-expansion accessors (`_add_composite_components` invokes `tt["glyf"]` and `glyf[glyph_name]`, lazy-decompiling glyphs into the shared `_tt` cache). The determinism assertion does not consume `_tt`, but isolating the comparison from any future `_tt` mutation a sibling test could introduce removes the entire vector class.
- **Fix.** Added a dedicated function-scoped `fresh_liberation_sans` fixture in `tests/fontbox/ttf/test_ttf_subsetter_round_out_wave1369.py` that parses a *new* `TrueTypeFont` per invocation. The determinism test now consumes the fresh fixture; the other 15 tests in the module continue to share the module-scoped `liberation_sans` (their assertions are state-tolerant). No source-level changes — `TTFSubsetter.to_bytes()` semantics are unchanged, and the determinism guarantee is now anchored to a freshly-parsed font for every test run regardless of sibling-test ordering or future additions to the module.
- **Verification.** `tests/fontbox/ttf/test_ttf_subsetter_round_out_wave1369.py` 16/16 passing in isolation and in the full `tests/fontbox/` (5,071 passed) and full-suite (45,343 passed) runs; `uv run ruff check` clean.
- **No new Python dependencies.** `pytest-randomly` was installed in the venv only as a diagnostic and uninstalled at the end; pyproject is untouched.
- **Files touched**: `tests/fontbox/ttf/test_ttf_subsetter_round_out_wave1369.py`, `CHANGES.md` (this entry).

## Wave 1395 — close wave-1393 leftover coverage in nine `tools/*.py` modules (62 → 0 missing)

- **Context.** Wave 1393 fixed 6 latent `COSDocument`-vs-`PDDocument` bugs in `pypdfbox/tools/` plus a `str`-vs-`ImageType`-enum bug in `pdf_to_image.py`. Each fix introduced new defensive branches (`_open_doc` context-manager helpers detecting the loader return type; `ImageType[name.upper()]` resolution; `_help` / `_Help` / `_debug_class` / `_Debug` adapters; `-page N=FILE` argparse map parsing). The 15 wave-1393 CLI smoke tests in `tests/tools/test_pdfbox_app_cli_wave1393.py` exercise every tool end-to-end, but they shell out via `subprocess.run` so the in-process coverage tracer doesn't see the executed lines. The wave-1394 authoritative refresh accordingly flagged 62 newly-uncovered lines across 9 files.

## Wave 1394 (cont.) — branch-coverage closure on `text/bidi.py` + discrepancy audit between wave-1391 and wave-1392 measurements

- **Discrepancy resolution.** Wave 1391 Agent E reported `pypdfbox/text/bidi.py` closed to 0 missing **statement** lines (90 → 0 with 47 new tests in `tests/text/test_bidi_wave1391.py` + 3 documented `# pragma: no cover` markers on truly unreachable defensive guards). Wave 1392 Agent C's audit then reported "281 missing" lines, which contradicted the on-disk `coverage.json` snapshot. Re-measurement under wave 1394 confirms Wave 1391's report is the accurate one: `coverage.json` carries `pypdfbox/text/bidi.py` at 312 / 312 statements covered (100%, 0 missing) with 8 excluded lines from the wave-1391 pragmas, and a fresh `.venv/bin/python -m coverage run --include='*/pypdfbox/text/bidi.py' -m pytest tests/text/` reproduces the same: **312 statements, 0 missing, 100% line coverage** as of wave 1394 baseline. Wave 1392 Agent C's "281 missing" was either a stale measurement (predating wave 1391 close-out), a misreporting of branch totals (the file has 196 branches; "281" doesn't match any single dimension), or an off-by-one against a different file. No real coverage gap existed at the statement level when wave 1392 ran.
- **Real residual gap found — branch coverage.** Switching to `--branch` revealed `pypdfbox/text/bidi.py` at 99% branch coverage (5 partial branches): `179->181` (LRE/RLE/LRO/RLO encountered while `overflow_isolate > 0` — inner `if overflow_isolate == 0` guard never flipped FALSE), `246->259` (`_fsi_substring_direction` loop falls off the end without finding strong or hitting matching PDI), `353->350` (W2 inner backward-scan iterates past at least one non-strong type without breaking), `405->410` (W7 inner backward-scan similarly walks past non-{L, R} chars), and `461->459` (N1 backward-scan encounters a non-strong type — e.g. BN — and continues to the next iteration). All five were genuinely reachable via behavioural inputs (no `# pragma: no cover` markers needed).
- **Tests added (32 new in `tests/text/test_bidi_wave1394.py`):**
  - 2 branch-targeted: LRE / RLO inside an overflowed-isolate region built by stacking 126 RLIs / LRIs (62 valid frames pushing the level up to 124-125, then 63+ overflow_isolate increments) so the embed-marker hits `overflow_isolate > 0` and falls through line 179 to 181.
  - 2 branch-targeted: bare FSI followed only by whitespace / ON-neutrals with no matching PDI (loop exhausts → return 0 fallthrough at 246->259).
  - 2 branch-targeted: AN-then-EN and ZWSP-then-EN in an LTR paragraph (W2 inner scan iterates past the non-strong type without breaking; EN gets W7-demoted to L by sos == 'L').
  - 2 branch-targeted: same shapes covering W7 inner scan at 405->410.
  - 2 branch-targeted: ZWSP-then-space-then-L and ZWSP-ZWSP-space-L (N1 backward scan iterates past BN — neither strong nor in `_NEUTRAL_TYPES` — at 461->459).
  - 6 behavioural UAX #9 regressions: pure-LTR English keeps all level 0, pure-Hebrew on level 1, pure-Arabic AL on level 1, English-inside-Hebrew nests at level 2, Hebrew-inside-English nests at level 1, Arabic-numerals-inside-Arabic land on level 2.
  - 3 reorder regressions: pure-RTL paragraph reverses end-to-end, pure-LTR stays in logical order, `reorder_runs_visually` reorders a parallel object array consistently.
  - 6 end-to-end `PDFTextStripper.handle_direction` checks: ASCII pass-through, empty-input pass-through, Hebrew word reverses, L4 bracket-mirror with Hebrew context (`(`/`)` round-trip through visual reorder + mirror so they remain a paired open-before-close), LTR word inside RTL paragraph, idempotent on pure-LTR.
  - 5 `get_paragraph_direction` corner cases: empty / first-strong-L / first-strong-R / AL counts as RTL / no-strong falls back to LTR.
  - 1 `_bidi_class` unassigned-codepoint fallback.
  - 1 longer mixed-paragraph smoke test exercising every resolver phase (X-W-N-I-L).
- **Coverage delta.** `pypdfbox/text/bidi.py` branch coverage 99% → **100%** (5 → 0 partial branches). Statement coverage stays at 100% (no regression). No new `# pragma: no cover` markers (the 5 residual branches were behaviourally reachable). ## Wave 1394 (cont.) — standalone-file coverage closure for `text_position.py` (generic-angle `get_*_dir_adj` fallback)

- **Context.** Wave 1392 Agent C flagged two text-module files as having large missing-line counts: `pypdfbox/text/text_position.py` (alleged 130 missing) and `pypdfbox/text/pdf_marked_content_extractor.py` (alleged 115 missing). The wave 1393/1394 full-suite coverage run shows both already at **100% line coverage** — the 130/115 figures came from a focused-tests-only measurement that missed the transitive coverage from `PDFTextStripper`, `PDFMarkedContentExtractor`, and `LegacyPDFStreamEngine` paths. Running coverage with only `tests/text/test_text_position.py` (plus the wave-307 / parity / upstream variants) leaves 4 lines uncovered: the generic-angle (non-cardinal) trigonometric fallback inside `get_x_dir_adj` (lines 361-362) and `get_y_dir_adj` (lines 385-386).
- **Branch analysis.** Both `get_x_dir_adj` and `get_y_dir_adj` short-circuit on the four cardinal page rotations (0 / 90 / 180 / 270) and return a coordinate read or page-extent subtraction. Any other ``dir`` value (e.g. 37, 45, 60, 135) falls through to the generic rotation about the page origin: `x' = x·cos(θ) + y·sin(θ)`, `y' = -x·sin(θ) + y·cos(θ)`. Upstream PDFBox doesn't actually emit these — the production path always picks one of the four cardinals — but the lite port keeps the trig fallback for callers that synthesise rotated text positions in tests or for future non-rectilinear-page support.
- **Tests added (6 new in `tests/text/test_text_position.py`):**
  - `test_get_x_dir_adj_generic_angle_rotates_about_origin` — 45-deg ``dir`` lands on the trig branch; asserts `x·cos+y·sin`.
  - `test_get_x_dir_adj_generic_angle_negative_quadrant` — 135-deg exercises a negative-cosine value.
  - `test_get_x_dir_adj_generic_angle_normalises_modulo_360` — 405 deg (= 45 after `% 360`) still hits the trig path because the cardinal-match runs against the modulo result.
  - `test_get_y_dir_adj_generic_angle_rotates_about_origin` — 45-deg ``dir`` for the y-axis: `-x·sin+y·cos`.
  - `test_get_y_dir_adj_generic_angle_60_deg` — 60 deg exercises a non-degenerate-cos / non-degenerate-sin pair.
  - `test_get_x_dir_adj_and_y_dir_adj_generic_angle_orthogonal` — invariant: rotation preserves L2 norm of (x, y) for any θ.
- **Coverage delta.** `pypdfbox/text/text_position.py` standalone (its own four test files only): 4 → 0 missing = 100%. Full-suite coverage: was already 100% (no change). `pypdfbox/text/pdf_marked_content_extractor.py`: already at 100% standalone — no test additions needed.
- **Files touched:**
  - `tests/text/test_text_position.py` (+6 tests + `import math`)
  - `CHANGES.md` (this entry)

## Wave 1394 — close final missing line in `pdf_text_stripper.py` (`handle_direction` all-LTR post-resolve branch)

- **Context.** Wave 1392 Agent C flagged `pypdfbox/text/pdf_text_stripper.py` as the largest remaining coverage gap (alleged 406 missing lines). The latest pre-wave-1394 `coverage.json` rebuild showed the file was already at 99.89% (951/952 statements covered) — the 406-line estimate was stale, predating the wave-1370 / 1387 / 1391 stripper rounds. Only one statement was uncovered: `pdf_text_stripper.py:1963`, the `if all(level == 0 for level in levels): return word` short-circuit inside `PDFTextStripper.handle_direction`.
- **Branch analysis.** The branch fires when (1) the cheap pre-scan finds at least one character whose `unicodedata.bidirectional` class is in `{R, AL, AN, RLE, RLO, RLI, FSI, LRE, LRO, LRI}` (so the resolver is invoked), but (2) the UAX #9 resolver assigns embedding level 0 to every codepoint (so reordering is a no-op). The minimal reproducer is a word consisting solely of explicit-isolate format characters with no strong-directional content between them — e.g. a bare U+2068 First-Strong Isolate, or a U+2068 + U+2069 pair with empty isolate body. The pre-scan sees FSI (class `FSI`) and proceeds to `BidiResolver`, which returns `[0]` / `[0, 0]` because there is no strong content to embed.
- **Test added.** `tests/text/test_bidi_wave1387.py::test_handle_direction_explicit_iso_chars_resolve_to_all_ltr_unchanged` — passes the bare FSI and the FSI+PDI pair through `PDFTextStripper.handle_direction` and asserts the input is returned verbatim (no reorder, no mirroring).
- **Result.** `pypdfbox/text/pdf_text_stripper.py`: 1 → 0 missing lines (100% statement coverage). No `# pragma: no cover` markers added; the branch is reachable by real input. No source code changed.
- **Files touched:**
  - `tests/text/test_bidi_wave1387.py` (+1 test)
  - `CHANGES.md` (this entry)

  - `CHANGES.md` (this entry)

## Wave 1393 — `pdfbox-app` CLI parity (unified `pdfbox` console script, missing flags, latent loader bugs)

- **Context.** Upstream `pdfbox-app/` is a Maven shading-only module with no Java source — it bundles `pdfbox-tools` into a single executable JAR whose `Main-Class` is `org.apache.pdfbox.tools.PDFBox` (picocli dispatcher). Porting "pdfbox-app" therefore means: (a) confirm every subcommand registered by upstream `PDFBox.java` is reachable through `pypdfbox.tools.pdf_box.PDFBox.main`, (b) audit each subcommand's flag surface against the corresponding `@Option` set in its upstream `*.java` counterpart, and (c) expose the dispatcher as a real console script so `pdfbox <subcmd> …` matches the `java -jar pdfbox-app.jar <subcmd>` muscle memory.
- **Subcommand parity (`pypdfbox/tools/pdf_box.py`).** Added two upstream subcommands that were missing from `_SUBCOMMANDS`: `debug` → `pypdfbox.debugger.pd_debugger.PDFDebugger` (lazy-imported so headless/Tk-less environments can still import the dispatcher) and `help` → built-in `_Help` adapter (mirrors picocli's `CommandLine.HelpCommand`, listing every registered subcommand or printing `<subcmd> --help` on demand). The pre-existing `decompress` extension stays registered.
- **Flag parity audit (8 missing CLI flags wired).** `pypdfbox/tools/encrypt_tool.py::Encrypt.main` was missing argparse wiring for the 8 `AccessPermission` flags upstream documents (`-canAssemble`, `-canExtractContent`, `-canExtractForAccessibility`, `-canFillInForm`, `-canModify`, `-canModifyAnnotations`, `-canPrint`, `-canPrintFaithful`); they exist as `Encrypt` instance attributes but no `add_argument` call previously connected them. Each now accepts a `true`/`false` string (matching picocli's boolean `@Option` rendering, default `true`). `pypdfbox/tools/overlay_pdf.py::OverlayPDF.main` was missing the upstream `-page <N>=<file>` `Map<Integer,String>` option (specific-page overlay file); now parsed as a repeatable `append` argument with `N=FILE` syntax.
- **New console script (`pdfbox`).** `pyproject.toml` `[project.scripts]` now exposes `pdfbox = "pypdfbox.tools.pdf_box:_console_main"` alongside the existing `pypdfbox`. The new thin wrapper calls `sys.exit(PDFBox.main(sys.argv[1:]))`. Both scripts coexist: `pypdfbox` is the argparse dispatcher with pypdfbox-native flat subcommand names; `pdfbox` is the upstream-shaped picocli mirror with colon-namespaced names (`export:text`, `import:fdf`, etc.).
- **Latent loader bugs fixed (6 tool modules).** `extract_text.py`, `extract_xmp.py`, `extract_images.py`, `pdf_split.py`, `pdf_to_image.py`, `decompress_objectstreams.py`, `write_decoded_doc.py` all called `Loader.load_pdf` and then immediately invoked `PDDocument`-level methods (`get_current_access_permission`, `get_document_catalog`, `get_pages`) on the returned object. But `Loader.load_pdf` returns a low-level `COSDocument`, not a `PDDocument` — so every end-to-end CLI invocation crashed with `AttributeError: 'COSDocument' object has no attribute 'get_current_access_permission'`. Each module now defines a tiny module-local `_open_doc` context-manager helper that detects the return type and wraps it in `PDDocument` when needed, while still accepting the `_PDLoaderShim` pattern used by the wave-1314/1315/1319/1323/1345 coverage tests. The `Loader` symbol stays at module scope so the existing test monkey-patches continue to work.
- **`pdf_to_image.py` enum mismatch fixed.** `PDFToImage.call` passed the `-color` string (`"RGB"`) straight to `renderer.render_image_with_dpi(...)`, but the renderer expects an `ImageType` enum. Added an upgrade step that resolves the string to `ImageType[name.upper()]` before the render call (matches upstream picocli's automatic enum conversion).
- **Files touched:**
  - `pypdfbox/tools/pdf_box.py` (added `debug`/`help` subcommands, `_console_main` thin wrapper, lazy `_debug_class` import)
  - `pypdfbox/tools/encrypt_tool.py` (+8 permission flags wired through argparse to `Encrypt` attributes)
  - `pypdfbox/tools/overlay_pdf.py` (+`-page N=FILE` map argument)
  - `pypdfbox/tools/extract_text.py` (+`_open_doc` helper, fixed `Loader.load_pdf` ↔ `PDDocument` mismatch)
  - `pypdfbox/tools/extract_xmp.py` (same)
  - `pypdfbox/tools/extract_images.py` (same)
  - `pypdfbox/tools/pdf_split.py` (same)
  - `pypdfbox/tools/pdf_to_image.py` (`_open_doc` + `ImageType` enum upgrade)
  - `pypdfbox/tools/decompress_objectstreams.py` (`_open_doc`)
  - `pypdfbox/tools/write_decoded_doc.py` (`_open_doc`)
  - `pyproject.toml` (new `pdfbox` console script)
  - `tests/tools/test_pdfbox_app_cli_wave1393.py` (new, 15 end-to-end subprocess tests covering merge / split / export:text / export:xmp / render / decode / decompress / encrypt + decrypt round-trip / version / help / `-canPrint=false` flag / `_console_main` wiring)
- **Parallel-naming duplicates audit.** Confirmed each pair (`extract_text.py`+`extracttext.py`, `encrypt.py`+`encrypt_tool.py`, `image_to_pdf.py`+`imagetopdf.py`, `split.py`+`pdf_split.py`, `merge.py`+`pdf_merger.py`, `decrypt.py`+`decrypt_tool.py`, `text_to_pdf.py`+`texttopdf.py`, `version.py`+`version_tool.py`) is intentional: the lowercase no-suffix module is the argparse-style `build_parser(subparsers)` wrapper used by `cli.py` (`pypdfbox` console script); the underscored / `_tool` / `_to_pdf` module is the upstream `Callable<Integer>` class-shape port used by `pdf_box.py` (`pdfbox` console script). No dead code to remove — both shapes have live importers.
- **Wired subcommands now exposed via `pdfbox`:** debug, decrypt, encrypt, decode, export:images, export:xmp, export:text, export:fdf, export:xfdf, import:fdf, import:xfdf, overlay, print, render, merge, split, fromimage, fromtext, version, help, decompress (21 total = upstream 18 + `debug` + `help` + `decompress` extension).
- **Tests.** 811 / 811 in `tests/tools/` pass (pre-existing 796 + 15 new). Full suite stays green: 45,035 passed / 138 skipped / 0 failures.

## Wave 1392 (cont.) — close residual 185 missing lines in `rendering/pdf_renderer.py` (fixtures + exception paths)

- **Context.** Wave 1391's renderer-cluster pass closed 82 of the 267 missing lines in `pdf_renderer.py` (267 → 185). The remaining 185 lines were concentrated in four real-world clusters that white-box unit tests couldn't reach: patch-mesh shading rasteriser exception paths (lines 4237-4655), inline-image generic per-pixel CS dispatch (6494-6605), text-knockout composite layer rendering (6679-6820), and annotation appearance-stream walking paths (4956-5096). The wave-1391 agent flagged these as needing real-world fixtures.
- **Files closed to 100%:**
  - `pypdfbox/rendering/pdf_renderer.py` (185 → 0 missing). All four clusters covered + the 50+ other small straggler defensive paths the wave-1391 agent left uncovered (ExtGState exception paths, BG/UCR function-create returning None, stencil mask edge cases, inline-image filter dispatch, image XObject decode error handling, soft-mask render-raises path, overprint stroke-only suppression, and the Bezier-flatten subpath helper).
- **New tests (95 in `tests/rendering/test_pdf_renderer_wave1392_coverage.py`):** Cover all four target clusters plus the small straggler defensive paths the wave-1391 agent left uncovered. Includes synthetic patch-mesh shadings whose `/Decode` is too short (triggers `parse_patches` → `ValueError`), a /Function-routed Coons patch (green→red gradient), patch with /Background + /BBox + /AntiAlias, inline images with /CS = `[/CalGray <<dict>>]`, ICCBased / Separation / DeviceN custom CS via stubs, a per-pixel `to_rgb` loop that returns short tuples / None / raises mid-loop, end-to-end text-knockout `_maybe_begin_text_knockout` / `_maybe_end_text_knockout` cycles with both Normal and Multiply blend modes (sub-canvas opaque-black → 50%-gray after half-alpha composite), and 15 annotation widget tests that drive each defensive raise path in `_render_annotation` via a class-level `PDPage.get_annotations` monkey-patch (the `doc.get_pages()` re-wrap loses instance patches, hence the class-level swap with `autouse` teardown).
- **Coverage delta.** `pypdfbox/rendering/pdf_renderer.py` 185 → 0 missing = **185 lines closed**; module-level coverage went from 95.3% to 100.0%. Full rendering suite: 1470 passed / 1 skipped in 22s (up from 1376 / 1 in the wave-1391 baseline; +94 new tests).

  - `_select_script_tag` was the genuine remaining gap. The old comment claimed `OpenTypeScript` constants were "as-yet-unported"; they had shipped at `pypdfbox/fontbox/ttf/open_type_script.py` (`INHERITED = "Inherited"`, `TAG_DEFAULT = "DFLT"`). The implementation also missed the `INHERITED` single-tag branch from upstream `GlyphSubstitutionTable.java:715-745` — a lone `Inherited` tag now correctly falls back to the cached `lastUsedSupportedScript` (or the first script if no cache), matching upstream L720-732. The `TAG_DEFAULT` branch is now keyed on the actual `OpenTypeScript.TAG_DEFAULT` constant rather than a hardcoded `"DFLT"` literal so future constant refactors stay consistent. Lowercase-`"dflt"` tolerance preserved as a pypdfbox-side extension.

## Wave 1391 — `_draw_glyph` text-rendering-matrix order bug (BidiSample / poems-beads white-page regression)

- **Root cause.** `PDFRenderer._draw_glyph` composed the per-glyph CTM in the wrong order. The legacy code was `glyph_to_device = _matmul(self._gs.ctm, _matmul(text_local * Tm, device_ctm))` — i.e. it prefixed the page CTM onto a matrix that already had the device y-flip applied, so any non-pure-translation page-CTM (`cm`) issued *before* the `Tm` font-size matrix landed the painted glyph thousands of pixels off the canvas. Examples: `tests/fixtures/text/BidiSample.pdf` (per-line `q 1 0 0 1 X Y cm BT 14 0 0 14 0 0 Tm /TT2 1 Tf [...] TJ ET Q`) and `tests/fixtures/pdfwriter/PDFBOX-3110-poems-beads.pdf` (same producer pattern from PDFBox's own pdfbox-tools) rendered as 100% white pages because every glyph ended up at e.g. `f = -9962` on an 842-pixel-tall canvas, then was clipped out by the `_paint_glyph_path_through_clip` mask compositor.
- **Fix.** Route through `self._full_ctm()` (which already returns `gs.ctm * device_ctm`) so the composition becomes the spec-correct `text_local * Tm * (gs.ctm * device_ctm)`, matching PDF 32000-1 §9.4.4 ("Trm = TfontSize · Tm · CTM" then device-space mapping). Single-line change in `pypdfbox/rendering/pdf_renderer.py::_draw_glyph` plus an expanded comment block. No behaviour change for renders whose `gs.ctm` is identity inside the BT/ET block (the bulk of synthetic-test PDFs).
- **Coverage.** New `tests/rendering/test_glyph_ctm_wave1391.py` (3 tests): `BidiSample.pdf` page 0 renders ≥0.5% non-white pixels, `poems-beads.pdf` page 0 renders ≥5% non-white pixels, white-box pin on `_draw_glyph` source referencing `self._full_ctm()` and not referencing the legacy `_matmul(self._gs.ctm, glyph_to_device)` two-step. All 1,287 tests under `tests/rendering/` pass after the fix (`uv run ruff check` clean).
- Files touched: `pypdfbox/rendering/pdf_renderer.py` (one matrix composition line + comment), `tests/rendering/test_glyph_ctm_wave1391.py` (new), `CHANGES.md` (this entry).

## Wave 1391 (cont.) — `_render_annotation` matrix-order swap + unembedded Helvetica `/Differences` encoding fall-through (AcroFormsRotation widget appearances)

- **Root cause #1 — matrix-order bug in ``PDFRenderer._render_annotation``.** The historical call `_matmul(a_matrix, m_appear)` means "apply `a_matrix` first, then `m_appear`" — but upstream PDFBox does `Matrix.concatenate(a, matrix)` which is defined as `matrix.multiply(a)` and means "apply `matrix` first, then `a`" (PDFBox `Matrix.java` line 434-437: `concatenate(a, b) → b.multiply(a)`). For widgets with rotated appearances (`/MK /R 90` and `/R 180`) the swapped order ran the translate leg *before* the rotate leg, pushing the painted region hundreds of points off the page (e.g. widget 2 on page 0 of `tests/fixtures/pdmodel/interactive/form/AcroFormsRotation.pdf` mapped bbox corner (0,0) to (-540.9, 182.4) instead of the expected (206.7, 565.3)). Net effect: 12 of 16 widgets on each page rendered as completely blank rectangles. The wave-1390 visual battery flagged the symptom — `AcroFormsRotation.pdf` rendered at 0.78% non-white pixels vs `pdftocairo`'s 4.72% reference.

- **Root cause #2 — base-less `DictionaryEncoding` for unembedded Standard 14 fonts.** `PDSimpleFont.get_encoding_typed()` builds a `DictionaryEncoding(font_encoding=raw)` *without* a base encoding when `/Encoding` is a COSDictionary — that's upstream's Type 3 mode where `/Differences` is the *complete* mapping. For regular Type 1 fonts with `/Differences` (no `/BaseEncoding`) — the shape Acrobat emits for `/Helv` in AcroForm widget appearances — every code outside the differences table drops to `.notdef`. Downstream `PDType1Font.get_glyph_width(116)` then returned 0.0 (and `get_glyph_path` returned `[]`), so the renderer painted nothing for the field-value text inside the widget appearances (e.g. `(acrobat.portrait.single.rotation0) Tj` painted zero glyphs). Upstream's `PDSimpleFont.readEncoding` constructor (called from `PDType1Font(...)` line 282) passes `is_non_symbolic=true` to the encoding constructor so the base resolves to `StandardEncoding`; the Python port's lazy `get_encoding_typed` short-cut omitted that argument.

- **Fix.** Two narrow edits:
  - `pypdfbox/rendering/pdf_renderer.py::_render_annotation` — swap the args: `aa = _matmul(m_appear, a_matrix)`. One executable-line change + expanded comment block.
  - `pypdfbox/pdmodel/font/pd_type1_font.py::get_glyph_width` and `get_glyph_path` — extend the existing Standard 14 fall-through path so when the typed encoding is a base-less `DictionaryEncoding` whose `/Differences` overlay didn't cover `code`, the lookup retries through the family's default PostScript encoding (Symbol / ZapfDingbats / Standard). Reuses the family-default dispatch that already existed for the "no `/Encoding`" branch; the lazy `get_encoding_typed` itself is left untouched (rewriting it would break the existing test `test_simple_font_standard14_false_for_dictionary_encoding_without_base` which pins the base-less behaviour for `is_standard_14`).

- **Coverage.** New `tests/rendering/test_annotation_appearance_wave1391.py` (7 tests): `AcroFormsRotation` page 0 / page 1 each render ≥5% non-white pixels (vs the historical 0.78%), `transitions_test` pages 0/1/2 each paint ≥100 non-white pixels (the PDF intrinsically only carries `(First Page) Tj` etc in Helvetica-Bold 12pt — `pdftocairo` produces 0.06-0.08% non-white too, so the threshold pins that text isn't silently dropped rather than enforcing a meaningless 5% floor), white-box pin that `PDType1Font.get_glyph_width(116)` returns 278.0 on a base-less `/Differences` Helvetica, and white-box pin on `_render_annotation` source referencing `_matmul(m_appear, a_matrix)` and not the legacy `_matmul(a_matrix, m_appear)`.

- **Verification.** Full pytest suite: `44,828 passed, 138 skipped, 37 warnings` after the fix (clean across `tests/rendering/` 1,294 tests + `tests/pdmodel/font/` 4,248 tests). `uv run ruff check --fix && uv run ruff check` clean. AcroFormsRotation pages now render at 5.18% / 5.09% non-white pixels (vs `pdftocairo` 4.72% / 4.86% — within 0.5% of the oracle).

- Files touched: `pypdfbox/rendering/pdf_renderer.py` (one matrix composition line + expanded comment), `pypdfbox/pdmodel/font/pd_type1_font.py` (Standard 14 encoding fall-through in `get_glyph_width` and `get_glyph_path`), `tests/rendering/test_annotation_appearance_wave1391.py` (new), `CHANGES.md` (this entry).

## Wave 1391 (cont.) — `PDTrueTypeFont._code_to_gid` per-platform cmap fallback (poems-beads ".notdef-grid" follow-up)

- **Root cause.** `PDTrueTypeFont._code_to_gid` consulted only `TrueTypeFont.get_unicode_cmap_subtable` (the priority-ordered Unicode subtable picker). Embedded TrueType subsets that ship only a (1,0) Mac-Roman cmap — for example the QuarkXPress-era `QXCTPF+Helvetica` / `DOPBHD+Helvetica-Oblique` subsets in `tests/fixtures/pdfwriter/PDFBOX-3110-poems-beads.pdf` — therefore returned 0 for every code. Even after the sibling `_draw_glyph` CTM fix made the glyph paint-calls visible, every glyph painted as the fontTools `.notdef` placeholder box: the page was a 5-row × ~80-column grid of identical rectangles, structurally non-white (passing the wave-1391 `>=5%` pixel test) but unreadable.
- **Fix.** Re-port `_code_to_gid` to mirror upstream `PDTrueTypeFont.codeToGID` (PDTrueTypeFont.java lines 612-715). The existing `extract_cmap_table` per-platform extraction (Win-Unicode (3,1), Win-Symbol (3,0), Mac-Roman (1,0) + the (0,0)/(0,3) Unicode-platform → Win-Unicode aliases) is now actually used: `_code_to_gid` calls `extract_cmap_table()` first, then walks the per-platform views in the upstream order — non-symbolic fonts try Win-Unicode-via-AGL, then Mac-Roman-via-inverted-MacOS-Roman-encoding, then the `post` table by glyph name; symbolic fonts route Win-Unicode either through AGL (WinAnsi / MacRoman encoding) or by direct code, then Win-Symbol with F000/F100/F200 private-use offsets, then Mac-Roman by raw code. `_CmapPlatformView` gains a real `get_glyph_id` (was previously only `get_name`); the extraction loop passes the font's glyph order so each platform view can materialise a per-platform `code → gid` map at construction time.
- **Legacy stub-TTF fallback.** Parity tests that pass `_TrueTypeFontStub(cmap)` (no real fontTools `_tt` directory) keep working through a new `_code_to_gid_via_unicode_subtable` that preserves the pre-wave-1391 lookup shape. The main `_code_to_gid` routes through this helper whenever every per-platform slot is `None` *and* whenever the non-symbolic branch finds the font has no resolvable `/Encoding` (the lite-port `PDSimpleFont.get_encoding_typed` short-cut returns `None` for missing `/Encoding` entries rather than synthesising the StandardEncoding default upstream guarantees from the constructor; the fallback path keeps those test-only fonts producing real glyphs).
- **Coverage.** New `tests/rendering/test_cmap_platform_fallback_wave1391.py` (3 tests): poems-beads' embedded subsets resolve real GIDs for ASCII letters; poems-beads page 0 renders ≥5% non-white pixels (overlap with the sibling CTM test); OrphanPopups renders without exception (the page is correctly all-white because the two annotations have the `/F` Hidden bit set and the page content stream is empty — upstream `shouldSkipAnnotation` matches). All 5,623 tests under `tests/pdmodel/font/` + `tests/rendering/` pass.
- Files touched: `pypdfbox/pdmodel/font/pd_true_type_font.py` (`_code_to_gid` rewrite + new `_code_to_gid_via_unicode_subtable` helper, `_CmapPlatformView` gains `get_glyph_id`, `extract_cmap_table` passes glyph order to per-platform views), `tests/rendering/test_cmap_platform_fallback_wave1391.py` (new), `CHANGES.md` (this entry).

- **Agent A — close the last two LOW-severity DEFERRED items by porting their upstream-shaped surfaces.** Both entries had canonical equivalents elsewhere (`pypdfbox.util.matrix.Matrix.transform` / `create_affine_transform`; inline `list(...)` clones at every patch-decode site), but the upstream-shaped public method on the legacy `PDMatrix` / `Patch` classes themselves was absent. (1) **`PDMatrix.transform_vector` / `PDMatrix.transform` / `PDMatrix.create_affine_transform`** on `pypdfbox/pdmodel/common/pd_matrix.py`: `transform_vector(Vector | tuple) -> Vector | tuple` applies the linear part (rotation + scale) and explicitly ignores translation (mirrors upstream `Matrix.transform(Vector)`); polymorphic `transform(point_or_vector)` dispatches to `transform_vector` for `Vector` input, `transform_point` for `(x, y)` tuple input, and mutates a `Point2D`-shaped object in-place via `set_location` for upstream's `transform(Point2D)` overload (returning `None` per the upstream void contract); `create_affine_transform() -> (a, b, c, d, e, f)` returns the six geometric components in `java.awt.geom.AffineTransform` order (mirrors upstream `Matrix.createAffineTransform` plus the existing canonical `util.matrix.Matrix.create_affine_transform`). The pre-existing `transform_point(x, y)` is retained unchanged. (2) **`Patch.cloned_point2_d_array`** on `pypdfbox/pdmodel/graphics/shading/patch.py`: new static helper returns a fresh outer tuple of fresh `(x, y)` tuples (the per-element clone is conceptually a no-op because Python tuples are immutable, but the outer container is materialised distinct so callers can mutate one collection without disturbing the other — matches upstream's `clonedPoint2DArray` defensive-copy contract). Anchored by 16 hand-written tests in `tests/pdmodel/common/test_pd_matrix_transform_wave1390.py` (transform_point identity + translate/scale/rotate composition, transform_vector with pure-translate / pure-scale / pure-rotate / combined-translate-and-scale / tuple input, polymorphic transform with Vector / tuple / Point2D-shape, create_affine_transform identity / six-arg / canonical-Matrix cross-check + 3-row parametrised constructor-input round-trip with `ids=[...]` per cross-platform CI policy) and 11 hand-written tests in `tests/pdmodel/graphics/shading/test_patch_cloned_point2_d_array_wave1390.py` (different-container-equal-values, input-preservation, empty-input, list-input-returns-tuple, int-component-coercion, static-method-callable + 5-row parametrised-size round-trip with `ids=[...]`). ## Wave 1389 — close parity-audit residuals

- **Agent C — close the wave-1388 `XrefParser` DEFERRED residual via a thin parity façade.** Wave 1388 had filed `org.apache.pdfbox.pdfparser.XrefParser` as deferred on the grounds that all of its functionality already lived inlined on `pypdfbox/pdfparser/cos_parser.py::COSParser` (`parse_xref`, `parse_xref_table`, `parse_xref_obj_stream`, `parse_trailer`, `parse_start_xref`, `check_x_ref_offset`, `check_x_ref_stream_offset`, `calculate_x_ref_fixed_offset`, `validate_xref_offsets`, `check_xref_offsets`, `find_object_key`) and `pypdfbox/pdfparser/xref_trailer_resolver.py::XrefTrailerResolver.get_xref_table` for the merged-table assembly — but per the CLAUDE.md "preserve class names exactly" rule any caller porting upstream Java that says `new XrefParser(cosParser).parseXref(doc, off)` would hit an `ImportError`. Wave 1389 agent C verified the inlined surface line-for-line against upstream `pdfbox/src/main/java/org/apache/pdfbox/pdfparser/XrefParser.java` (constructor `XrefParser(COSParser)`, public `Map<COSObjectKey, Long> getXrefTable()`, public `COSDictionary parseXref(COSDocument, long startXRefOffset)`) and confirmed every method is reachable on `COSParser`. To close the parity-surface gap without re-shuffling the implementation it adds `pypdfbox/pdfparser/xref_parser.py` — a 100-line façade that wraps a `COSParser`, exposes the upstream public trio (`XrefParser(cos_parser)`, `get_xref_table()`, `parse_xref(document, start_x_ref_offset)`), mirrors upstream's private constants (`_X = 0x78`, `_XREF_TABLE = b"xref"`, `_STARTXREF = b"startxref"`, `_MINIMUM_SEARCH_OFFSET = 6`) for parity-audit visibility, and forwards each call to the inlined implementation. `parse_xref` rebinds the supplied document onto the wrapped parser before delegating, matching upstream's per-call document-supply contract. The new class is re-exported from `pypdfbox/pdfparser/__init__.py` so `from pypdfbox.pdfparser import XrefParser` works. Coverage anchored by `tests/pdfparser/test_xref_parser_wave1389.py` (10 hand-written tests: upstream-public-surface pin via `inspect`, constructor binds wrapped parser without cloning, `get_xref_table` returns empty without a bound document, `get_xref_table` returns the document's table with `None`-key placeholders filtered, end-to-end `parse_xref` on a minimal-shape PDF with one xref table + trailer returns a `COSDictionary` and rebinds the document, `parse_xref` inherits `/Prev`-loop detection from the inlined implementation, plus a 4-row parametrise sweep with explicit `ids=[...]` per the cross-platform CI policy pinning each upstream private constant). - **Agent A — port the upstream `DebugLogAppender` as a stdlib-logging adapter.** The wave-1388 audit had marked `org.apache.pdfbox.debugger.ui.DebugLogAppender` "Not applicable" (the upstream class subclasses log4j's `AbstractAppender` and pypdfbox uses stdlib `logging` per the project-wide deviation in `CHANGES.md` "Project-wide deviations vs upstream") — but per the scope-no-priority-gradient rule, every detail must be ported. Wave 1389 agent A ports it to `pypdfbox/debugger/ui/debug_log_appender.py` as a `logging.Handler` subclass that mirrors upstream's API surface 1:1: per-event `emit` callback (Java: `append`), level filter (default `logging.INFO`, matching upstream's `Level.INFO` root in `setupCustomLogger`), in-memory ring buffer backed by `collections.deque(maxlen=max_records)` for upstream's "evict oldest on overflow" semantics (default cap 1024), `get_records()` snapshot accessor returning a list of formatted strings oldest-first, `clear()` buffer-drop, `attach(logger=None, level=None)` / `detach()` lifecycle pair (default target is the root logger; accepts a `Logger` instance or a logger-name string), `attached_logger` read-only property, and a module-level `setup_custom_logger()` convenience helper matching upstream's static `setupCustomLogger`. The formatter mirrors upstream's PatternLayout pattern `"%d [%t] %-5level: %msg%n%throwable"` via the stdlib equivalent `"%(asctime)s [%(threadName)s] %(levelname)-5s: %(message)s"` (the trailing `%n%throwable` is handled by stdlib `Formatter` automatically — it appends `record.exc_text` after the formatted message when `exc_info` is present, so the captured-line shape is upstream-equivalent). `attach()` is augment-don't-replace: it only lowers the target logger's level when the existing level is `NOTSET` or higher than the handler threshold, preserving any wiring the host application installed. Re-attaching to a different logger first detaches from the previous one so the same record never fires twice. Coverage anchored by `tests/debugger/ui/test_debug_log_appender_wave1389.py` (29 hand-written tests: default-construction defaults pin, custom-cap honour, non-positive-cap rejection, INFO records captured, WARNING + ERROR captured, DEBUG dropped at default threshold, DEBUG captured at explicit DEBUG threshold, max-records ring-buffer eviction order, formatter shape pin, formatter exception-text capture, `UPSTREAM_PATTERN` constant round-trip, `clear()` empties + buffer remains usable, `attach()` returns target + registers handler, `detach()` removes handler + idempotent, re-attach pulls handler off previous logger, attach-by-name-string accepts a logger name, attach defaults to root logger + cleans up on detach, attach lowers `NOTSET` logger but never raises an already-permissive one, `setup_custom_logger` convenience helper round-trip, `extend_buffer` bulk-append helper, and a parametrised 8-row level-matrix sweep covering INFO-threshold × {DEBUG, INFO, WARNING, ERROR} and WARNING/ERROR thresholds with explicit `ids=[...]` per the cross-platform CI policy). All 29 new tests pass; all 1,916 `tests/debugger/` tests pass. No new Python dependencies (stdlib `logging` + `collections.deque` only). No camelCase aliases. No `# noqa` suppressions added. ## Wave 1388 — close last divergences + comprehensive audit

- **Agent B — eliminate the last 21 `# noqa: N802` camelCase BasePen-contract methods via a centralised bridge layer.** The wave-1382 audit left 21 noqa: N802 markers as "legitimate external-library contract keepers" — 7 in `_AggdrawPathPen` (`pypdfbox/rendering/pdf_renderer.py`) and 14 across `_DecomposingCommandPen` + `_CommandRecordingPen` (`pypdfbox/pdmodel/font/standard14_fonts.py`). Each one named a fontTools `BasePen` method (`moveTo` / `lineTo` / `curveTo` / `qCurveTo` / `closePath` / `endPath` / `addComponent`) by its camelCase form because fontTools' `glyph.draw(pen)` calls them by name. Wave 1388 Agent B closes the cluster by **inverting the dependency direction**: our internal pens now expose strictly snake_case methods (`move_to` / `line_to` / `curve_to` / `q_curve_to` / `close_path` / `end_path` / `add_component`), and a single new bridge class (`pypdfbox/rendering/_pen_bridge.py::make_base_pen_bridge`) subclasses fontTools' real `BasePen`, accepts a snake_case delegate, and translates each camelCase BasePen entry-point to the matching snake_case method via `getattr` (missing delegate methods silently no-op, so collectors are free to implement only the verbs they care about). Every `glyph.draw(pen)` callsite that used to hand a raw `_AggdrawPathPen` / `_DecomposingCommandPen` to fontTools is now wrapped: `glyph.draw(make_base_pen_bridge(pen, glyph_set=glyph_set))`. Test callsites under `tests/rendering/` (5 files) and `tests/pdmodel/font/test_standard14_fonts_coverage_wave1332.py` were rewritten to the snake_case API. Net effect: the project-wide `# noqa: N802` count drops from 21 to 7 — all 7 remaining markers live inside the bridge file itself where they are **not aliases** but the fontTools framework's own public method names, isolated to one well-named module. Coverage anchored by `tests/rendering/test_pen_bridge_wave1388.py` (new, 16 hand-written tests: one camelCase→snake_case translation test per BasePen entry point, missing-delegate-method silent-no-op coverage, end-to-end Standard-14 `get_glyph_path("Helvetica", "A")` regression guard verifying the bridge is correctly wired into the live rasterisation pipeline, `_CommandRecordingPen` via bridge round-trip, `glyph_set` argument acceptance, and a parametrised coordinate-shape sweep with explicit `ids=[...]` for cross-platform CI parity). All 5,518 tests in `tests/rendering/` + `tests/pdmodel/font/` pass (25 pre-existing skips unchanged). Additionally stripped one unrelated stale `# noqa: N802` on line 1651 of `pdf_renderer.py` (the `("paste", "draw_image", "drawImage")` getattr duck-probe loop — N802 doesn't apply to string literals, the marker was a leftover from a prior refactor). - **Agent A — close the slash-separated `MM/dd/yyyy` skip in `tests/util/upstream/test_date_util.py` (closes the last live skip in the upstream `TestDateUtil` port).** Pre-1388 the upstream `testExtract` slash-separated cases (`"D:05/12/2005"` and `"5/12/2005 15:57:16"`) were skipped under a stale reason claiming the Python port's `_SIMPLE_FORMAT_HANDLERS` table didn't carry `MM/dd/yyyy` entries. In fact the lenient `M/d/yy` handler at `pypdfbox/xmpbox/date_converter.py::_make_handler_md_yy*` already accepts 4-digit years (`\d{2,4}` group on the year capture) and routes month-first per upstream's `Locale.ENGLISH` default — both cases parsed correctly all along. Wave 1388 (1) **removes the stale skip** and ports the upstream assertions from `TestDateUtil.java` lines 60-63 into a live test body (`D:05/12/2005` → `datetime(2005, 5, 12, tzinfo=UTC)`, `5/12/2005 15:57:16` → `datetime(2005, 5, 12, 15, 57, 16, tzinfo=UTC)`); (2) **adds explicit `MM/dd/yyyy` aliases** to `_SIMPLE_FORMAT_HANDLERS` (`_make_handler_mmdd_yyyy_hms` for `"MM/dd/yyyy HH:mm:ss"`, `_make_handler_mmdd_yyyy_hm` for `"MM/dd/yyyy HH:mm"`, `_make_handler_mmdd_yyyy` for the bare `"MM/dd/yyyy"`) so the dispatch table is 1:1 with the commented-out upstream format list at `DateConverter.java` lines 136-142, plus the matching entries appended to `_DIGIT_START_FORMATS`. The new handlers require a strict 4-digit year (`\d{4}` on the year capture) so they fail-fast on 2-digit-year inputs that the lenient `M/d/yy` handler above them in the table already covers — the ordering matches upstream's "longer prefixes precede shorter ones" rule (`DateConverter.java` lines 100-104). `D:`-prefix strip uses the existing `to_calendar` pre-handler (the `D:` slice happens before the SimpleDateFormat dispatch, so no per-handler change needed). Out-of-range months / days route through `cal.validate()` per upstream's `Calendar.setLenient(false)` semantics and surface the upstream-equivalent `OSError("Invalid date format")` at the `to_calendar` boundary.
