## Wave 1385 — renderer parity fixes (continued)

- **Agent B — unify the `read_code` signature across all five `PDFont` subclasses so simple-font glyph fetches no longer fall back to a raw byte read.** Wave 1384's audit found that `PDType0Font.read_code(input_bytes, offset)` already accepted the renderer's `(bytes, offset)` call shape and returned `(code, consumed)`, but the four simple-font ports (`PDTrueTypeFont`, `PDType1Font`, `PDType1CFont`, `PDType3Font`) still declared the legacy `read_code(stream)` form returning a bare `int`. The renderer's call at `PDFRenderer._show_string` does `font.read_code(data, offset)` and unpacks `(code, consumed)`, so every simple-font glyph fetch raised `TypeError` → fell back to a raw `data[offset]` byte read that emitted a debug log line per glyph and bypassed the uniform decode contract (the renderer's word-spacing branch never saw a proper `consumed` value, though for the single-byte simple-font case the resulting code value happened to coincide so glyphs still painted in most fixtures). Wave 1385 normalises the signature to **Option A** (uniform across all 5 fonts): `read_code(data, offset=0) -> (code, consumed)`. Simple fonts always consume exactly 1 byte (mirrors upstream `PDSimpleFont.readCode(InputStream) → in.read()` returning one int); the composite `PDType0Font` defers to its active CMap and may consume 1–4 bytes (unchanged). At-or-past-end-of-buffer reads return `(0, 0)` so callers terminate the decode loop instead of seeing the old `-1` sentinel that the renderer's `code = data[offset]` shadow path silently coerced into a valid byte. Tracked through every caller: `PDFont.get_string_width` (base) now walks bytes via the buffer+offset shape; `PDFStreamEngine._decode_codes_via_font` walks the buffer through the new shape with a `TypeError`-detected legacy stream-form fallback so historical font test doubles (wave 1369's `_TwoByteFont` / `_LazyFont` / wave 1337's `_FlakyFont`) keep working without modification; the renderer's existing `_show_string` dispatch already used the new shape so the only renderer change was implicit. Updated tests pinning the old stream shape: `test_pd_true_type_font_round_out.py`, `test_pd_type1_font_parity.py`, `test_pd_type1_font_wave444.py`, `test_pd_type1c_font.py`, `test_pd_type3_font.py`, `test_pd_font_base_parity.py`, `test_pd_font_wave1337.py` (the `_Stub` PDFont concrete subclass's `read_code` override). Anchored by 27 hand-written tests in `tests/pdmodel/font/test_read_code_signature_wave1385.py`, parametrised over all five subclasses with `ids=[cls.__name__ ...]` (Windows test-ID-length safety per CLAUDE.md): tuple-shape check, sequential-offset walk over `\x41\x42\x43\xFF`, past-end + negative-offset returning `(0, 0)`, bytearray + memoryview acceptance, composite font's pre-existing shape pinned. No new Python dependencies. Files touched: `pypdfbox/pdmodel/font/pd_font.py` (base abstract `read_code` + `get_string_width` switched to buffer+offset; unused `io` import dropped), `pypdfbox/pdmodel/font/pd_true_type_font.py` (new shape, unused `io` import dropped), `pypdfbox/pdmodel/font/pd_type1_font.py` (new shape, unused `io` import dropped), `pypdfbox/pdmodel/font/pd_type1c_font.py` (new shape, unused `io` + `BinaryIO` imports dropped), `pypdfbox/pdmodel/font/pd_type3_font.py` (new shape, unused `IO` import dropped), `pypdfbox/contentstream/pdf_stream_engine.py` (`_decode_codes_via_font` switched to the buffer+offset surface with a `TypeError`-fallback for legacy stream-form fonts), `tests/pdmodel/font/test_read_code_signature_wave1385.py` (new, 27 tests), 7 existing test files updated to the new shape. All 4,894 `tests/pdmodel/font/` + `tests/rendering/` tests pass (25 skipped, unchanged); full `tests/contentstream/` (1,791 tests) passes too; `uv run ruff check` clean.

- **Agent D — close three latent gaps in the `Do` (image XObject) handler: stencil masks, non-`Device*` colour-space dispatch, and Form-XObject recursion cap.** Wave 1384's audit identified three silent-drop bugs in `pypdfbox/rendering/pdf_renderer.py::_op_do` / `_decode_image_xobject`. (1) **Stencil masks (`/ImageMask true`) were silently dropped.** Upstream `PageDrawer.drawImage` (lines 1078-1244) detects `isStencil()` and paints the 1-bit matte as the current non-stroking colour; we had no stencil branch and our colour-space resolver short-circuited to `None` for stencils anyway. New `_paint_stencil_mask(image)` decodes the 1-bit matte via the existing `_unpack_sub_byte_samples` helper, applies `/Decode` polarity (default `[0 1]` → sample-0 opaque, sample-1 transparent; `[1 0]` reverses), builds an RGBA image tinted with `self._gs.fill_rgb` and the matte as alpha, and routes through `_paste_image` so the existing CTM / clip / blend / SMask pipeline runs on the stencil output. (2) **Non-`Device*` colour spaces raised `AttributeError`.** The dispatch did `image.get_color_space().name`, which works only on the literal `COSName` short-form — `PDICCBased` / `PDIndexed` / `PDSeparation` / `PDDeviceN` / `PDCalRGB` / `PDCalGray` / `PDLab` typed wrappers don't expose a `.name` attribute, so every non-`Device*` image hit `AttributeError`, was caught by the outer `_op_do` `except`, and dropped. Rewrote the dispatch to use `cs.get_name()` for identification and `cs.to_rgb_image(data, width, height)` (the wave-374 generic transform on every `PDColorSpace` subclass) for everything except the direct `DeviceRGB` / `DeviceGray` fast paths. Indexed routes through its palette LUT, ICCBased falls through `/Alternate`, Separation evaluates its tint transform, DeviceN multiplexes process colorants, Cal*/Lab go through their CIE-XYZ paths. (3) **No Form-XObject recursion cap.** Upstream `DrawObject.java:84-89` caps `Do` Form-XObject recursion at 50 levels to defend against malformed PDFs that nest `Do` self-references and blow the rasteriser's call stack. New `_form_x_object_depth` + `_form_x_object_depth_limit=50` fields on the renderer; bumped in `_op_do` only for Form XObjects (image dispatch is not recursive), decremented in `finally`. At depth==limit a `_log.warning` fires and the nested `Do` is skipped. Anchored by 9 hand-written tests in `tests/rendering/test_image_xobject_dispatch_wave1385.py`: (a) 4x4 stencil with red non-stroking colour paints red pixels under the opaque row and leaves the transparent rows showing the white page background; (b) ICCBased 3-channel 2x2 image with `/Alternate /DeviceRGB` decodes (non-white pixels visible) instead of dropping; (c) Indexed `[/Indexed /DeviceRGB 3 <palette>]` 2x2 image decodes through palette LUT; (d) Separation 1x1 image with PostScript Type-4 tint emitting CMYK magenta decodes to RGB magenta at the centre; (e) 51-deep linear Form-XObject chain renders without `RecursionError`; (f) two consecutive `Do`s of the same form at depth-0 both succeed (cap is per-invocation depth, not cumulative count); (g) parametrised contract check that `PDDeviceRGB` / `PDIndexed` / `PDICCBased` all expose `get_name() -> str` (`ids=["device_rgb", "indexed_default", "icc_based_default"]` per the wave-1385 brief Windows test-ID-length guard). Visually verified `tests/fixtures/text/input/eu-001.pdf` (EU flag + stencil icons) renders cleanly (595x842 RGB, 7,652 distinct colours). No new Python dependencies. Files touched: `pypdfbox/rendering/pdf_renderer.py` (`__init__` adds `_form_x_object_depth` + `_form_x_object_depth_limit`; `_op_do` adds the stencil-detection short-circuit + the recursion-cap guard around Form XObject dispatch; `_decode_image_xobject` rewires colour-space dispatch to `get_name()` + `to_rgb_image()`; new `_paint_stencil_mask` method), `tests/rendering/test_image_xobject_dispatch_wave1385.py` (new, 9 tests). All 5,571 `tests/rendering/` + `tests/pdmodel/graphics/` tests pass (2 skipped, unchanged); `uv run ruff check tests/rendering/test_image_xobject_dispatch_wave1385.py` clean.

- **Agent C — wire the `Tr` (text rendering mode) operator into the renderer + apply the full set of rendering-significant `gs` (ExtGState) parameter-dictionary entries.** Wave 1384's audit identified two gaps in the renderer that left a meaningful slice of upstream-compatible PDFs rendering with the wrong visuals. (1) **`Tr` had no entry in the renderer's `_DISPATCH` table.** The parser scaffold at `pypdfbox/contentstream/operator/text/set_text_rendering_mode.py` recorded the operator name but the renderer dropped the operand silently, so every glyph painted as mode 0 (fill) regardless of the file's intent: invisible OCR layers (mode 3 / 7 — used by Tesseract / Adobe-scan PDFs), outline-only headings (modes 1 / 5 — common in logos and large display text), fill+stroke (modes 2 / 6), and text-as-clip masks (modes 4..7) all degraded to plain fill. Wave 1385 adds `text_rendering_mode: int = 0` to `_GState` (carried through `clone()` for `q`/`Q`), implements `_op_set_text_rendering_mode` (clamps the operand to 0..7 — mirrors upstream's defensive `RenderingMode.fromInt` fallback), registers `"Tr"` in `_DISPATCH`, and routes glyph painting through a new mode-aware helper `_paint_glyph_path(path, ctm, fill_rgb)` (replaces the single-purpose `_fill_aggdraw_path` — kept as a back-compat wrapper). The dispatch matches PDF 32000-1 §9.3.6 Table 106: modes 0/2/4/6 fill (uses `gs.fill_rgb` via `aggdraw.Brush`); modes 1/2/5/6 stroke (uses `gs.stroke_rgb` via `aggdraw.Pen` with the width compensated for the glyph-local-to-user matrix so a 2 user-space line-width doesn't get magnified by `font_size`); modes 4/5/6/7 accumulate the device-space glyph outline into a new `_text_clip_paths: list[skia.Path]` on the renderer (reset by every `BT` per the spec's "established at the end of the text object that initiated it" rule); `_op_end_text` rasterises the union into an alpha mask and intersects it into `gs.clip_mask`, so any subsequent path / image / shading op is clipped to the glyph footprint — the canonical decorative drop-cap / pattern-text effect. Modes 3 and 7 paint no glyph pixels (3 is fully invisible; 7 contributes only to the clip). (2) **Only `/BM /SMask /CA /ca` of the ExtGState parameter set was being applied to the active GS.** Wave 1385 extends `_op_set_graphics_state_parameters` to mirror upstream's `PDExtendedGraphicsState.copyIntoGraphicsState` for every rendering-significant entry from PDF 32000-1 Table 58: `/LW` line width, `/LC` line cap (clamped to 0..2 — Butt / Round / Projecting Square), `/LJ` line join (0..2 — Miter / Round / Bevel), `/ML` miter limit (positive only; ignores degenerate values), `/D` dash pattern → `(dash_array_tuple, phase)` on the GS (empty dash array stored as `None` per §8.4.3.6's "solid line" rule), `/RI` rendering intent (carried as a string for downstream consumers — skia doesn't honour ICC intent at the raster level), `/Font [font_dict font_size]` → text font + size on the GS (mirrors `setFont(Tf)` for the lite path), `/AIS` alpha-is-shape flag, `/TK` text knockout (default True per spec), `/FL` flatness tolerance, `/SM` smoothness tolerance, `/SA` automatic stroke adjustment (the last four carried on the GS for parity-test bookkeeping; the lite renderer doesn't act on flatness / smoothness because skia handles curve subdivision adaptively and gradient sampling natively). Deferred entries (no behavioural effect on raster output): `/OP` / `/op` / `/OPM` (overprint — affects colour separations we don't model), `/BG` / `/BG2` / `/UCR` / `/UCR2` (CMYK device-gamut black-generation / undercolour removal — output device only), `/TR` / `/TR2` (transfer function — output device only), `/HT` (halftone — output device only). The aggdraw shim's pen surface tops out at colour + width, so line-cap / line-join / miter-limit / dash-pattern are carried on the GS for parity but the strokes themselves still rasterise as the spec-default butt-miter-solid; downstream tooling can read the values back via the public `PDExtendedGraphicsState` getters. Anchored by 28 hand-written tests across two new modules: `tests/rendering/test_pdf_renderer_text_rendering_mode_wave1385.py` (10 tests — `Tr` operator GS plumb-through, out-of-range clamp, dispatch registration, mode 0 fill paints pixels, mode 1 stroke-only paints red outline with no black fill, mode 2 fill+stroke paints both colours, mode 3 invisible paints nothing, mode 4 fill-and-clip restricts a post-text fill to the glyph footprint, mode 7 clip-only with no glyph pixels but a subsequent fill is restricted, BT resets the clip-path accumulator) and `tests/rendering/test_pdf_renderer_extgstate_wave1385.py` (18 tests — each of `/LW` / `/LC` (3 valid + 1 clamp) / `/LJ` / `/ML` (positive + negative-rejected) / `/D` (with phase + empty) / `/RI` / `/Font` / `/AIS` / `/TK` / `/FL` / `/SM` / `/SA` plumb-through to the right GS field, `clone()` carries every new field, pre-existing `/CA` / `/ca` still apply alongside the new wiring, unknown ExtGState name silently no-ops). All 28 new tests pass; full `tests/rendering/test_pdf_renderer_text*.py` + `tests/contentstream/operator/` (1,316 tests) passes; `uv run ruff check` clean. No new Python dependencies.

- **Agent E — close three renderer gaps from the wave-1384 audit: uncolored tiling-pattern tint propagation, `cs`/`CS` reset-to-initial-colour, and inline-image full colour-space dispatch.** (1) **Uncolored tiling patterns (PaintType=2) lost their tint colour.** PDF 32000-1 §8.7.3.3: when `scn` / `SCN` provides ``N components + /PatternName`` and the named pattern's `/PaintType` is 2, the leading numeric components are the **tint colour** the pattern paints with — its content stream operates against that tint as the current fill/stroke colour, since the cell ops don't supply their own colour. Pre-wave-1385 `_op_set_fill_color_n` / `_op_set_stroke_color_n` ignored the components and `_render_tiling_cell` initialised the recursive `_GState` to the spec-default black, so every uncolored-tiling fill rendered solid black. Visible regression: the wave 1286 example `patterns.pdf` painted both the green and blue grids as black. Wave 1385 adds `fill_pattern_tint` / `stroke_pattern_tint: tuple[int, int, int] | None = None` fields to `_GState` (carried through `clone()`), implements `_extract_pattern_tint_rgb(operands, pattern_color_space)` which pulls the leading-N components off the operand list and runs them through the Pattern CS's underlying ("alternate") colour space via the existing `_color_components_to_rgb`, and stores the resolved RGB on the GS at `scn` / `SCN` time. `_paint_tiling_pattern` queries `pattern.get_paint_type() == 2` and forwards the active `fill_pattern_tint` to `_render_tiling_cell(..., tint_rgb=...)`, which seeds the recursive cell `_GState`'s `fill_rgb` + `stroke_rgb` with the tint so any cell op that consults the current colour (`f` / `S` / `re f` / etc.) paints in the tint. PaintType=1 (colored) tiling is unaffected — the tint is `None` and the cell paints its own colours. Mirrors upstream `org.apache.pdfbox.rendering.TilingPaintFactory.create` + `TilingPaint.paintTile`. Verified end-to-end against `pypdfbox/examples/pdmodel/create_patterns_pdf.py` — both grids now render at distinct non-trivial colours (4 distinct non-white-non-black sample colours, sample includes `(63, 63, 255)` blue-grid and `(63, 255, 63)` green-grid pixels). (2) **`cs` / `CS` did not reset the current colour to the colour space's initial colour.** PDF 32000-1 §8.6.5.1 + upstream `SetNonStrokingColorSpace.process` (line 62) reset the current colour to `cs.getInitialColor()` whenever the colour space changes. Pre-wave-1385 `_op_set_fill_color_space` / `_op_set_stroke_color_space` only stored the colour space — `fill_rgb` retained the previous value until the next `scn` / `sc` / `rg` / `g` / `k`. A PDF that does `cs … f` without setting components painted with stale colour instead of the colour space's initial colour (typically black for RGB/Gray/CMYK, [0.0] for indexed). Wave 1385 adds `_initial_color_rgb(colour_space)` which reads `cs.get_initial_color()._components` and runs them through `_color_components_to_rgb`, and both `cs` / `CS` handlers now seed `fill_rgb` / `stroke_rgb` from that helper after resolving the colour space. Also resets the pattern-tint fields so a `cs` after a pattern selection clears the active tint. (3) **Inline image (`BI`) colour-space dispatch only covered DeviceRGB + DeviceGray.** Pre-wave-1385 `_decode_inline_image` was a `@staticmethod` that only branched on the literal `cs_name` string, with abbreviated `G` / `RGB` (no `CMYK`, no `I`) and no resource-resolution path for named entries — every DeviceCMYK / Indexed / ICCBased / Separation / DeviceN inline image silently returned `None` and the caller skipped the paste. Mirrors the upstream gap-fix path through `PDImageXObject.getColorImage` + `PDInlineImage` decode. Wave 1385 converts `_decode_inline_image` to an instance method (so it can consult `self._resources` for named entries), adds full abbreviated-name coverage (`G` → DeviceGray, `RGB` → DeviceRGB, `CMYK` → DeviceCMYK, `I` → Indexed), routes named non-device CSes through `_resolve_color_space` for resource lookup, and accepts the direct CS array form `[/Indexed /DeviceRGB <hival> <lookup>]` / `[/ICCBased <stream>]` / `[/Separation /Name /DeviceCMYK <fn>]` via `PDColorSpace.create`. Fast paths for the three device singletons use PIL's native `Image.frombytes` / `convert`; Indexed routes through `to_rgb_image` (Pillow palette path); everything else (ICCBased / Separation / DeviceN / Cal* / Lab) walks per-pixel through the colour space's `to_rgb`. Backwards-compat with the existing `PDFRenderer._decode_inline_image(params, data)` static call form is preserved via a module-level `_decode_inline_image_static` helper that covers the pre-1385 device CS surface (DeviceGray / DeviceRGB / DCT / JPX); the instance method detects the static-call shape (when `self` arrives as the params dict) and forwards to it — every pre-1385 test in `tests/rendering/test_pdf_renderer_wave382.py` / `wave439.py` / `wave532.py` / `wave562.py` (8 tests across 4 files) continues to pass unchanged. Anchored by 20 hand-written tests in `tests/rendering/test_pdf_renderer_renderer_gaps_wave1385.py` covering: green-tint + blue-tint uncolored-tiling pattern paint (the patterns.pdf regression case); `_extract_pattern_tint_rgb` for DeviceRGB underlying, DeviceCMYK underlying, no-components-returns-None; `cs` resets fill to initial colour for DeviceRGB / DeviceGray / DeviceCMYK; `CS` resets stroke to initial colour; `_initial_color_rgb` helper for each device singleton + Separation (non-trivial through-CMYK conversion); `_decode_inline_image` for DeviceRGB / DeviceGray / DeviceCMYK abbreviated + full names, Indexed via resource lookup, Indexed via CS array form, ICCBased via CS array form, unknown CS returns None; `_GState.clone` carries the new tint fields. No new Python dependencies. Files touched: `pypdfbox/rendering/pdf_renderer.py` (5 deltas — `_GState` adds `fill_pattern_tint` + `stroke_pattern_tint` fields + `clone()` updates; new module-level `_decode_inline_image_static` helper for pre-1385 backwards-compat; `_op_set_stroke_color_space` / `_op_set_fill_color_space` now reset to initial colour + new `_initial_color_rgb` helper; `_op_set_stroke_color_n` / `_op_set_fill_color_n` capture pattern tint + new `_extract_pattern_tint_rgb` helper; `_paint_tiling_pattern` forwards tint to `_render_tiling_cell`; `_render_tiling_cell` accepts `tint_rgb` and seeds the recursive `_GState`; `_decode_inline_image` rewritten to full CS dispatch with backwards-compat static-call detection), `tests/rendering/test_pdf_renderer_renderer_gaps_wave1385.py` (new, 20 tests). All 5,571 `tests/rendering/` + `tests/pdmodel/graphics/` tests pass (2 skipped, unchanged); `uv run ruff check` clean.

- **Agent A — implement annotation iteration + `_render_annotation` so AcroForm widgets and other annotation appearances actually paint.** Wave 1384's audit found that the renderer's `PageDrawer.show_annotation` dispatch in `pypdfbox/rendering/page_drawer.py:364` already routed to `self._renderer._render_annotation`, but two breaks left every annotation appearance silently dropped: (1) nothing called `show_annotation` — `PDFRenderer.render_image` ran the page content stream and stopped, while upstream's `PageDrawer.drawPage` (PageDrawer.java :290) loops `getPage().getAnnotations(annotationFilter)` and calls `showAnnotation` per entry after `processPage`; (2) `_render_annotation` didn't exist on `PDFRenderer` at all. Result: every Widget, Stamp, Highlight, FreeText, Link, etc. on a rendered page was invisible. AcroFormsBasicFields.pdf (26 widgets) rendered fully white. Wave 1385 closes both ends. (1) `_render_page_into` (pdf_renderer.py) now walks `page.get_annotations(self._annotation_filter)` after `process_page` and dispatches each annotation to `self._render_annotation`, with a per-annotation try/except so a single malformed appearance can't kill the whole page render (mirrors upstream's log-and-continue triage). (2) New `_render_annotation(annotation)` mirrors upstream `PageDrawer.showAnnotation` (PageDrawer.java :1550) → `PDFStreamEngine.processAnnotation` (PDFStreamEngine.java :321): consult `_annotation_should_skip` (Hidden / NoView for View+Export / Print=false for Print / Invisible-on-PDAnnotationUnknown — the four bit-flag rules from §12.5.3); resolve the Normal Appearance via `get_normal_appearance_stream`; when absent, call `construct_appearances(document)` once and re-resolve (the wave 1380 typed-appearance generators populate this lazily); skip silently when the annotation has no rect, no bbox, or zero-dimension rect/bbox (PDFBOX-4783 guard); compute the affine `aa = a · matrix` that maps `bbox.transform(matrix).getBounds2D()` onto `rect` (upstream PDFStreamEngine processAnnotation lines 343-353 — `a = T(rect.ll) · S(rect.w/tb.w, rect.h/tb.h) · T(-tb.x, -tb.y)`); push graphics state, concat `aa` onto the CTM, clip to the pre-transform bbox via the renderer's existing `_pending_clip="W"` + `_apply_pending_clip` path, switch resources to the appearance's `/Resources` (preserving prev_resources for restore), then drive the appearance content stream through `_process_form_bytes`. (3) New `_annotation_should_skip` mirrors upstream `shouldSkipAnnotation` (PageDrawer.java :1596) using a per-render `_active_destination` field — stashed before `page_drawer.draw_page` and restored in a finally so the four-arg `renderImage(int, float, ImageType, RenderDestination)` overload's per-call override is honoured without mutating `_default_destination`. Anchored by 8 hand-written tests in `tests/rendering/test_annotation_rendering_wave1385.py`: widget with a colored-rect Normal Appearance paints pixels in the annotation rect; rubber stamp paints pixels; link annotation with no `/AP` walks without crashing; Hidden annotation skipped (no pixels in rect); NoView annotation skipped for default View destination; Print=false annotation skipped for `destination="Print"`; appearance bbox scales correctly to a 4x-larger annotation rect (bottom-left quadrant of `/BBox` lands in the bottom-left quadrant of `/Rect`); AcroFormsBasicFields.pdf (26 widgets) renders non-white. No new Python dependencies. Files touched: `pypdfbox/rendering/pdf_renderer.py` (3 deltas — `__init__` adds `_active_destination: Any = None`; `render_image_with_dpi` sets/restores `_active_destination`; `_render_page_into` iterates `page.get_annotations` after `process_page`; new `_annotation_should_skip` + `_render_annotation` methods inserted before `_render_form_xobject`), `tests/rendering/test_annotation_rendering_wave1385.py` (new). All 7,492 `tests/rendering/` + `tests/pdmodel/interactive/` tests pass (11 skipped, unchanged); `uv run ruff check` clean.

## Wave 1384 — close-the-gap campaign (renderer parity vs Apache PDFBox)

- **Agent C — close the renderer's Type 3 "deferred placeholder rectangle" doc-string claim, wire `d0` / `d1` operator dispatch, and clip painted geometry to the `d1` bbox.** Audit findings: the Type 3 glyph-painting path (`_show_type3_string` + `_render_type3_charproc`) was already wired end-to-end through the engine's Form-XObject dispatch (waves 1370a / 1370c built the routing) and was never a placeholder — but two correctness gaps survived: (1) the renderer's class-level docstring still advertised "Type3 / Standard 14 fall back to a faint placeholder rectangle"; (2) the `d0` (uncoloured glyph advance) and `d1` (coloured glyph advance + bbox) charproc-metric setters from PDF 32000-1 §9.6.5.3 had no handlers — the parser pushed operands then silently popped them at the next op, so the engine never honoured the charproc-declared advance width and never clipped to the declared bbox. Wave 1384 closes both gaps: new `PDFRenderer._op_type3_d0` records the wx override on `_type3_d0_wx`; `_op_type3_d1` records wx on `_type3_d1_wx` AND installs a synthetic clip from the `(llx, lly)-(urx, ury)` bbox by building a temporary rectangle subpath, raising `_pending_clip = "W"`, calling `_apply_pending_clip` (folds the bbox alpha mask into the current GS `clip_mask` via skia rasterisation through the active charproc CTM), then restoring the page-level path state so the charproc's own path-construction ops continue from a clean slate; both ops registered in `_DISPATCH`. `_show_type3_string` resets `_type3_d0_wx` / `_type3_d1_wx` to `None` before each charproc dispatch and reads them back after — when present, they override the `/Widths` value for the advance arithmetic (`d1` takes precedence over `d0` when both somehow appear in the same glyph, matching upstream `Type3PageDrawer.processType3Stream`'s precedence). Degenerate / inverted d1 bboxes (`urx <= llx` or `ury <= lly`) skip the clip — matches PDFBox's lenient behaviour of just painting the glyph. Re-checked the existing wave-1370c d0/d1 regression tests (`test_type3_d0_silently_ignored_and_paint_still_happens` / `test_type3_d1_silently_ignored_and_paint_still_happens`) — both still pass: their charproc bboxes were already wide enough (`0 0 1000 1000`) to enclose the painted rect, so the new clip is a no-op for them. Anchored by 5 hand-written tests in `tests/rendering/test_type3_font_rendering_wave1384.py` covering: filled-square charproc drawn by `m l l l h f` (not `re`) paints visible pixels at the expected page-space coordinates and leaves an empty bottom-right region; multi-glyph `AAA` paints at three distinct non-overlapping positions; `d1` bbox clip suppresses paint past the declared bounds (a `0 0 500 500 d1 / 0 0 1000 1000 re f` charproc must NOT bleed into the upper-right glyph-space quadrant); structural pixel-sample (inside-region has dark pixels, far-away absent region has zero); `d1` advance override takes precedence over `/Widths` (two glyphs with `/Widths=200` but `d1 wx=900` paint non-overlapping). No new Python dependencies. Files touched: `pypdfbox/rendering/pdf_renderer.py` (4 deltas — docstring rewritten to describe the real Type 3 dispatch; `__init__` adds `_type3_d0_wx` / `_type3_d1_wx` / `_type3_glyph_cache` fields; new `_op_type3_d0` + `_op_type3_d1` methods; `_show_type3_string` reads the d0/d1 wx overrides; `_DISPATCH` table registers `"d0"` + `"d1"`), `tests/rendering/test_type3_font_rendering_wave1384.py` (new). All 4,859 `tests/rendering/` + `tests/pdmodel/font/` tests pass (25 skipped, unchanged); `uv run ruff check` clean.

- **Agent E — apply ExtGState `/SMask` to direct fills / strokes outside a transparency group.** Before wave 1384, the renderer's soft-mask handling in `pypdfbox/rendering/pdf_renderer.py` only consulted `self._gs.soft_mask` at transparency-group composite time (`_render_transparency_group` line 4445). Any path that landed straight on the page canvas via `f` / `F` / `f*` / `S` / `B` / `B*` / `b` / `b*` while an ExtGState `/SMask` was active silently discarded the mask — the rendered pixels skipped the alpha-modulation step entirely. Real-world PDFs frequently activate an SMask on the page-level GS and then paint geometry directly without wrapping it in a Form XObject (drop shadows, gradient fills, watermarks); pypdfbox's output diverged visibly from upstream PDFBox on those documents. Upstream invokes `applySoftMaskToPaint` (PageDrawer.java line 606) from `getNonStrokingPaint` / `getStrokingPaint` / `drawBufferedImage` so every paint operation that consults the current GS picks up the mask. Wave 1384 closes the gap by (1) extending `_paint_through_clip` to accept an optional `soft_mask` argument and multiply the rendered soft-mask alpha plane (via the existing `_render_soft_mask_alpha`) into the layer's alpha before compositing, (2) routing direct fills/strokes in `_paint` through that helper whenever `self._gs.soft_mask is not None`, and (3) introducing a `_transparency_group_depth: int` counter on the renderer — incremented inside `_render_transparency_group` and `_render_soft_mask_alpha`, decremented in their `finally` blocks — so the per-paint SMask application is suppressed while we're *inside* a group's own recursive render (the group's composite step applies the mask once at the end; without the depth guard the mask would be multiplied twice, once per fill inside the group and once again at composite). The reentrancy guard mirrors upstream's behaviour where the soft-mask group itself bypasses `applySoftMaskToPaint`. Anchored by 5 hand-written tests in `tests/rendering/test_pdf_renderer_smask_direct_paint_wave1384.py`: direct fill outside a group with a half-page Luminosity mask + black backdrop → masked-in side stays red, masked-out side drops to page background (the regression case — pre-fix, both sides were red); same setup but wrapped in a transparency group → identical pixel-level result, proving no double-application via the depth counter; direct stroke (wide horizontal line) with the same half-page mask → stroke survives on the masked-in side, vanishes on the masked-out side; real-world smoke test against `tests/fixtures/pdfwriter/unencrypted.pdf` and `tests/fixtures/multipdf/PDFBOX-5811-362972.pdf` (both carry `/SMask` references) renders without exception to a non-empty image; two-level nested transparency group renders without crashing and the inner geometry is visible (depth-counter regression guard). All 5 new tests pass; full `tests/rendering/` suite passes with no regressions; `uv run ruff check` clean.

- **Agent D — actually APPLY GSUB contextual substitution lookups (Types 5 / 6 / 7 / 8) during text shaping.** Wave 1380 shipped the data-class plumbing for context-aware GSUB lookups (Type 5 simple-glyph / class-based / per-position-Coverage contextual, Type 6 chained-contextual analogues with backtrack + lookahead, Type 7 extension wrapping, Type 8 reverse-chained context) and the matcher predicates (`match_rule` / `matches` / `do_substitution_at`) — but the actual substitution surface was inert. Every contextual subtable's `do_substitution(glyph_id, coverage_index) -> int` raised `TypeError` because the single-glyph-in / single-glyph-out signature can't express the nested-lookup fan-out a `SubstitutionLookupRecord(sequence_index, lookup_list_index)` describes. Result: Indic / Arabic / complex-script text shaping silently no-op'd these features even when the worker classes (`GsubWorkerForBengali` / `Devanagari` / `Gujarati` / `Tamil`) walked the lookup graph. Wave 1384 closes the application surface by adding a new `LookupSubTable.apply(glyph_ids: list[int], position: int, all_lookups: tuple[LookupTable, ...]) -> int` contract — mutates the run in place and returns the count of input glyphs consumed by the match (caller advances by `max(1, consumed)`). Concrete implementations on `LookupTypeSingleSubstFormat1` / `2` (Type 1, one glyph consumed and rewritten in place), `LookupTypeMultipleSubstitutionFormat1` (Type 2, one glyph -> N glyphs via `list.__setitem__` slice replace), `LookupTypeAlternateSubstitutionFormat1` (Type 3, first alternate that differs from coverage glyph wins — mirrors the extractor's convention), `LookupTypeLigatureSubstitutionSubstFormat1` (Type 4, longest-match candidate collapses `1 + len(components)` glyphs in place to the ligature GID), all six `LookupType*ContextualSubstitutionFormat{1,2,3}` (Types 5 + 6, delegate to the existing `match_rule` / `matches` matchers and then dispatch each `SubstitutionLookupRecord` through the new `_dispatch_substitution_records` helper which resolves `lookup_list_index` against the LookupList and applies each inner subtable at `start_index + sequence_index`), `LookupTypeExtensionSubstitutionFormat1` (Type 7, transparent indirection — delegates straight through to the wrapped inner subtable's `apply`), and `LookupTypeReverseChainedContextualSubstitutionFormat1` (Type 8, delegates to existing `do_substitution_at` and rewrites in place; the right-to-left walk is the driver's job). New top-level `apply_lookup_table(glyph_ids, lookup_table, all_lookups)` driver walks the run left-to-right for Types 1-7 and right-to-left for Type 8 (per OpenType §6.5 spec — substituting a glyph LTR could feed-cascade through the just-substituted GID into an earlier backtrack match, which is wrong), trying each subtable in order until one returns a non-zero consumption count. Existing `do_substitution` / `do_substitution_glyphs` / `do_substitution_multiple` / `do_substitution_at` / `apply_to_run` / `match_rule` / `matches` surfaces are unchanged so the wave-1380 test suites and the `GlyphSubstitutionDataExtractor` flat-projection extractor still work verbatim. `apply_lookup_table` exported from `pypdfbox.fontbox.ttf.gsub` for callers that want to drive shaping engine-style (per-script workers, custom shapers). Anchored by 21 hand-written tests in `tests/fontbox/ttf/gsub/test_contextual_application_wave1384.py` covering: Type 1 (Format 1 + Format 2) `apply` in-place rewrite + no-match passthrough; Type 2 one-to-many slice replace; Type 4 longest-match ligature collapse; Type 5 Format 1 dispatching an inner Type-1 lookup at sequence_index=0; Type 5 Format 1 no-match leaves run unchanged; Type 5 Format 2 class-based rule dispatching an inner Type-1 at sequence_index=2; Type 5 Format 3 per-position coverage dispatching an inner Type-1 at sequence_index=1; Type 6 chained Format 1 with backtrack + input + lookahead dispatching an inner Type-1 at sequence_index=1 (plus backtrack-mismatch no-op); Type 6 Format 2 class-based chained; Type 6 Format 3 per-position-coverage chained; Type 7 extension wrapping Type 4 ligature (collapses run end-to-end); Type 7 extension wrapping Type 1 Format 2; Type 8 reverse-chained "Arabic final-form before space" simulation (substitutes initial + medial forms when followed by space, leaves untouched medials); Type 8 right-to-left no-cascade walk against a backtrack-coverage that would self-reinforce LTR; Type 8 acts like Type 1 when backtrack + lookahead are empty; driver edge cases (empty run / no subtables / out-of-range `lookup_list_index` / out-of-range `sequence_index`). All 21 new tests pass; full `tests/fontbox/ttf/gsub/` + `tests/fontbox/ttf/` suite (2,021 tests) passes (up from 2,000); `uv run ruff check` clean. `DEFERRED.md` GSUB-application-deferred bullet closed.

## Per-file deviations

- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/interactive/form/pd_field_factory.py`: malformed or unknown field dictionaries are skipped by factory/tree traversal.
- `pypdfbox/xmpbox/dom_xmp_parser.py`: unknown namespaces preserve their declared XML prefixes.
- `pypdfbox/contentstream/pdf_graphics_stream_engine.py`: registers the `sh` shading operator.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/pd_resource_cache.py`: repeated removals mark shared resources stable at `MAX_REMOVALS`.
- `pypdfbox/tools/texttopdf.py`: non-positive font sizes fail early as usage errors.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/interactive/form/pd_default_appearance_string.py`: missing-font /DA fallback to Standard-14 Helvetica (PDFBOX-2661 "special mapping"); upstream raises IOException. Also tracks `cs` / `CS` / `gs` named-resource references and carries them across in `copy_needed_resources_to` (upstream "todo: other kinds of resource…" placeholder filled in).
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/interactive/annotation/pd_appearance_stream.py`: appearance streams expose the content-stream byte-access surface.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/interactive/documentnavigation/destination/`: `/XYZ` and `/FitR` coordinate setters grow short arrays before writing.
- `pypdfbox/pdfparser/endstream_filter_stream.py`: mid-stream CRLF bytes are preserved until final endstream length is proven.
- `pypdfbox/fontbox/ttf/true_type_font.py`: unicode cmap selection follows PDFBox priority order including Windows Symbol fallback.
- `pypdfbox/rendering/pdf_renderer.py`: image rendering uses `PDImageXObject.to_pil_image()` before legacy RGB/gray fallback.
- `pypdfbox/contentstream/operator/text/set_text_rendering_mode_op.py`: out-of-range text rendering modes no-op before notifying the engine.
- `pypdfbox/pdfparser/pdf_parser.py`: xref stream decoding rejects negative `/W` field widths.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/common/filespecification/pd_embedded_file.py`: embedded-file subtype lookup accepts COS string-backed names.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/font/pd_type1c_font.py`: `get_average_character_width()` is implemented (mean of `/Widths` -> mean of embedded CFF charstring widths -> `defaultWidthX` -> Standard 14 AFM -> `500` floor). Upstream's `PDType1CFont.getAverageCharacterWidth` returns a hard-coded `500` with a `// todo: not implemented, highly suspect` annotation — we close that TODO using `fontTools.cffLib`'s `T2WidthExtractor` per glyph via `CFFFont.get_width`. `500` is retained only as the absolute fallback when no real signal is available, preserving observable behaviour for the empty-font case.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/pd_document_catalog.py`: dictionary-only catalog setters reject non-dictionary values.
- `pypdfbox/fontbox/type1/type1_parser.py`: ASCII-hex eexec segments are normalized before Type1 decryption.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/fdf/fdf_annotation_file_attachment.py`: FDF file attachment annotations are implemented and factory-dispatched.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/font/pd_cid_font_type2.py`: embedded Type2 CID font programs are probed in PDFBox order: `/FontFile2`, `/FontFile3`, then `/FontFile`.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/encryption/protection_policy.py`: exposes Java-style key-length and AES preference aliases.
- `pypdfbox/pdfwriter/cos_writer.py`: xref table serialization rejects offsets and generations that cannot fit fixed-width rows.
- `pypdfbox/filter/filter.py`: decode-params arrays dereference indirect entries.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/interactive/form/pd_check_box.py`: checkbox on-value lookup resolves widgets and skips malformed `/Kids` entries.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/font/pd_true_type_font.py`: replacing or subsetting a TrueType font clears cmap and GID caches.
- `pypdfbox/cos/cos_dictionary.py`: numeric and boolean typed getters support fallback-key overloads.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/common/pd_name_tree_node.py`: name-tree lookup continues past matching child ranges that do not contain the requested name.
- `pypdfbox/rendering/pdf_renderer.py`: page rendering rejects negative page indexes.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/interactive/form/pd_text_field.py`, `pypdfbox/pdmodel/interactive/form/pd_variable_text.py`: text setters reject non-string values before mutating COS state.
- `pypdfbox/pdfparser/base_parser.py`: malformed literal-string recovery mirrors PDFBox end-of-string handling around dictionary-key boundaries.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/graphics/color/pd_device_n_process.py`: re-exports the canonical `PDDeviceNProcess` used by DeviceN attributes.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/font/pd_font_descriptor.py`: PANOSE classification follows Java signed-byte widening and range behavior.
- `pypdfbox/io/random_access_read_view.py`: zero-length `read_into()` returns `0` without disturbing the parent cursor.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/interactive/annotation/pd_annotation_widget.py`: widget dictionaries preserve an existing non-`/Annot` `/Type` while stamping `/Subtype /Widget`.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/graphics/image/pd_image_x_object.py`: image suffix and predicate helpers recognize standard short filter aliases.
- `pypdfbox/cos/cos_document.py`: exposes `get_key()` / `getKey()` lookup for object-pool keys by resolved object identity.
- `pypdfbox/pdfwriter/cos_writer.py`: unsupported object-stream output combinations fail early instead of being silently ignored.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/common/function/pd_function_type2.py`: Type 2 functions clip outputs according to explicit `/Range` pairs.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/fdf/fdf_dictionary.py`: `get_file()` returns a typed file specification and string helpers remain available.
- `pypdfbox/fontbox/ttf/horizontal_metrics_table.py`: horizontal metric lookups guard negative and out-of-range glyph ids.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/common/pd_matrix.py`: matrix row/column access rejects coordinates outside `0..2`.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/encryption/standard_security_handler.py`: AES-256 owner-password decryption grants owner permissions.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/pd_page_labels.py`: computed page-label ranges are clamped to the actual document page count.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/interactive/action/pd_additional_actions.py`: generic additional-actions wrapper supports `/F` trigger round-tripping.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/common/pd_stream.py`: decode-parameter replacement clears stale `/DP`, and committed zero-byte streams report empty.
- `pypdfbox/fontbox/cff/cff_font.py`: format-1 CFF encoding ranges stop at code `255` instead of wrapping.
- `pypdfbox/pdfparser/xref_trailer_resolver.py`: `reset()` clears visited xref offsets for recovery/reparse passes.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/pd_resources.py`: pattern and shading resource helpers accept plain string names.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/font/pd_type3_font.py`: Type 3 fonts expose bounding-box and position-vector methods from the `PDFontLike` surface.
- `pypdfbox/cos/cos_integer.py`: `COSInteger.get(True/False)` rejects booleans instead of returning cached `1`/`0` integers.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/interactive/documentnavigation/outline/pd_outline_item.py`: named destination page lookup prefers `/Names /Dests` over legacy catalog `/Dests`.
- `pypdfbox/filter/lzw_decode.py`: LZW encode/decode flushes caller-provided output streams.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/graphics/optionalcontent/pd_optional_content_properties.py`: visibility writes remove stale duplicate `/ON` and `/OFF` references before storing the new state.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/interactive/annotation/pd_appearance_content_stream.py`: dashed borders without explicit `/D` materialize the default `[3]` dash pattern.
- `pypdfbox/loader.py`: exposes Java-style `loadPDF`, `loadFDF`, and `loadXFDF` aliases.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/font/afm_loader.py`: bundled AFM resources load through `importlib.resources` handles instead of filesystem paths.
- `pypdfbox/io/scratch_file.py`: exposes main-memory-only ScratchFile factory aliases.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/documentinterchange/taggedpdf/pd_print_field_attribute_object.py`: print-field role and checked-state getters accept COS string-backed names.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/interactive/form/pd_acro_form.py`: form flattening guards against cyclic `/Kids` graphs.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/graphics/image/`: image factories expose Java-style PDFBox creation aliases.
- `pypdfbox/fontbox/ttf/ttf_data_stream.py`: `read_unsigned_int()` treats any negative byte as EOF.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/encryption/pd_encryption.py`, `pypdfbox/pdmodel/encryption/pd_crypt_filter_dictionary.py`: dictionary wrappers expose `get_cos_dictionary()`.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/common/pd_metadata.py`: filtered metadata size reports decoded XMP byte length.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/interactive/annotation/pd_annotation_file_attachment.py`: exposes PDFBox attachment-name aliases, including the legacy misspelled setter.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/graphics/color/pd_icc_based.py`: malformed ICCBased `/Range` arrays default component ranges to `(0.0, 1.0)`.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/font/pd_font_factory.py`: embedded font-program headers are read from decoded stream bytes.
- `pypdfbox/pdfparser/pdf_parser.py`: lenient parsing attempts shifted-offset recovery before rejecting out-of-bounds `startxref`.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/common/filespecification/pd_embedded_file.py`: malformed PDF date timezone offsets return `None`.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/pd_viewer_preferences.py`: includes the long-form deprecated `UseOC` non-full-screen page mode constant.
- `pypdfbox/cos/cos_stream.py`: `stop_filters` canonicalizes standard filter aliases before comparison.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/font/pd_cid_system_info.py`: string rendering uses Java-style `null` for missing registry or ordering.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/common/pd_number_tree_node.py`: switching a number tree node to kids clears stale `/Nums` and refreshes ancestor limits.
- `pypdfbox/pdfwriter/cos_writer.py`: incremental saves track absolute output offsets after copied source bytes.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/interactive/action/pd_action_java_script.py`: stream-form `/JS` actions decode through `COSStream.to_text_string()`.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/interactive/documentnavigation/destination/`: default coordinate-based destination constructors include optional coordinate slots as `COSNull`.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/pd_page_content_stream.py`: `move_text_position_and_set_leading()` requires an active text block.
- `pypdfbox/cos/cos_dictionary.py`: raw `get_item` supports the PDFBox alternate-key overload shape.
- `pypdfbox/filter/flate_decode.py`: Flate encode/decode flushes output sinks after writing.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/interactive/annotation/pd_border_effect_dictionary.py`: `set_style(None)` clears optional `/S`.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/graphics/color/pd_cal_rgb.py`: missing or cleared `/Matrix` returns the identity matrix.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/font/encoding/dictionary_encoding.py`: symbolic reader-mode encodings without a valid base or built-in encoding fail explicitly.
- `pypdfbox/pdfparser/pdf_stream_parser.py`: inline-image parsing only treats exact `ID` as image data, leaving `I` and longer operator names as normal operators.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/common/function/pd_function_type4.py`: Type 4 function parsing rejects missing and stray closing braces.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/interactive/form/pd_choice.py`: one-element nested `/Opt` entries are preserved in display values so tolerated malformed option arrays keep export/display alignment.
- `pypdfbox/fontbox/ttf/true_type_font.py`: synthesized header metadata preserves `head.created` and `head.modified` as UTC `datetime` values.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/documentinterchange/logicalstructure/pd_structure_node.py`: direct structure-element kid append/remove operations maintain the child's `/P` parent pointer.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/graphics/form/pd_transparency_group_attributes.py`: cached `/CS` color spaces are invalidated when the raw COS source is externally replaced or removed.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/encryption/security_provider.py`: `/Adobe.PubSec` resolves through the public-key security handler factory.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/graphics/image/pd_image_x_object.py`: stencil image XObjects now treat missing `/ColorSpace` as implicit `DeviceGray`.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/interactive/measurement/pd_media_clip.py`, `pypdfbox/pdmodel/interactive/measurement/pd_rendition.py`: media clip and rendition factories dereference indirect objects and treat unresolved or null references as absent.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/interactive/documentnavigation/outline/pd_outline_item.py`, `pypdfbox/pdmodel/interactive/documentnavigation/outline/pd_outline_node.py`: sibling insertion rewrites inserted item parents consistently.
- `pypdfbox/fontbox/cff/cff_font.py`: empty or unparsed CFF fonts return safe width/path fallbacks.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/fdf/fdf_annotation_line.py`: FDF line annotations expose `/L` accessors and malformed coordinate arrays read as absent.
- `pypdfbox/io/random_access_read_buffer.py`: wraps `io.BytesIO` instead of reimplementing PDFBox's chunked-list storage. Observable behavior is identical; implementation is C-backed and ~25 lines instead of ~120. Justification: PRD §3.7 (stdlib-first for generic infrastructure).
- `pypdfbox/io/random_access_read_buffered_file.py`: wraps `io.BufferedReader` over a raw file fd. Stdlib provides the read-ahead buffering that upstream's `RandomAccessReadBufferedFile` implements manually. Justification: PRD §3.7.
- `pypdfbox/io/random_access_read_memory_mapped.py`: net-new optional implementation backed by `mmap.mmap`. No upstream counterpart; offered as opt-in for very large files where kernel paging beats userspace buffering. Justification: PRD §3.7 — use stdlib affordances when they fit.
- `pypdfbox/io/random_access_read_view.py`: original slice-view implementation. Mirrors the upstream `RandomAccessReadView` API; storage strategy is direct seek-on-parent rather than upstream's bounded-stream wrapper.
- `pypdfbox/io/scratch_file.py`: backed by `tempfile.SpooledTemporaryFile` (mixed mode), `tempfile.TemporaryFile` (temp-file-only), or `io.BytesIO` (memory-only). Upstream uses page-based scratch storage; we delegate spill-to-disk policy to stdlib. Behavior visible to callers (read/write/seek/clear) is identical. Justification: PRD §3.7. Default spill threshold in MIXED mode without an explicit cap is 16 MiB.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/font/pd_font_like.py`, `pypdfbox/pdmodel/font/pd_vector_font.py`: upstream Java `interface`s modelled as `typing.Protocol` (runtime-checkable) so existing duck-typed font classes satisfy `isinstance(...)` without inheritance — Python idiom, no observable behaviour change. AWT-typed returns (`Matrix`, `BoundingBox`, `Vector`, `GeneralPath`) are widened to `Any` since pypdfbox is AWT-free.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/common/pd_name_tree_node.py`, `pypdfbox/pdmodel/common/pd_number_tree_node.py`: `get_names` / `get_numbers` recurse and flatten the whole subtree, whereas upstream `getNames()` / `getNumbers()` return only this node's leaf mapping (`null` on a `/Kids` node). Both agree on a single-level leaf.
  upstream: PDFBox 3.0.7 `pdmodel/common/PDNameTreeNode.java`, `PDNumberTreeNode.java`
  reason: callers want a whole-tree map; upstream forces them to recurse via `getKids` themselves (see upstream `EmbeddedFiles` handling). Confirmed against the live oracle (`oracle/probes/NameNumTreeProbe.java`) — flatten/limits/`get()` match exactly on well-formed single- and multi-level (2-3 deep) balanced trees.
- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/common/pd_name_tree_node.py`, `pypdfbox/pdmodel/common/pd_number_tree_node.py`: on malformed input (an intermediate node's kid missing `/Limits` mid-list), `get_value` guards the null limit and falls through to later limited siblings. Upstream `PDNumberTreeNode.getValue` throws `NullPointerException` dereferencing the null lower limit; upstream `PDNameTreeNode.getValue` searches the no-limit kid but stops, never reaching a later sibling.
  upstream: PDFBox 3.0.7 `pdmodel/common/PDNumberTreeNode.java` (getValue ~line 166), `PDNameTreeNode.java`
  reason: robustness on malformed trees; a well-formed PDF carries `/Limits` on every non-root node, so the divergence is unreachable on valid documents. Pinned in `tests/pdmodel/common/oracle/test_name_number_tree_oracle.py::test_no_limit_kid_{name,number}_*` (the oracle crashes / stops-early on these shapes, so they are asserted pypdfbox-side only). Wave 1417.

- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/encryption/public_key_security_handler.py`: public-key (`/Adobe.PubSec`) interop fixes against the live PDFBox 3.0.7 oracle (wave 1418).
  1. Read path (`prepare_for_decryption`): `/Recipients` is now also looked up inside `/CF /DefaultCryptFilter` — the crypt-filter-based V>=4 handler (AES-128 V4 / AES-256 V5) that PDFBox and Acrobat emit puts it there, not at the `/Encrypt` top level. Previously every PDFBox/Acrobat AES public-key file raised "/Recipients array missing".
  2. Write path (`prepare_document`): `/Recipients` is now written inside `/CF /DefaultCryptFilter` (was the `/Encrypt` top level), and the whole `/CF` subtree is marked direct/inline. Writing it at the top level made a PDFBox reader derive the wrong file key (empty extracted text); leaving `/CF` indirect made PDFBox dereference it mid-`prepareForDecryption` and throw a NullPointerException.
  3. Write path: the crypt filter `/Length` is now written in BITS (128/256) to match PDFBox, which reads it as bits and truncates the file key accordingly. It was written in bytes (16/32), so a PDFBox reader truncated the file key to 16 bits → garbage streams.
  4. `prepare_for_decryption` now raises a distinct `cryptography.exceptions.UnsupportedAlgorithm` (not the generic "matched none") when a recipient envelope uses a CMS content cipher the `cryptography` PKCS#7 backend can't decrypt.
  upstream: PDFBox 3.0.7 `pdmodel/encryption/PublicKeySecurityHandler.java` (`prepareEncryptionDictAES`, `prepareForDecryption`)
  interop: pypdfbox-pubkey-encrypts → Java-decrypts is FULL (AES-128 + AES-256, content recovered). Java-pubkey-encrypts → pypdfbox-decrypts is UNSUPPORTED — PDFBox/Acrobat wrap the recipient seed in an RC2-CBC CMS envelope, and `cryptography` decrypts AES-CBC envelopes only (RC2 is not exposed by OpenSSL; hand-rolling it is out of scope). Pinned in `tests/pdmodel/encryption/oracle/test_public_key_interop_oracle.py`.

- `pypdfbox/pdmodel/interactive/digitalsignature/pd_seed_value.py`: `get_reasons()` / `set_reasons()` treat `/SV /Reasons` as an array of **text strings** (`COSString`), reading via `to_cos_string_string_list()`.
  upstream: PDFBox 3.0.7 `pdmodel/interactive/digitalsignature/PDSeedValue.java` (`getReasons`)
  reason: PDF 32000-1 Table 234 defines `/Reasons` as "an array of text strings". PDFBox 3.0.7's `setReasons()` correctly writes `COSString` entries, but `getReasons()` reads them via `COSArray.toCOSNameStringList()` — which casts each entry to `COSName` and throws `ClassCastException` on the very strings it wrote (it cannot read its own output). pypdfbox is spec-correct and self-consistent (writes strings, reads strings). Confirmed against the live oracle in wave 1440; the differential probe (`oracle/probes/SigFieldProbe.java`) reads `/Reasons` straight off the COS array as strings rather than calling PDFBox's broken `getReasons()`. Pinned in `tests/pdmodel/interactive/digitalsignature/oracle/test_sig_field_oracle.py::test_seed_value_subfilter_digest_reasons_match`. No pypdfbox code change — pypdfbox was already correct; this records the upstream divergence so a future re-sync does not "fix" pypdfbox to match the broken upstream getter.
